Salah — Prayer
beginner
12 min
The Meaning and Historical Prescription of Salah
Definition and historical origin of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and Shari'ah definitions of salah and identify the historical prescription of each of the five daily prayers based on the prophetic narratives.

Core Idea
Salah linguistically means supplication; in Shari'ah, it is a specific worship; its five daily prayers were prefigured in earlier prophets.

This lesson opens the Book of Prayer by examining the word 'salah' itself. We first clarify its linguistic root and how the Sacred Law redefines it. Then we trace a remarkable narration that links each of the five prayers to an event in prophetic history, showing the continuity of worship across revelations.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the linguistic definition
The text states that salah in language is supplication (du'a). Determine why this is the primary meaning and what evidence supports it.
Look for the Quranic verse and hadith citation.
2
Separate the Shari'ah definition
Contrast the legal definition (specific acts from takbir to taslim) with the linguistic meaning. Note that the Shari'ah meaning is a specialized term.
The passage emphasizes 'salah' as a technical term after the advent of revelation.
3
Trace the historical prescription
For each of the five prayers, identify the associated prophet, the event, and the number of rak'ahs as per the At-Tahawi narration.
Fajr: Adam at dawn (2). Zuhr: Ishaq at noon (4). Asr: Uzayr after resurrection (4). Maghrib: Dawud at sunset (3). Isha: our Prophet (SAW) first.
4
Identify unique features of Islamic prayer
List the distinctive elements attributed to the Muslim prayer: adhan, iqamah, opening takbir, amin, wording after bowing, prohibition of speech.
These are found in the sentence beginning 'وخص بالأذان والإقامة...'
5
Synthesize the insights
Combine the linguistic, Shari'ah, and historical insights to explain why salah is central in Islam.
Consider the universality of supplication and the specificity of the five daily prayers.

لا بد من بيان معناها لغة وشريعة ووقت افتراضها وعدد أوقاتها وبيانها وركعاتها وحكمة افتراضها وسببها وشروطها وحكمها وركتها وصفتها فهي في اللغة عبارة عن  
كتاب الصلاة  
شروع في المقصود بعد بيان الوسيلة، ولم يخل عنها شريعة مرسل ومما اختص به مجموع الصلوات الخمس، ولم تجمع لأحد من الأنبياء غيره، وخص بالأذان والإقامة وافتتاح الصلاة بالتكبير وبالتأمين، وبالركوع فيما ذكره جماعة من المفسرين وبقول: اللهم ربنا ولك الحمد، وبتحريم الكلام في الصلاة كذا ذكره السيوطي في الأنموذج كذا في شرح السيد، وأخرج الطحاوي عن عبيد الله بن محمد عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن آدم لما تيب عليه عند الفجر صلى ركعتين فصارت صلاة الصبح وفدى إسحاق عند الظهر، فصلى أربع ركعات فصارت الظهر، وبعث عزير فقيل له : كم لبثت قال : لبثت يوماً فرأى الشمس، فقال: أو بعض يوم فقيل له : إنك لبثت مائة عام ميتاً، ثم بعثت فصلي أربع ركعات فصارت العصر، وغفر لداود عند المغرب، فقام فصلى أربع ركعات فجهد في الثالثة أي تعب فيها عن الإتيان بالرابعة لشدة ما حصل له من البكاء على ما اقترفه مما خلاف الأولى فصارت المغرب ثلاثاً، وأوّل من هو صلى العشاء الأخيرة نبينا . قال في شرح المشكاة! ومعناه أن نبينا أول من صلى العشاء أمته، فلا ينافي أن الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام صلوها دون أممهم، ويؤيده قول جبريل عليه السلام في حديث الإمامة هذا وقت الأنبياء من قبلك اهـ. قوله : (فهي في الدعاء) أي حقيقة وتستعمل في غيره مجازاً، وهو قول الجمهور وبه جزم الجوهري، وغيره  
مع  
اللغة عبارة عن  
لأنه الشائع في كلامهم قبل ورود الشرع، والقرآن ورد بلغة العرب قال تعالى: ﴿وصل عليهم [التوبة: ٩] أي ادع لهم وفي الحديث في إجابة الدعوة وإن كان صائماً فليصل أي فليدع لهم بالخير والبركة ومنه الصلاة على الميت والصلاة اسم مصدر صلى والمصدر التصلية وإنما
It is necessary to explain its meaning linguistically and in Shari'ah, the time of its obligation, the number of its times, their explanation, their rak'ahs, the wisdom of its obligation, its cause, its conditions, its ruling, its rak'ah, and its description. So in language it is...
The Book of Prayer.
An introduction to the intended subject after explaining the means. No messenger's religion was devoid of it, and among the unique features of this Ummah is the collection of the five prayers; they were not collected for any other prophet. It is distinguished by the adhan and iqamah, opening the prayer with takbir, saying amin, bowing as mentioned by a group of exegetes, saying 'Allahumma Rabbana wa laka al-hamd', and the prohibition of speech during prayer. As-Suyuti mentioned this in al-Anmudhaj, and similarly in Sharh as-Sayyid. At-Tahawi narrated from 'Ubayd Allah ibn Muhammad from 'A'ishah (RA) that when Adam's repentance was accepted at dawn, he prayed two rak'ahs, so it became the dawn prayer. Ishaq was ransomed at noon, so he prayed four rak'ahs, so it became the noon prayer. 'Uzayr was sent, it was said to him: How long did you stay? He said: I stayed a day and saw the sun, so he said: Or part of a day. It was said to him: You stayed dead for a hundred years, then you were resurrected. So he prayed four rak'ahs, so it became the 'Asr prayer. Dawud was forgiven at sunset, so he stood and prayed four rak'ahs but became exhausted in the third, i.e., tired from performing the fourth due to the intensity of his weeping over his sin of doing something contrary to the better, so it became three rak'ahs. And the first to pray the 'Isha' prayer was our Prophet (SAW). It is said in Sharh al-Mishkat: The meaning is that our Prophet was the first to pray 'Isha' among his Ummah, so it does not contradict that the prophets prayed it without their nations. Supporting this is the statement of Jibril in the hadith of leadership: 'This is the time of the prophets before you.' His saying: (it is in supplication) meaning in reality, and it is used otherwise metaphorically. This is the position of the majority, and al-Jawhari was certain of it, etc.
With
Language is about...
Because it is widespread in their speech before the advent of revelation, and the Quran was revealed in the language of the Arabs. He said: {And pray for them} (9:103) meaning supplicate for them. In the hadith about answering the invitation, 'If he is fasting, let him pray,' meaning let him supplicate for them with goodness and blessing. From this is the prayer over the deceased. Salah is a verbal noun of salla, and the masdar is tasliyah, and...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi opens the section on the Book of Prayer (Kitab al-Salah) by defining its linguistic and technical meanings. In language, salah primarily means supplication (du'a), and this is the consensus of the majority of scholars. In Shari'ah, it refers to the specific acts of worship that begin with takbir and end with taslim. The passage highlights that no revealed religion was devoid of prayer, but the five daily prayers as a combined set are unique to the Ummah of Muhammad (SAW).

The text then provides a historical narration from At-Tahawi, tracing the origin of each prayer to specific events in the lives of earlier prophets: Adam's repentance at dawn gave two rak'ahs as Fajr; Ishaq's ransom at noon gave four rak'ahs as Zuhr; 'Uzayr's resurrection at 'Asr gave four rak'ahs as 'Asr; Dawud's forgiveness at Maghrib gave three rak'ahs (he failed to complete the fourth due to weeping); and our Prophet (SAW) introduced 'Isha'. This narration indicates that the timing and rak'ahs were established based on these events, though it is understood that the prophets prayed these prayers before their nations.

The passage also mentions unique features of this Ummah's prayer: the adhan, iqamah, takbir for opening, saying amin, the specific wording after bowing, and the prohibition of speech. These are part of the distinctiveness of Islamic prayer.

The verse from Surah at-Tawbah (9:103) is cited to show that 'salah' in the Quran can mean supplication, confirming the linguistic meaning. The hadith about answering an invitation also uses 'salah' in the sense of supplication. The verbal noun 'tasliyah' is the proper source word for the act of praying.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salah): Linguistically means supplication; in Shari'ah, specific acts of worship starting with takbir and ending with taslim.
التصلية (al-tasliya): The masdar (verbal noun) form of the verb salla, meaning the act of performing salah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary linguistic meaning of 'salah' according to the majority?
A) Bowing
B) Worship
C) Supplication (du'a)
D) Prostration

Key Takeaway
Salah is both a universal act of supplication and a specific Shari'ah worship; its five daily prayers have roots in the prophetic traditions before Islam.

The Definition of Salah: Linguistic and Shariah
Defines salah and discusses the nature of the term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and Shariah definitions of salah and explain the Hanafi debate on whether it is a transferred or altered name.

Core Idea
Salah linguistically means supplication; in Shariah it retains that meaning while adding specific actions.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the dual definition of salah. Understanding the connection between the linguistic root (du'a) and the Shariah meaning (specific acts) is essential for grasping why certain rulings apply, such as the validity of a mute person's prayer. The commentator also clarifies a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the term is 'transferred' (manqul) or 'altered' (mugheyyar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Read the first line: 'فهي في اللغة عبارة عن الدعاء، وفي الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان والأفعال المخصوصة.' Note that linguistically it is supplication; in Shariah it is specific pillars and actions.
2
Understand the morphological derivation
Follow the etymology: أصل صلاة صلوة, and the transformation to alif. This shows the word is derived from دعاء, reinforcing the linguistic meaning.
3
Analyze the debate: transferred vs. altered name
The commentator presents two views. The first (al-mughayyar) says the Shariah meaning includes the linguistic meaning with an addition. The second (al-manqul) says the original meaning is abandoned entirely. Identify the key evidence for each view mentioned in the text.
The mashhur (preferred) view is that it is altered, not transferred.
4
Apply the evidence to the mute person case
The text mentions that a mute person can pray without uttering du'a. Consider how this supports the manqul view (no actual supplication) but also how the mugheyyar view can account for it (the act is still called salah because it includes the intention and meaning of supplication).
This shows the practical significance of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهي في اللغة عبارة عن الدعاء، وفي الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان والأفعال المخصوصة. عدلوا عن المصدر إلى اسمه لإيهامه خلاف المقصود وهو التصلية بمعنى التعذيب بالنار فإنه مصدر مشترك بين صلى بالتشديد بمعنى دعا وصلى بالتخفيف بمعنى أحرق، وأصل صلاة صلوة كتمرة نقلت فتحة الواو إلى الساكن قبلها فتحركت الواو بحسب الأصل، وانفتح ما قبلها الآن فقلبت الواو ألفاً بدليل الجمع على صلوات، ولا ترسم بالواو إلا في القرآن. قوله: (وفي الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان الخ) أي حقيقة وفي الدعاء مجازاً فهي في اللغة حقيقة في الدعاء مجاز في العبادة المخصوصة وفي الشرع بالعكس سميت بها هذه الأفعال المخصوصة لاشتمالها على الدعاء ففي المعنى الشرعي المعنى اللغوي وزيادة فتكون من الأسماء المغيرة. قال في الغاية، والظاهر أنها من الأسماء المنقولة لوجود الصلاة بدون الدعاء في الأمي، والأخرس والفرق بين النقل والتغيير أن النقل لا يكون فيه المعنى الأصلي منظوراً إليه لأن النقل في اللغة كالنسخ في الشرع وفي التغيير يكون منظوراً له لكن زيد عليه شيء آخر.
So it (salah) in language is an expression for supplication, and in Shariah it is an expression for specific pillars and actions. They turned away from the verbal noun to its name because it conceals the opposite of what is intended, and it is 'tasliyah' meaning punishment with fire, for it is a shared verbal noun between 'salla' with tashdid meaning called upon (du'a) and 'salla' without tashdid meaning burned. The origin of 'salah' is 'salwah' like 'tamrah'; the fatha of the waw was moved to the preceding silent letter so the waw became movable by origin, and now what precedes it is open so the waw turned to an alif, evidenced by the plural 'salawat', and it is not written with waw except in the Quran. He said (i.e., the author): (In Shariah it is an expression for the pillars etc.) meaning in reality, and in supplication it is metaphorical. So it is in language real in supplication, metaphorical in the specific worship, and in Shariah it is the opposite; these specific actions are called by this name because they include supplication, so in the Shariah meaning there is the linguistic meaning and an addition, so it is from 'al-asma' al-mughayyarah' (altered names). He said in al-Ghayah: it appears that it is from 'al-asma' al-manqulah' (transferred names) because salah exists without supplication in the illiterate and the mute; and the difference between transfer (naql) and alteration (taghyir) is that in transfer the original meaning is not considered, because transfer in language is like abrogation in Shariah, whereas in alteration the original meaning is considered but something else is added to it.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling presented as a critical refinement by the commentator. It explains the linguistic and Shariah definitions of salah. Linguistically, 'salah' means supplication (du'a), and the commentary explains why the verbal noun 'tasliyah' was avoided (due to its shared homonym meaning 'burning'). The morphological derivation from 'salwah' is given. In Shariah, 'salah' refers to the specific actions and pillars (arkan) of prayer. The commentator then discusses whether the term is a 'transferred name' (manqul) or an 'altered name' (mugheyyar). The difference is that in a transferred name (like many Islamic terms), the original linguistic meaning is completely abandoned; in an altered name, the original meaning is included but with an added stipulation. The commentator notes that the position of al-Ghayah is that it is a transferred name because salah (prayer) exists without actual supplication (e.g., by a mute person). However, the mashhur (well-known) view in the Hanafi school is that it is an altered name, as the linguistic meaning of supplication is still contained within the Shariah act, as prayer includes supplication. This linguistic subtlety has implications for understanding the nature of worship: the Shariah meaning builds upon the linguistic foundation.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salah): Linguistically: supplication (du'a). In Shariah: specific pillars and actions (arkan wa af'al makhsusah).
الأسماء المغيرة (al-asma' al-mughayyarah): Altered names: the original linguistic meaning is still considered but an additional Shariah element is added.
الأسماء المنقولة (al-asma' al-manqulah): Transferred names: the original linguistic meaning is abandoned entirely and replaced by a Shariah meaning.
شروع (shuru'): Commencement: the start of the book of prayer after the introductory material on purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between a transferred name (manqul) and an altered name (mugheyyar) according to the passage?
A) A transferred name keeps the original meaning; an altered name abandons it.
B) A transferred name abandons the original meaning completely; an altered name retains it with an addition.
C) There is no difference; the terms are synonymous.
D) A transferred name is used only for acts of worship; an altered name for transactions.

Key Takeaway
Salah in Shariah is an altered name (mugheyyar) that retains the linguistic sense of supplication while adding specific physical acts.

The Obligation of Salah and the Fard/Wajib Distinction
Ruling with proof on the obligation of salah and the fard/wajib distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal status of the five daily prayers and witr according to the Hanafi school, and explain the distinction between fard and wajib based on evidentiary strength.

Core Idea
The five daily prayers are fard; witr is wajib — a category distinct from fard based on the strength of evidence.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the foundational obligation of salah. It specifies when and how the prayer was made obligatory, establishes the number of daily prayers, and clarifies the Hanafi distinction between fard and wajib. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper fiqh literacy, as it governs many acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling regarding the five daily prayers
The text states the five prayers are fard, established by hadith and ijma. Recognize that fard here means individual obligation (fard 'ayn).
2
Identify the status of witr
The text explicitly says 'al-witr wajib laysa minha' — witr is wajib, not among the five. Understand the separate category of wajib in Hanafi law.
Wajib is an obligation proven by zanni evidence, while fard is proven by qat'i evidence.
3
Understand the basis for the fard/wajib distinction
The proof for the five prayers is stronger (mutawatir or qat'i) while witr's proof is ahad (zanni), leading to different legal categories.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub, but the level of evidence determines whether the ruling is called fard or wajib.
4
Note the historical context of the obligation
Salah was made obligatory on the night of Mi'raj, originally 50 rak'ahs reduced to 5. The times are exactly five per day, set by hadith and consensus.
The commentary expands on the date and the reduction through Musa (peace be upon him).
5
Grasp the wisdom and cause of obligation
The wisdom (hikmah) is gratitude to Allah and expiation of sins. The original cause (sabab asli) is Allah's eternal command; the times are apparent causes (asbab zahira) for facilitation.
This distinction between sabab asli and sabab zahir is important for understanding how rulings are triggered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرضت ليلة المعراج وعدد أوقاتها خمس للحديث والإجماع والوتر واجب ليس منها، وفرضت في الأصل ركعتين ركعتين إلا المغرب فأقرت في السفر وزيدت في الحضر إلا في الفجر وحكمة إفتراضها شكر المنعم وسببها الأصلي خطاب الله تعالى الأزلي والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً. قوله: وفرضت ليلة (المعراج وهي ليلة الإسراء على ما عليه جمهور المحدثين والمفسرين والفقهاء والمتكلمين، وهو الحق كما قاله القاضي عياض، وكانت بعد البعثة على الصواب قبل الهجرة بسنة كما جرى عليه النووي ونقل ابن حزم فيه الإجماع، وقيل غير ذلك وقيل في ربيع الأول ليلة وعشرين وجرى عليه جمع وقيل ليلة سبع وعشرين من رجب، وعليه العمل في جميع الأمصار، وجزم به النووي في الروضة، تبعاً للرافعي، وقيل غير ذلك وفي فرضها تلك الليلة التنبيه على فضلها حيث لم تفرض إلا في الحضرة المقدسة فوق السموات السبع بعد طهارة باطنه، وظاهره بماء زمزم وفرضت أولاً خمسين وردت إلى خمس بواسطة سيدنا موسى عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام. قوله للحديث) وهو تعليمه الأعرابي وإمامة جبريل. قوله: ( والوتر واجب أي لا فرض وبين الفرض، والواجب فرق بين السماء والأرض، والمشهور أنه فرض عملي يفوت الجواز بفواته ومن أطلق الوجوب أراد به هذا المعنى، ومن تأمل تفاريعهم جزم به ولا يرد الوتر على قوله وعدد الخ لأنه في بيان الأوقات لا في تعيين المفروض وأيضاً هو فرض عملي وصلوات الأوقات إعتقادية. قوله: شكر المنعم) أي وتكفير الذنوب.
And it was made obligatory on the night of Mi'raj, and the number of its times is five based on hadith and ijma', and witr is wajib not from them (i.e., not among the five fard prayers). It was originally made obligatory as two rak'ahs each, except Maghrib, so it was confirmed in travel (as two) and increased in residence (to four) except for Fajr. The wisdom of its obligation is thanks to the Benefactor, and its original cause is the eternal address of Allah Most High, and the times are apparent causes for facilitation. His statement: 'and it was made obligatory on the night of Mi'raj' and it is the night of Isra according to the majority of hadith scholars, exegetes, jurists, and theologians; it is the truth as said by Qadi Iyad; it was after the prophethood, correctly one year before the Hijra as stated by Nawawi; Ibn Hazm reported consensus on this; others said it was on the night of the 20th of Rabi' al-Awwal, and a group acted on this; others said the 27th of Rajab, and this is acted upon in all cities; Nawawi decided this in Rawdah following al-Rafi'i. The making it fard on that night indicates its excellence because it was only made fard in the sacred presence above the seven heavens after his inner and outer purification with Zamzam water; it was originally fifty (rak'ahs) and reduced to five through the mediation of our master Musa. His statement 'based on hadith' refers to the teaching of the Bedouin and the leadership of Jibril. His statement: 'and witr is wajib' meaning it is not fard, and between fard and wajib is a difference like heaven and earth; the mashhur is that it is 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation) whose permissibility is lost upon missing it; whoever absolutely says wajib intends this meaning; whoever examines their derivations will decide this; and witr does not contradict his statement 'and the number of its times...' because he is explaining the times, not specifying the fard; also it is a practical fard while the five are doctrinal. His statement: 'wisdom of its obligation is thanks to the Benefactor' meaning and expiation of sins.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the obligation of salah. The commentator expands on the matn by detailing the exact night of obligation (the night of Mi'raj/Isra), noting the scholarly consensus that it was about one year before Hijra. He emphasizes the honor of the occasion: the Prophet was purified with Zamzam and received the command directly above the heavens. The original obligation of fifty prayers reduced to five through Moses (peace be upon him) is mentioned. The number of daily prayers is five, established by hadith (the Bedouin's question and Jibril's leadership) and ijma'. The commentator clarifies that witr is wajib, not fard, and explains the Hanafi distinction: fard is what is established by qat'i evidence (Quran, mutawatir sunnah); wajib is established by zanni evidence. Some later Hanafis call witr 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation) meaning that its loss is critical and it must be performed, but it is not part of the five daily prayers. The wisdom of salah is gratitude to Allah (shukr al-mun'im) and expiation of sins. The original cause of the obligation is Allah's eternal command (khitab Allah al-azali), while the times are external causes (asbab) for facilitation.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): An obligation established by qat'i evidence (Quran or mutawatir sunnah); the five daily prayers are fard.
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligation established by zanni evidence (like ahad hadith); witr is wajib.
الوتر (al-witr): An odd-numbered prayer performed after isha, considered wajib in Hanafi school, not among the five fard prayers.
المعراج (al-mi'raj): The night ascent of the Prophet to heaven where salah was made obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the status of witr prayer in relation to the five daily prayers?
A) Witr is one of the five obligatory prayers.
B) Witr is fard 'ayn like the five prayers.
C) Witr is wajib, not fard, and distinct from the five.
D) Witr is sunnah mu'akkadah and recommended.

Key Takeaway
The five daily prayers are fard; witr is wajib, a distinct category in Hanafi law based on evidentiary strength.

The Definition of Salah: Linguistic and Legal Meanings
Commentary on the definition of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the linguistic and legal definitions of salah and state why the legal definition is primary in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Salah is a legal term for specific actions, not primarily supplication.

The author opens the chapter on prayer by clarifying what 'salah' means. While the word lexically means 'supplication', in Sacred Law it is a technical term for the well-known pillars and actions. This distinction matters because it affects how we understand the obligation and the conditions of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings
Locate where the text defines salah linguistically (du'a) and legally (arkan wa af'al makhsusah). The commentator then discusses which is real and which is metaphorical in each domain.
The text states: 'و في الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان والأفعال المخصوصة'
2
Analyze the linguistic transformation
Trace the morphological development from 'salwah' to 'salah'. Understand why the waw was changed to alif and why it is spelled with waw only in the Quran.
The root is ص ل و; the original form was صَلْوَة.
3
Distinguish naql from taghyir
The commentator explains that the legal meaning is a 'naql' (transmission) that completely shifts the meaning, not a 'taghyir' (change) that retains the original. Compare how this affects the relationship between the two meanings.
Naql is like abrogation; the original meaning is no longer considered.
4
Apply the distinction
Consider the implications: if salah is primarily a technical term, then the presence or absence of supplication (du'a) does not define the act. This solves the issue of the illiterate or mute person who prays without verbal supplication.
The text refers to 'الأمي والأخرس' as examples.

كتاب الصلاة الدعاء، وفي الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان والأفعال المخصوصة وفرضت ليلة المعراج وعدد أوقاتها خمس للحديث والإجماع والوتر واجب ليس منها، وفرضت في الأصل ركعتين ركعتين إلا المغرب فأقرت في السفر وزيدت في الحضر إلا في الفجر وحكمة إفتراضها شكر المنعم وسببها الأصلي خطاب الله تعالى الأزلي والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً عدلوا عن المصدر إلى اسمه لإيهامه خلاف ،المقصود وهو التصلية بمعنى التعذيب بالنار فإنه مصدر مشترك بين صلى بالتشديد بمعنى دعا (۱) وصلى بالتخفيف بمعنى أحرق، وأصل صلاة صلوة كتمرة نقلت فتحة الواو إلى الساكن قبلها فتحركت الواو بحسب الأصل، وانفتح ما قبلها الآن فقلبت الواو ألفاً بدليل الجمع على صلوات، ولا ترسم بالواو إلا في القرآن كما في الحموي على الأشباه وغيره قوله : ( وفي الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان الخ) أي حقيقة وفي الدعاء مجازاً فهي في اللغة حقيقة في الدعاء مجاز في العبادة المخصوصة وفي الشرع بالعكس سميت بها هذه الأفعال المخصوصة لاشتمالها على الدعاء ففي المعنى الشرعي المعنى اللغوي وزيادة فتكون من الأسماء المغيرة .اهـ. قال في الغاية، والظاهر أنها من الأسماء المنقولة لوجود الصلاة بدون الدعاء في الأمي، والأخرس والفرق بين النقل والتغيير أن النقل لا يكون فيه المعنى الأصلي منظوراً إليه لأن النقل في اللغة كالنسخ في الشرع وفي التغيير يكون منظوراً له لكن زيد عليه شيء آخر. قوله : وفرضت ليلة (المعراج وهي ليلة الإسراء على ما عليه جمهور المحدثين والمفسرين والفقهاء والمتكلمين، وهو الحق كما قاله القاضي عياض، وكانت بعد البعثة على الصواب قبل الهجرة بسنة كما جرى عليه النووي ونقل ابن حزم فيه الإجماع، وقيل غير ذلك وقيل في ربيع الأول ليلة وعشرين وجرى عليه جمع وقيل ليلة سبع وعشرين من رجب، وعليه العمل في جميع الأمصار ، وجزم به النووي في الروضة، تبعاً للرافعي، وقيل غير ذلك وفي فرضها تلك الليلة التنبيه على فضلها حيث لم تفرض إلا في الحضرة المقدسة فوق السموات السبع بعد طهارة باطنه، وظاهره بماء زمزم وفرضت أولاً خمسين وردت إلى خمس بواسطة سيدنا موسى عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام قوله للحديث) وهو تعليمه الأعرابي وإمامة جبريل قوله : ( والوتر واجب أي لا ،فرض وبين الفرض، والواجب فرق بين السماء والأرض، والمشهور أنه فرض عملي يفوت الجواز بفواته ومن أطلق الوجوب أراد به هذا المعنى، ومن تأمل تفاريعهم جزم به ولا يرد الوتر على قوله وعدد الخ لأنه في بيان الأوقات لا في تعيين المفروض وأيضاً هو فرض عملي وصلوات الأوقات إعتقادية. قوله: شكر المنعم) أي وتكفير الذنوب كما قال : أرأيتم لو أن نهراً بباب أحدكم يغتسل فيه كل يوم خمساً هل يبقى من درنه شيء؟ قالوا: لا قال: فذلك مثل الصلوات الخمس يمحوا الله بهن الخطايا. قوله : (وسببها الأصلي خطاب الله تعالى (الأزلي أي سبب وجوب أدائها. واعلم أن عندهم وجوباً ووجوب أداء ووجود أداء ، ولكل منها سبب حقيقي، وسبب مجازي فالوجوب سببه الحقيقي إيجاب الله تعالى في الأزل، لأن الموجب للأحكام هو الله تعالى وحده لكن لما كان إيجابه تعالى غيباً عنا لا تطلع عليه جعل لنا سبحانه وتعالى أسباباً مجازية ظاهرة تيسيراً علينا، وهي الأوقات بدليل تجدد الوجوب بتجددها، والسبب من كل وقت جزء يتصل به الأداء، فإن لم يتصل الأداء بجزء منه أصلاً، فالجزء الأخير متعين للسببية، ولو ناقصاً، الأداء ووجوب الحقيقي خطاب الله تعالى أي طلبه منا ذلك وسببه الظاهري هو اللفظ الدال على ذلك كلفظ أقيموا الصلاة، والفرق بين الوجوب، ووجوب الأداء أن الوجوب هو شغل الذمة، ووجوب الأداء طلب تفريغها، كما في غاية البيان، وسبب وجود الأداء الحقيقي خلق الله تعالى له وسببه الظاهري إستطاعة العبد وهي مع الفعل قوله : ( والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً) اعلم أن الأوقات لها جهات مختلفة بالحيثيات فمن حيث أن الصلاة لا تجوز قبلها وإنما تجب بها أسباب، ومن حيث أن الأداء لا بعدها لإشتراط الوقت له وإنما تكون قضاء شروط، ومن حيث أنها يجوز فيها أداء الفرض وغيره كالنفل ظروف بخلاف شهر رمضان فإنه معيار للصوم حتى لو نوى نفلاً واجباً آخر يقع عن الفرض قوله : (سقوط الواجب) أي في الدنيا . قوله : (ونيل الثواب) أي في العقبي أن كان مخلصاً أما المرائي، فلا ثواب له على ما في مختارات النوازل، ويخالفه ما نقله البيري عن الذخيرة من أن الرياء إنما ينفي تضاعف الثواب فقط وذكر بعضهم أن الرياء لا يدخل في الفرائض أي في حق سقوط الواجب . تنبيه : المختار أنه لم يكن قبل بعثته متعبداً بشرع أحد لأنه قبل الرسالة في مقام النبوة، ولم يكن من أمة نبي بل كان يعمل بما يظهر له بالكشف الصادق من شريعة إبراهيم، وقيل غير ذلك قوله : (أي لتكليف الشخص) تفسير مراد قوله : (لأنه شرط للخطاب) تقدم أنه أحد أقوال والأصح التكليف وفائدته التعذيب على تركها في الآخرة زيادة على عذاب الكفر . قوله : (ولكن تؤمر بها الأولاد ذكوراً وإناثاً والصوم كالصلاة كما في صوم القهستاني، وفي الدر عن حظر الاختيار أنه يؤمر بالصوم والصلاة وينهي عن شرب الخمر يتألف الخير ويعرض عن الشر والظاهر منه أن هذا واجب على الولي. قوله : رفقاً به علة لقوله لا بخشبة، وقوله : وزجراً
The Book of Prayer: supplication, and in the Sacred Law it is an expression for the specific pillars and actions. It was made obligatory on the night of the Ascension. The number of its times is five, by hadith and consensus. Witr is obligatory (wajib), not from them. It was originally made obligatory two rak'ahs at a time except Maghrib, so it was confirmed in travel and increased in residence except for Fajr. The wisdom of its obligation is gratitude to the Benefactor. Its original cause is the pre-eternal address of Allah, and the times are apparent causes for facilitation. They turned from the verbal noun to its name to avoid suggesting the opposite, which is 'tasliyah' meaning punishment with fire, for it is a homonymous verbal noun between 'salla' with shaddah meaning supplication and 'salla' with tashdid meaning burned. The origin of 'salah' is 'salwah' like 'tamrah'; the fathah of the waw was moved to the preceding silent letter, so the waw became moving according to origin, and now its preceding letter is open, so the waw was turned into an alif, evidenced by the plural 'salawat'. It is not written with a waw except in the Quran, as in al-Hamawi on al-Ashbah and others. His saying: 'and in the Sacred Law it is an expression for the pillars etc.' meaning truly, and in supplication metaphorically. So in language it is literal for supplication and metaphorical for the specific worship, and in Sacred Law the opposite. These specific actions are named with it because they include supplication. So in the legal meaning, there is the linguistic meaning and an increase, so it becomes among the transferred names. End quote. He said in al-Ghayah: apparently it is among the transmitted names, because prayer exists without supplication for the illiterate and the mute. The difference between transmission and change is that in transmission the original meaning is not considered, because transmission in language is like abrogation in law, while in change the original meaning is considered but something else is added. His saying: 'It was made obligatory on the night of the Ascension' which is the night of the Isra, according to the majority of hadith scholars, commentators, jurists, and theologians, and it is the truth as Qadi Iyad said. It was after the mission, correctly one year before the Hijra, as al-Nawawi stated, and Ibn Hazm reported consensus on it. Others said differently: some said on the night of the 20th of Rabi' al-Awwal, and a group followed it; some said on the 27th of Rajab, and upon it is the practice in all regions. Al-Nawawi asserted it in al-Rawdah following al-Rafi'i. Others said differently. Its obligation on that night indicates its virtue, as it was not obligated except in the holy presence above the seven heavens after the purification of his inner and outer self with Zamzam water. It was first obligated as fifty and reduced to five through Sayyidina Musa, peace be upon him. His saying: 'by hadith' i.e., his teaching of the Bedouin and the leadership of Jibril. His saying: 'and Witr is wajib' i.e., not fard. Between fard and wajib is a difference like between heaven and earth. The well-known view is that it is a practical fard whose permissibility is lost by its loss. Whoever says 'wajib' means this meaning. Whoever ponders their subdivisions concludes it. Witr does not contradict his statement 'and the number of its times...' because it is about the times, not about specifying the obligatory. Also, it is a practical fard while the prayers of the times are doctrinal. His saying: 'gratitude to the Benefactor' i.e., expiation of sins, as he said: 'Do you think that if a river were at the door of one of you and he bathed in it five times daily, would any dirt remain on him?' They said: No. He said: 'That is the likeness of the five prayers; Allah erases sins by them.' His saying: 'Its original cause is the address of Allah, the Pre-Eternal' i.e., the cause of the obligation of performing it. Know that according to them there is obligation, obligation of performance, and existence of performance. Each has a real cause and a metaphorical cause. The real cause of obligation is Allah's making it obligatory in pre-eternity, because the Obligator of rulings is Allah alone. But since His pre-eternal obligation is hidden from us, He made for us metaphorical apparent causes as a facilitation, which are the times, evidenced by the renewal of obligation with their renewal. The cause from each time is a part connected to performance. If performance is not connected to any part of it at all, then the last part is determined for causality, even if it is deficient for performance. His saying: 'and the times are apparent causes for facilitation' – know that the times have different aspects: from the perspective that prayer is not valid before them and is obligatory by them, they are causes; from the perspective that performance is not after them because the time is a condition for it, it becomes a qada condition; from the perspective that it is permissible to perform the obligatory and other acts like nafl within them, they are containers, unlike Ramadan which is a standard for fasting so that if one intends a nafl or another obligatory, it falls for the obligatory. His saying: 'fulfillment of the wajib' i.e., in this world. His saying: 'and attainment of reward' i.e., in the Hereafter, if he is sincere. As for the one who shows off, he has no reward according to what is in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil. This is contradicted by what al-Bayri transmitted from al-Dhakhirah that ostentation only negates the multiplication of reward. Some mentioned that ostentation does not enter into the obligatory acts, i.e., with regard to the fulfillment of the wajib. Note: The chosen view is that he was not obligated by the law of anyone before his mission, because before his message he was in the station of prophethood and was not of the nation of any prophet, but he acted according to what appeared to him through true unveiling from the law of Ibrahim. Others said otherwise. His saying: 'that is for the taklif of the person' is an interpretation of the intended meaning of his saying: 'for it is a condition for the address'. It was mentioned earlier that this is one of the views, and the most correct is taklif. Its benefit is punishment for abandoning them in the Hereafter, in addition to the punishment for disbelief. His saying: 'but children are commanded with it' – males and females. Fasting is like prayer, as in Sawm al-Qahistani. In al-Durr from Hidd 'ala al-Ikhtiyar, that he is commanded to fast and pray, and forbidden from drinking wine, to attract good and turn away from evil. It appears that this is obligatory on the guardian. His saying: 'as a kindness to him' is the cause for his saying 'not with a wooden stick'. His saying: 'and as a deterrent'.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah opens the Book of Prayer by defining the term, stating its obligation, its times, and the conditions for its obligation. The author begins by clarifying that although 'salah' lexically means supplication, in Sacred Law it is a technical term referring to specific pillars and actions. The commentator then discusses the linguistic origin of the word, noting the homonymous roots and the transformation from 'salwah' to 'salah'. He explains the distinction between 'naql' (transmission) and 'taghyir' (change), with the former completely shifting the meaning. The passage then addresses the historical event of the obligation of the five daily prayers on the night of the Mi'raj, noting scholarly differences on the exact date but affirming the well-known view that it was one year before the Hijra. The obligation was initially fifty prayers, reduced to five through the intercession of Musa (AS). The five times are established by hadith and ijma. Witr is classified as wajib, not fard, and a distinction is drawn between fard and wajib in the Hanafi school: fard is established by qat'i evidence, while wajib is established by zanni evidence. The wisdom behind prayer is expressed as gratitude and expiation of sins, supported by the hadith of the river. The passage then delves into the causes of obligation: the original cause is Allah's pre-eternal command, while the apparent causes are the times themselves. A nuanced discussion follows on the distinction between wujub (obligation), wujub al-ada' (obligation of performance), and wujud al-ada' (existence of performance), each with a real and apparent cause. Finally, the conditions for the obligation of prayer on a person are listed: Islam, puberty, and sanity. However, children are commanded to pray from age seven and beaten at ten, as a disciplinary measure. The commentator notes that the guardian is obliged to order this. This passage sets the foundational framework for the entire chapter on prayer.

Key Terms
صلاة (salāh): In this passage, defined lexically as supplication but legally as specific pillars and actions.
نقل (naql): Transmission, where the original meaning is completely abandoned in favor of a new technical meaning.
تغيير (taghyir): Change, where the original meaning is retained but expanded or modified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal definition of salah?
A) Supplication (du'a)
B) Specific pillars and actions (al-arkan wa al-af'al al-makhsusah)
C) Both A and B equally
D) Purification of the heart

Key Takeaway
Salah is a legal term for specific actions; its linguistic meaning of supplication is secondary and not required for validity.

The Obligation and Times of Salah: From Mi'raj to the Five Daily Prayers
Commentary on the obligation and times of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state how the five daily prayers were made obligatory, identify the five times, and explain why witr is classified as wajib not fard in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The five prayers were made obligatory during the Mi'raj; witr is wajib, not fard.

This passage recounts the foundational event of the obligation of prayer—the Night of Ascension (Mi'raj). It also clarifies the number of daily prayers (five), the evidence from hadith and consensus, and the Hanafi ruling that witr is wajib, not fard. Understanding the difference between fard and wajib is essential for knowing the legal weight of each component of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Locate the event of obligation
Find where the text states that salah was made obligatory on the night of Mi'raj. Note the scholarly discussion on the exact date.
The text says 'وفرضت ليلة المعراج'.
2
Identify the number of times and evidence
The text says the number of times is five, based on hadith (teaching of the Bedouin, leadership of Jibril) and consensus. List the five times.
The hadith of the Bedouin and the leadership of Jibril are mentioned.
3
Understand the Hanafi position on witr
The passage states that witr is wajib, not fard. It explains the difference: fard is established by qat'i evidence, wajib by zanni evidence. Witr is a 'fard amali' (practical fard) not a 'fard i'tiqadi' (doctrinal fard).
The phrase 'بين الفرض والواجب فرق بين السماء والأرض' emphasizes the distinction.
4
Evaluate the hadith of the river
The hadith illustrates the wisdom behind the five prayers: they expiate sins. This is mentioned as part of the benefit of obligation.
The hadith is quoted: 'أرأيتم لو أن نهراً...'

للحديث) وهو تعليمه الأعرابي وإمامة جبريل قوله : ( والوتر واجب أي لا ،فرض وبين الفرض، والواجب فرق بين السماء والأرض، والمشهور أنه فرض عملي يفوت الجواز بفواته ومن أطلق الوجوب أراد به هذا المعنى، ومن تأمل تفاريعهم جزم به ولا يرد الوتر على قوله وعدد الخ لأنه في بيان الأوقات لا في تعيين المفروض وأيضاً هو فرض عملي وصلوات الأوقات إعتقادية. قوله: شكر المنعم) أي وتكفير الذنوب كما قال : أرأيتم لو أن نهراً بباب أحدكم يغتسل فيه كل يوم خمساً هل يبقى من درنه شيء؟ قالوا: لا قال: فذلك مثل الصلوات الخمس يمحوا الله بهن الخطايا. قوله : (وسببها الأصلي خطاب الله تعالى (الأزلي أي سبب وجوب أدائها. واعلم أن عندهم وجوباً ووجوب أداء ووجود أداء ، ولكل منها سبب حقيقي، وسبب مجازي فالوجوب سببه الحقيقي إيجاب الله تعالى في الأزل، لأن الموجب للأحكام هو الله تعالى وحده لكن لما كان إيجابه تعالى غيباً عنا لا تطلع عليه جعل لنا سبحانه وتعالى أسباباً مجازية ظاهرة تيسيراً علينا، وهي الأوقات بدليل تجدد الوجوب بتجددها، والسبب من كل وقت جزء يتصل به الأداء، فإن لم يتصل الأداء بجزء منه أصلاً، فالجزء الأخير متعين للسببية، ولو ناقصاً، الأداء ووجوب الحقيقي خطاب الله تعالى أي طلبه منا ذلك وسببه الظاهري هو اللفظ الدال على ذلك كلفظ أقيموا الصلاة، والفرق بين الوجوب، ووجوب الأداء أن الوجوب هو شغل الذمة، ووجوب الأداء طلب تفريغها، كما في غاية البيان، وسبب وجود الأداء الحقيقي خلق الله تعالى له وسببه الظاهري إستطاعة العبد وهي مع الفعل قوله : ( والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً) اعلم أن الأوقات لها جهات مختلفة بالحيثيات فمن حيث أن الصلاة لا تجوز قبلها وإنما تجب بها أسباب، ومن حيث أن الأداء لا بعدها لإشتراط الوقت له وإنما تكون قضاء شروط، ومن حيث أنها يجوز فيها أداء الفرض وغيره كالنفل ظروف بخلاف شهر رمضان فإنه معيار للصوم حتى لو نوى نفلاً واجباً آخر يقع عن الفرض قوله : (سقوط الواجب) أي في الدنيا . قوله : (ونيل الثواب) أي في العقبي أن كان مخلصاً أما المرائي، فلا ثواب له على ما في مختارات النوازل، ويخالفه ما نقله البيري عن الذخيرة من أن الرياء إنما ينفي تضاعف الثواب فقط وذكر بعضهم أن الرياء لا يدخل في الفرائض أي في حق سقوط الواجب . تنبيه : المختار أنه لم يكن قبل بعثته متعبداً بشرع أحد لأنه قبل الرسالة في مقام النبوة، ولم يكن من أمة نبي بل كان يعمل بما يظهر له بالكشف الصادق من شريعة إبراهيم، وقيل غير ذلك قوله : (أي لتكليف الشخص) تفسير مراد قوله : (لأنه شرط للخطاب) تقدم أنه أحد أقوال والأصح التكليف وفائدته التعذيب على تركها في الآخرة زيادة على عذاب الكفر . قوله : (ولكن تؤمر بها الأولاد ذكوراً وإناثاً والصوم كالصلاة كما في صوم القهستاني، وفي الدر عن حظر الاختيار أنه يؤمر بالصوم والصلاة وينهي عن شرب الخمر يتألف الخير ويعرض عن الشر والظاهر منه أن هذا واجب على الولي. قوله : رفقاً به علة لقوله لا بخشبة، وقوله : وزجراً
The Book of Prayer: supplication, and in the Sacred Law it is an expression for the specific pillars and actions. It was made obligatory on the night of the Ascension. The number of its times is five, by hadith and consensus. Witr is obligatory (wajib), not from them. It was originally made obligatory two rak'ahs at a time except Maghrib, so it was confirmed in travel and increased in residence except for Fajr. The wisdom of its obligation is gratitude to the Benefactor. Its original cause is the pre-eternal address of Allah, and the times are apparent causes for facilitation. They turned from the verbal noun to its name to avoid suggesting the opposite, which is 'tasliyah' meaning punishment with fire, for it is a homonymous verbal noun between 'salla' with shaddah meaning supplication and 'salla' with tashdid meaning burned. The origin of 'salah' is 'salwah' like 'tamrah'; the fathah of the waw was moved to the preceding silent letter, so the waw became moving according to origin, and now its preceding letter is open, so the waw was turned into an alif, evidenced by the plural 'salawat'. It is not written with a waw except in the Quran, as in al-Hamawi on al-Ashbah and others. His saying: 'and in the Sacred Law it is an expression for the pillars etc.' meaning truly, and in supplication metaphorically. So in language it is literal for supplication and metaphorical for the specific worship, and in Sacred Law the opposite. These specific actions are named with it because they include supplication. So in the legal meaning, there is the linguistic meaning and an increase, so it becomes among the transferred names. End quote. He said in al-Ghayah: apparently it is among the transmitted names, because prayer exists without supplication for the illiterate and the mute. The difference between transmission and change is that in transmission the original meaning is not considered, because transmission in language is like abrogation in law, while in change the original meaning is considered but something else is added. His saying: 'It was made obligatory on the night of the Ascension' which is the night of the Isra, according to the majority of hadith scholars, commentators, jurists, and theologians, and it is the truth as Qadi Iyad said. It was after the mission, correctly one year before the Hijra, as al-Nawawi stated, and Ibn Hazm reported consensus on it. Others said differently: some said on the night of the 20th of Rabi' al-Awwal, and a group followed it; some said on the 27th of Rajab, and upon it is the practice in all regions. Al-Nawawi asserted it in al-Rawdah following al-Rafi'i. Others said differently. Its obligation on that night indicates its virtue, as it was not obligated except in the holy presence above the seven heavens after the purification of his inner and outer self with Zamzam water. It was first obligated as fifty and reduced to five through Sayyidina Musa, peace be upon him. His saying: 'by hadith' i.e., his teaching of the Bedouin and the leadership of Jibril. His saying: 'and Witr is wajib' i.e., not fard. Between fard and wajib is a difference like between heaven and earth. The well-known view is that it is a practical fard whose permissibility is lost by its loss. Whoever says 'wajib' means this meaning. Whoever ponders their subdivisions concludes it. Witr does not contradict his statement 'and the number of its times...' because it is about the times, not about specifying the obligatory. Also, it is a practical fard while the prayers of the times are doctrinal. His saying: 'gratitude to the Benefactor' i.e., expiation of sins, as he said: 'Do you think that if a river were at the door of one of you and he bathed in it five times daily, would any dirt remain on him?' They said: No. He said: 'That is the likeness of the five prayers; Allah erases sins by them.' His saying: 'Its original cause is the address of Allah, the Pre-Eternal' i.e., the cause of the obligation of performing it. Know that according to them there is obligation, obligation of performance, and existence of performance. Each has a real cause and a metaphorical cause. The real cause of obligation is Allah's making it obligatory in pre-eternity, because the Obligator of rulings is Allah alone. But since His pre-eternal obligation is hidden from us, He made for us metaphorical apparent causes as a facilitation, which are the times, evidenced by the renewal of obligation with their renewal. The cause from each time is a part connected to performance. If performance is not connected to any part of it at all, then the last part is determined for causality, even if it is deficient for performance. His saying: 'and the times are apparent causes for facilitation' – know that the times have different aspects: from the perspective that prayer is not valid before them and is obligatory by them, they are causes; from the perspective that performance is not after them because the time is a condition for it, it becomes a qada condition; from the perspective that it is permissible to perform the obligatory and other acts like nafl within them, they are containers, unlike Ramadan which is a standard for fasting so that if one intends a nafl or another obligatory, it falls for the obligatory. His saying: 'fulfillment of the wajib' i.e., in this world. His saying: 'and attainment of reward' i.e., in the Hereafter, if he is sincere. As for the one who shows off, he has no reward according to what is in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil. This is contradicted by what al-Bayri transmitted from al-Dhakhirah that ostentation only negates the multiplication of reward. Some mentioned that ostentation does not enter into the obligatory acts, i.e., with regard to the fulfillment of the wajib. Note: The chosen view is that he was not obligated by the law of anyone before his mission, because before his message he was in the station of prophethood and was not of the nation of any prophet, but he acted according to what appeared to him through true unveiling from the law of Ibrahim. Others said otherwise. His saying: 'that is for the taklif of the person' is an interpretation of the intended meaning of his saying: 'for it is a condition for the address'. It was mentioned earlier that this is one of the views, and the most correct is taklif. Its benefit is punishment for abandoning them in the Hereafter, in addition to the punishment for disbelief. His saying: 'but children are commanded with it' – males and females. Fasting is like prayer, as in Sawm al-Qahistani. In al-Durr from Hidd 'ala al-Ikhtiyar, that he is commanded to fast and pray, and forbidden from drinking wine, to attract good and turn away from evil. It appears that this is obligatory on the guardian. His saying: 'as a kindness to him' is the cause for his saying 'not with a wooden stick'. His saying: 'and as a deterrent'.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah opens the Book of Prayer by defining the term, stating its obligation, its times, and the conditions for its obligation. The author begins by clarifying that although 'salah' lexically means supplication, in Sacred Law it is a technical term referring to specific pillars and actions. The commentator then discusses the linguistic origin of the word, noting the homonymous roots and the transformation from 'salwah' to 'salah'. He explains the distinction between 'naql' (transmission) and 'taghyir' (change), with the former completely shifting the meaning. The passage then addresses the historical event of the obligation of the five daily prayers on the night of the Mi'raj, noting scholarly differences on the exact date but affirming the well-known view that it was one year before the Hijra. The obligation was initially fifty prayers, reduced to five through the intercession of Musa (AS). The five times are established by hadith and ijma. Witr is classified as wajib, not fard, and a distinction is drawn between fard and wajib in the Hanafi school: fard is established by qat'i evidence, while wajib is established by zanni evidence. The wisdom behind prayer is expressed as gratitude and expiation of sins, supported by the hadith of the river. The passage then delves into the causes of obligation: the original cause is Allah's pre-eternal command, while the apparent causes are the times themselves. A nuanced discussion follows on the distinction between wujub (obligation), wujub al-ada' (obligation of performance), and wujud al-ada' (existence of performance), each with a real and apparent cause. Finally, the conditions for the obligation of prayer on a person are listed: Islam, puberty, and sanity. However, children are commanded to pray from age seven and beaten at ten, as a disciplinary measure. The commentator notes that the guardian is obliged to order this. This passage sets the foundational framework for the entire chapter on prayer.

Key Terms
فرض (farḍ): An obligation established by qat'i evidence; includes the five daily prayers.
واجب (wājib): An obligation established by zanni evidence; includes witr.
الوتر (al-witr): An odd-numbered prayer (usually 1 or 3 rak'ahs) after Isha; wajib in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between fard and wajib?
A) Fard is based on zanni evidence; wajib on qat'i.
B) Fard is based on qat'i evidence; wajib on zanni.
C) There is no difference; they are synonyms.
D) Fard is for actions, wajib for beliefs.

Key Takeaway
The five daily prayers are fard; witr is wajib. Distinguishing them is essential for correct legal classification.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Causes and Conditions for the Obligation of Prayer
Commentary on the causes and conditions of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the original cause (taklif), the apparent cause (time), and the conditions for obligation (Islam, puberty, sanity), and explain how they interact.

Core Idea
The obligation of prayer is caused by Allah's command and the entry of time; it binds only Muslims who are adult and sane.

This passage delves into the theoretical framework of obligation (wujub). It distinguishes between the real cause (khitab Allah al-azali) and the apparent cause (the times), and between obligation (wujub), obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'), and existence of performance (wujud al-ada'). It also lists the conditions that make a person responsible for prayer: Islam, puberty, and sanity. Additionally, it discusses the training of children.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate between real and apparent causes
The text explains that the real cause of obligation is Allah's pre-eternal command. Since we cannot perceive that, the times serve as apparent causes that facilitate understanding when prayer becomes obligatory.
The phrase 'والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً' is key.
2
Identify the three levels: wujub, wujub al-ada', wujud al-ada'
Wujub is the state of being obliged; wujub al-ada' is the demand to fulfill it; wujud al-ada' is the actual performance. Each has real and apparent causes.
This is a technical distinction common in Hanafi usul.
3
List the conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub)
The text states that prayer is obligatory upon every Muslim who is adult and sane. These are the conditions that make a person mukallaf (responsible).
The passage also mentions the issue of children: they are not obliged but should be trained.
4
Understand the wisdom and benefit of obligation
The wisdom is gratitude (shukr) and expiation of sins. The benefit is reward in the Hereafter and avoidance of punishment.
The text also notes that ostentation (riya) can negate reward, with a discussion on its effect.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة الدعاء، وفي الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان والأفعال المخصوصة وفرضت ليلة المعراج وعدد أوقاتها خمس للحديث والإجماع والوتر واجب ليس منها، وفرضت في الأصل ركعتين ركعتين إلا المغرب فأقرت في السفر وزيدت في الحضر إلا في الفجر وحكمة إفتراضها شكر المنعم وسببها الأصلي خطاب الله تعالى الأزلي والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً عدلوا عن المصدر إلى اسمه لإيهامه خلاف ،المقصود وهو التصلية بمعنى التعذيب بالنار فإنه مصدر مشترك بين صلى بالتشديد بمعنى دعا (۱) وصلى بالتخفيف بمعنى أحرق، وأصل صلاة صلوة كتمرة نقلت فتحة الواو إلى الساكن قبلها فتحركت الواو بحسب الأصل، وانفتح ما قبلها الآن فقلبت الواو ألفاً بدليل الجمع على صلوات، ولا ترسم بالواو إلا في القرآن كما في الحموي على الأشباه وغيره قوله : ( وفي الشريعة عبارة عن الأركان الخ) أي حقيقة وفي الدعاء مجازاً فهي في اللغة حقيقة في الدعاء مجاز في العبادة المخصوصة وفي الشرع بالعكس سميت بها هذه الأفعال المخصوصة لاشتمالها على الدعاء ففي المعنى الشرعي المعنى اللغوي وزيادة فتكون من الأسماء المغيرة .اهـ. قال في الغاية، والظاهر أنها من الأسماء المنقولة لوجود الصلاة بدون الدعاء في الأمي، والأخرس والفرق بين النقل والتغيير أن النقل لا يكون فيه المعنى الأصلي منظوراً إليه لأن النقل في اللغة كالنسخ في الشرع وفي التغيير يكون منظوراً له لكن زيد عليه شيء آخر. قوله : وفرضت ليلة (المعراج وهي ليلة الإسراء على ما عليه جمهور المحدثين والمفسرين والفقهاء والمتكلمين، وهو الحق كما قاله القاضي عياض، وكانت بعد البعثة على الصواب قبل الهجرة بسنة كما جرى عليه النووي ونقل ابن حزم فيه الإجماع، وقيل غير ذلك وقيل في ربيع الأول ليلة وعشرين وجرى عليه جمع وقيل ليلة سبع وعشرين من رجب، وعليه العمل في جميع الأمصار ، وجزم به النووي في الروضة، تبعاً للرافعي، وقيل غير ذلك وفي فرضها تلك الليلة التنبيه على فضلها حيث لم تفرض إلا في الحضرة المقدسة فوق السموات السبع بعد طهارة باطنه، وظاهره بماء زمزم وفرضت أولاً خمسين وردت إلى خمس بواسطة سيدنا موسى عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام قوله يتألف الخير ويعرض عن الشر والظاهر منه أن هذا واجب على الولي. قوله : رفقاً به علة لقوله لا بخشبة، وقوله : وزجراً
The Book of Prayer: supplication, and in the Sacred Law it is an expression for the specific pillars and actions. It was made obligatory on the night of the Ascension. The number of its times is five, by hadith and consensus. Witr is obligatory (wajib), not from them. It was originally made obligatory two rak'ahs at a time except Maghrib, so it was confirmed in travel and increased in residence except for Fajr. The wisdom of its obligation is gratitude to the Benefactor. Its original cause is the pre-eternal address of Allah, and the times are apparent causes for facilitation. They turned from the verbal noun to its name to avoid suggesting the opposite, which is 'tasliyah' meaning punishment with fire, for it is a homonymous verbal noun between 'salla' with shaddah meaning supplication and 'salla' with tashdid meaning burned. The origin of 'salah' is 'salwah' like 'tamrah'; the fathah of the waw was moved to the preceding silent letter, so the waw became moving according to origin, and now its preceding letter is open, so the waw was turned into an alif, evidenced by the plural 'salawat'. It is not written with a waw except in the Quran, as in al-Hamawi on al-Ashbah and others. His saying: 'and in the Sacred Law it is an expression for the pillars etc.' meaning truly, and in supplication metaphorically. So in language it is literal for supplication and metaphorical for the specific worship, and in Sacred Law the opposite. These specific actions are named with it because they include supplication. So in the legal meaning, there is the linguistic meaning and an increase, so it becomes among the transferred names. End quote. He said in al-Ghayah: apparently it is among the transmitted names, because prayer exists without supplication for the illiterate and the mute. The difference between transmission and change is that in transmission the original meaning is not considered, because transmission in language is like abrogation in law, while in change the original meaning is considered but something else is added. His saying: 'It was made obligatory on the night of the Ascension' which is the night of the Isra, according to the majority of hadith scholars, commentators, jurists, and theologians, and it is the truth as Qadi Iyad said. It was after the mission, correctly one year before the Hijra, as al-Nawawi stated, and Ibn Hazm reported consensus on it. Others said differently: some said on the night of the 20th of Rabi' al-Awwal, and a group followed it; some said on the 27th of Rajab, and upon it is the practice in all regions. Al-Nawawi asserted it in al-Rawdah following al-Rafi'i. Others said differently. Its obligation on that night indicates its virtue, as it was not obligated except in the holy presence above the seven heavens after the purification of his inner and outer self with Zamzam water. It was first obligated as fifty and reduced to five through Sayyidina Musa, peace be upon him. His saying: 'by hadith' i.e., his teaching of the Bedouin and the leadership of Jibril. His saying: 'and Witr is wajib' i.e., not fard. Between fard and wajib is a difference like between heaven and earth. The well-known view is that it is a practical fard whose permissibility is lost by its loss. Whoever says 'wajib' means this meaning. Whoever ponders their subdivisions concludes it. Witr does not contradict his statement 'and the number of its times...' because it is about the times, not about specifying the obligatory. Also, it is a practical fard while the prayers of the times are doctrinal. His saying: 'gratitude to the Benefactor' i.e., expiation of sins, as he said: 'Do you think that if a river were at the door of one of you and he bathed in it five times daily, would any dirt remain on him?' They said: No. He said: 'That is the likeness of the five prayers; Allah erases sins by them.' His saying: 'Its original cause is the address of Allah, the Pre-Eternal' i.e., the cause of the obligation of performing it. Know that according to them there is obligation, obligation of performance, and existence of performance. Each has a real cause and a metaphorical cause. The real cause of obligation is Allah's making it obligatory in pre-eternity, because the Obligator of rulings is Allah alone. But since His pre-eternal obligation is hidden from us, He made for us metaphorical apparent causes as a facilitation, which are the times, evidenced by the renewal of obligation with their renewal. The cause from each time is a part connected to performance. If performance is not connected to any part of it at all, then the last part is determined for causality, even if it is deficient for performance. His saying: 'and the times are apparent causes for facilitation' – know that the times have different aspects: from the perspective that prayer is not valid before them and is obligatory by them, they are causes; from the perspective that performance is not after them because the time is a condition for it, it becomes a qada condition; from the perspective that it is permissible to perform the obligatory and other acts like nafl within them, they are containers, unlike Ramadan which is a standard for fasting so that if one intends a nafl or another obligatory, it falls for the obligatory. His saying: 'fulfillment of the wajib' i.e., in this world. His saying: 'and attainment of reward' i.e., in the Hereafter, if he is sincere. As for the one who shows off, he has no reward according to what is in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil. This is contradicted by what al-Bayri transmitted from al-Dhakhirah that ostentation only negates the multiplication of reward. Some mentioned that ostentation does not enter into the obligatory acts, i.e., with regard to the fulfillment of the wajib. Note: The chosen view is that he was not obligated by the law of anyone before his mission, because before his message he was in the station of prophethood and was not of the nation of any prophet, but he acted according to what appeared to him through true unveiling from the law of Ibrahim. Others said otherwise. His saying: 'that is for the taklif of the person' is an interpretation of the intended meaning of his saying: 'for it is a condition for the address'. It was mentioned earlier that this is one of the views, and the most correct is taklif. Its benefit is punishment for abandoning them in the Hereafter, in addition to the punishment for disbelief. His saying: 'but children are commanded with it' – males and females. Fasting is like prayer, as in Sawm al-Qahistani. In al-Durr from Hidd 'ala al-Ikhtiyar, that he is commanded to fast and pray, and forbidden from drinking wine, to attract good and turn away from evil. It appears that this is obligatory on the guardian. His saying: 'as a kindness to him' is the cause for his saying 'not with a wooden stick'. His saying: 'and as a deterrent'.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah opens the Book of Prayer by defining the term, stating its obligation, its times, and the conditions for its obligation. The author begins by clarifying that although 'salah' lexically means supplication, in Sacred Law it is a technical term referring to specific pillars and actions. The commentator then discusses the linguistic origin of the word, noting the homonymous roots and the transformation from 'salwah' to 'salah'. He explains the distinction between 'naql' (transmission) and 'taghyir' (change), with the former completely shifting the meaning. The passage then addresses the historical event of the obligation of the five daily prayers on the night of the Mi'raj, noting scholarly differences on the exact date but affirming the well-known view that it was one year before the Hijra. The obligation was initially fifty prayers, reduced to five through the intercession of Musa (AS). The five times are established by hadith and ijma. Witr is classified as wajib, not fard, and a distinction is drawn between fard and wajib in the Hanafi school: fard is established by qat'i evidence, while wajib is established by zanni evidence. The wisdom behind prayer is expressed as gratitude and expiation of sins, supported by the hadith of the river. The passage then delves into the causes of obligation: the original cause is Allah's pre-eternal command, while the apparent causes are the times themselves. A nuanced discussion follows on the distinction between wujub (obligation), wujub al-ada' (obligation of performance), and wujud al-ada' (existence of performance), each with a real and apparent cause. Finally, the conditions for the obligation of prayer on a person are listed: Islam, puberty, and sanity. However, children are commanded to pray from age seven and beaten at ten, as a disciplinary measure. The commentator notes that the guardian is obliged to order this. This passage sets the foundational framework for the entire chapter on prayer.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujūb): The state of being legally obliged; distinct from wujub al-ada' (obligation of performance).
تكليف (taklīf): The legal responsibility that comes with being a mukallaf (adult, sane Muslim).
ولي (walī): Guardian (parent or custodian) who is responsible for training children.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is obliged to pray?
A) Every Muslim, adult or child.
B) Every adult Muslim who is sane.
C) Every person who believes in Allah.
D) Only males who have reached puberty.

Key Takeaway
Prayer is obligatory upon every Muslim who has reached puberty and is sane; children are trained but not obligated.

The Real and Apparent Causes of Prayer Obligation
Definition and expansion of the causes of prayer obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the real and apparent causes of wujub, wujub al-ada, and wujud al-ada, and state the Hanafi position on each.

Core Idea
Prayer obligation has three levels – liability, demand to perform, actual performance – each with a hidden divine cause and an apparent worldly cause.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi unpacks the multifaceted concept of legal cause (sabab) in prayer. The author distinguishes between wujub (liability), wujub al-ada (obligation to perform), and wujud al-ada (existence of performance), showing that each has a real cause in the eternal divine command and an apparent cause accessible to humans. Understanding these layers is crucial for grasping how time triggers obligation and how rulings apply in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three terms
Find and define 'wujub', 'wujub al-ada', and 'wujud al-ada' in the passage. Note their distinct roles.
Wujub is the abstract liability in the dhimmah; wujub al-ada is the command to discharge it; wujud al-ada is the actual performance.
2
Locate real and apparent causes for each
For each of the three, the text gives a real cause (haqiqi) and an apparent cause (majazi). Identify them.
Real causes are divine (e.g., Allah's address); apparent causes are worldly (e.g., times, command wording, ability).
3
Understand why times are apparent causes
The text says the obligation is renewed with the renewal of times, proving the times are apparent causes.
This shows the sabab is conceptually tied to time, not just the divine command.
4
Distinguish wujub from wujub al-ada
Note the text's explicit difference: wujub is the burden, wujub al-ada is the request to discharge it.
This distinction affects whether mere passage of time suffices (wujub) or active urging is needed (wujub al-ada).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسببها الأصلي خطاب الله تعالى (الأزلي أي سبب وجوب أدائها. واعلم أن عندهم وجوباً ووجوب أداء ووجود أداء ، ولكل منها سبب حقيقي، وسبب مجازي فالوجوب سببه الحقيقي إيجاب الله تعالى في الأزل، لأن الموجب للأحكام هو الله تعالى وحده لكن لما كان إيجابه تعالى غيباً عنا لا تطلع عليه جعل لنا سبحانه وتعالى أسباباً مجازية ظاهرة تيسيراً علينا، وهي الأوقات بدليل تجدد الوجوب بتجددها، والسبب من كل وقت جزء يتصل به الأداء، فإن لم يتصل الأداء بجزء منه أصلاً، فالجزء الأخير متعين للسببية، ولو ناقصاً، الأداء ووجوب الحقيقي خطاب الله تعالى أي طلبه منا ذلك وسببه الظاهري هو اللفظ الدال على ذلك كلفظ أقيموا الصلاة، والفرق بين الوجوب، ووجوب الأداء أن الوجوب هو شغل الذمة، ووجوب الأداء طلب تفريغها، كما في غاية البيان، وسبب وجود الأداء الحقيقي خلق الله تعالى له وسببه الظاهري إستطاعة العبد وهي مع الفعل قوله : ( والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً) اعلم أن الأوقات لها جهات مختلفة بالحيثيات فمن حيث أن الصلاة لا تجوز قبلها وإنما تجب بها أسباب، ومن حيث أن الأداء لا بعدها لإشتراط الوقت له وإنما تكون قضاء شروط، ومن حيث أنها يجوز فيها أداء الفرض وغيره كالنفل ظروف بخلاف شهر رمضان فإنه معيار للصوم حتى لو نوى نفلاً واجباً آخر يقع عن الفرض قوله : (وأسبابها أوقاتها) عامة المشايخ على أن السبب هو الجزء الذي يتصل به الأداء مطلقاً فإن اتصل بأول الوقت، كان هو السبب، وإلا فينتقل إلى ما به يتصل وإن لم يتصل الأداء بجزء منه أصلاً فالجزء الأخير متعين للسببية، ولو ناقصاً حتى تجب على مجنون ومغمى عليه أفاقا وحائض، ونفساء طهرتا وصبي بلغ ومرتد أسلم في آخر الوقت ولو صليا في أوله وبعد خروجه تضاف السببية إلى جملة الوقت ليثبت الواجب بصفتة الكمال ولأنه الأصل حتى يلزمهم القضاء في كامل هو الصحيح كما في الدر
Its original cause is the address of Allah, the eternal, meaning the cause of the obligation of its performance. Know that according to them (the scholars) there is obligation (wujub), obligation of performance (wujub al-ada), and existence of performance (wujud al-ada). For each there is a real cause and a figurative cause. The obligation's real cause is Allah's command in eternity, because the obligator of rulings is Allah alone, but since His command is hidden from us, He made for us apparent figurative causes as a facilitation, and they are the times, evidenced by the renewal of obligation with their renewal. The cause from each time is the part to which performance is attached; if performance is not attached to any part of it at all, then the last part is determined for causality, even if deficient. The real cause of the obligation of performance is Allah's address, i.e., His asking it from us, and its apparent cause is the wording indicating that, like the phrase 'Establish prayer'. The difference between wujub and wujub al-ada is that wujub is the burden of the dhimmah, and wujub al-ada is the request to discharge it, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. The cause of the existence of performance: real is Allah's creation of it, and apparent is the slave's ability, which is concurrent with the act. He said: 'And the times are apparent causes as a facilitation' – know that times have different aspects: from the aspect that prayer is not valid before them and is obligated by them as causes; from the aspect that performance cannot be after them because the time is a condition for it, and thus it would be a qada; from the aspect that it is permissible to perform the obligatory and other (nafl) within them as containers, unlike Ramadan which is a measure for fasting such that if one intends a nafl or other wajib, it falls for the wajib. He said: 'And their causes are the times' – the general body of mashayikh hold that the cause is the part to which performance is attached absolutely. If it attaches to the first part of the time, that is the cause; otherwise it shifts to that with which it attaches; if performance does not attach to any part at all, the last part is determined for causality, even if deficient, such that it becomes obligatory upon a madman or unconscious person who recovers, a menstruating woman or postpartum woman who becomes pure, a child who reaches puberty, and an apostate who becomes Muslim, at the end of the time. If they had prayed at the beginning, and after its exit, the causality is attributed to the entire time to establish the wajib with its perfect quality, and because it is the original, such that they are obligated to make up (qada) in complete form, which is the correct view as in al-Durr.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is an expansion probe into the legal cause (sabab) of prayer obligation. The author distinguishes between three levels: wujub (the liability in the dhimmah), wujub al-ada (the obligation to perform), and wujud al-ada (the actual performance). Each has a real cause (the eternal divine command) and an apparent cause (the time, the wording of command, and the slave's ability respectively). The key point is that the times are the apparent cause for the obligation to perform prayer, as the obligation is renewed with each time. The commentary then refines the concept of the cause (sabab) according to the majority of Hanafi scholars: it is the specific part of the time to which the performance attaches. If one prays at the beginning, that part is the cause; if one delays, the cause shifts to the later part; if one does not pray at all, the last part of the time becomes the cause, making the prayer a qada but still liable. This explains why those who become responsible at the end of the time (like a recovering madman) must pray even if the time is short.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): The legal liability (shughl al-dhimmah) meaning the obligation is established in the abstract sense.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada): The obligation to perform the prayer by discharging the liability.
سبب حقيقي (sabab haqiqi): The real cause, which is the divine command in eternity.
سبب مجازي (sabab majazi): The figurative/apparent cause, such as the times, which are observable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the apparent cause (sabab majazi) for wujub (the abstract obligation)?
A) The command 'Establish prayer'
B) The times of prayer
C) The slave's ability
D) The act of prayer

Key Takeaway
Prayer obligation has three layers, each with a hidden divine cause and an observable apparent cause, with the times serving as the apparent cause for the abstract obligation.

The Part of Time as the Cause of Obligation and Its Consequences
Refinement of the sabab of prayer as the part of time attached to performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the sabab for prayer is the specific part of time attached to performance, and determine obligation in cases of late entry or missed time.

Core Idea
The cause of prayer performance is the part of time to which the act attaches, shifting if delayed, and the last part becomes the cause if none was used.

In this section, al-Tahtawi refines the concept of sabab: it is not the entire time, but the particular part of time to which the performance connects. This has direct implications for latecomers – a madman who recovers at the last moment, a woman who becomes pure, a child who reaches puberty – they must pray even if only a takbir remains. The rule ensures that the obligation is tied to actual capacity and performance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the majority view on sabab
The passage states that the general body of mashayikh hold that the cause is the part of time to which performance is attached absolutely.
This is the operative principle for determining when obligation becomes concrete.
2
Trace the shifting of the cause
If performance attaches at the beginning, that beginning part is the cause. If delayed, the cause shifts to the later part. If no performance at all, the last part is determined for causality.
This allows for flexibility in timing within the prayer window.
3
Apply to the listed exceptions
The text gives examples: madman, unconscious, menstruating woman, child, apostate – each becomes obligated at the end of the time if they become responsible then.
Even if the time is short, the obligation is valid and the prayer is ada (timely).
4
Understand the qada ruling
If they had prayed at the beginning, the causality is attributed to the entire time to give the prayer perfect quality, and they are not required to make up. But if they missed it, qada is required in complete form.
This balances the attachment to a part with the completeness of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسببها الأصلي خطاب الله تعالى (الأزلي أي سبب وجوب أدائها. واعلم أن عندهم وجوباً ووجوب أداء ووجود أداء ، ولكل منها سبب حقيقي، وسبب مجازي فالوجوب سببه الحقيقي إيجاب الله تعالى في الأزل، لأن الموجب للأحكام هو الله تعالى وحده لكن لما كان إيجابه تعالى غيباً عنا لا تطلع عليه جعل لنا سبحانه وتعالى أسباباً مجازية ظاهرة تيسيراً علينا، وهي الأوقات بدليل تجدد الوجوب بتجددها، والسبب من كل وقت جزء يتصل به الأداء، فإن لم يتصل الأداء بجزء منه أصلاً، فالجزء الأخير متعين للسببية، ولو ناقصاً، الأداء ووجوب الحقيقي خطاب الله تعالى أي طلبه منا ذلك وسببه الظاهري هو اللفظ الدال على ذلك كلفظ أقيموا الصلاة، والفرق بين الوجوب، ووجوب الأداء أن الوجوب هو شغل الذمة، ووجوب الأداء طلب تفريغها، كما في غاية البيان، وسبب وجود الأداء الحقيقي خلق الله تعالى له وسببه الظاهري إستطاعة العبد وهي مع الفعل قوله : ( والأوقات أسباب ظاهراً تيسيراً) اعلم أن الأوقات لها جهات مختلفة بالحيثيات فمن حيث أن الصلاة لا تجوز قبلها وإنما تجب بها أسباب، ومن حيث أن الأداء لا بعدها لإشتراط الوقت له وإنما تكون قضاء شروط، ومن حيث أنها يجوز فيها أداء الفرض وغيره كالنفل ظروف بخلاف شهر رمضان فإنه معيار للصوم حتى لو نوى نفلاً واجباً آخر يقع عن الفرض قوله : (وأسبابها أوقاتها) عامة المشايخ على أن السبب هو الجزء الذي يتصل به الأداء مطلقاً فإن اتصل بأول الوقت، كان هو السبب، وإلا فينتقل إلى ما به يتصل وإن لم يتصل الأداء بجزء منه أصلاً فالجزء الأخير متعين للسببية، ولو ناقصاً حتى تجب على مجنون ومغمى عليه أفاقا وحائض، ونفساء طهرتا وصبي بلغ ومرتد أسلم في آخر الوقت ولو صليا في أوله وبعد خروجه تضاف السببية إلى جملة الوقت ليثبت الواجب بصفتة الكمال ولأنه الأصل حتى يلزمهم القضاء في كامل هو الصحيح كما في الدر
Its original cause is the address of Allah, the eternal, meaning the cause of the obligation of its performance. Know that according to them (the scholars) there is obligation (wujub), obligation of performance (wujub al-ada), and existence of performance (wujud al-ada). Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is an expansion probe into the legal cause (sabab) of prayer obligation. The author distinguishes between three levels: wujub (the liability in the dhimmah), wujub al-ada (the obligation to perform), and wujud al-ada (the actual performance).
