Key Terms
جزء (juz'): Part of the time; the specific portion of the prayer time to which the actual performance is attached.
الجزء الأخير (al-juz' al-akhir): The last part of the prayer time, which becomes the cause if no performance earlier.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a person does not perform any part of the prayer during the entire time?
A) The obligation is dropped because the time has passed.
B) The last part of the time becomes the cause, and the prayer must be made up as qada.
C) The person is not required to make it up because they missed the cause.
D) The person must pray it as soon as they remember, but it is considered ada.

Key Takeaway
The cause of prayer performance is the specific part of time to which the act attaches; if no performance, the last part becomes the cause, requiring qada.

Time of Fajr Prayer: Defining True Dawn
Defines the time of Fajr prayer and discusses the differing opinions on its start.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and explain why the spreading light (istitara) is the criterion for the start of Fajr prayer, distinguishing it from the first vertical spot (lam'a).

Core Idea
The true dawn is the spreading light across the horizon, not the first vertical column.

This lesson clarifies the precise moment when the Fajr prayer becomes obligatory. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the false dawn (a vertical column of light) and the true dawn (light spreading horizontally). Understanding this distinction is essential for correct prayer timing and also impacts the start of the daily fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Fajr prayer, whose time begins with the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq). The ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) to perform the prayer after this time enters.
The matn states 'Time of the morning prayer' indicating the moment obligation attaches.
2
Distinguish between the two appearances of dawn
Two phenomena are described: a vertical column of light (lam'a) and a horizontal spread (istitara). The passage reports two views on which marks the start.
Al-Halwani mentioned that some consider the first appearance (lam'a) sufficient, while others require spreading.
3
Analyze the preferred Hanafi view
Imam Muhammad is quoted: 'The spot is not considered with respect to prayer; only the spreading in the horizon is considered.' This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
The commentary notes that the 'spreading' view is clearer and broader, while the 'first spot' view is more precautionary but not preferred.
4
Note the evidence for Fajr being mentioned first
The passage also explains why Fajr is mentioned before other prayers in the hadith: the Prophet began with it when instructing the questioner in Medina, and because it was the first prayer prescribed on the night of Isra.
This is a secondary point but reinforces the importance of correct timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فلا حرج حتى يضيق) أي لا يأثم بالتأخير عن الجزء الأول والثاني، والثالث مثلاً إثم تارك الأداء في الوقت. قاله السيد، وتارك الصلاة غير مبال بها فاسق يحبس حتى يصلي، وقال المحبوبي : يضرب حتى يسيل منه الدم، ولا نيابة فيها أصلاً، ويحكم بإسلام فاعلها بالجماعة في الوقت إذا اقتدى فيها وتممها وكذا بالأذان في الوقت وبسجدة التلاوة وبزكاة السائمة لا لو صلى منفرداً أو إماماً، أو في غير الوقت، أو أفسد صلاته أو فعل غيرها من العبادات. قوله: (وقت صلاة الصبح) الصبح بياض يخلقه الله تعالى في الوقت المخصوص ابتداء وليس من تأثير الشمس، ولا من جنس نورها كما في التفسير الكبير قهستاني قوله من إبتداء طلوع الفجر) في الروايات ذكر الحلواني في شرحه للصوم أن العبرة لأول الطلوع وبه قال بعضهم فإذا بدت له لمعة أمسك عن المفطرات، وقال بعضهم: العبرة لاستطارته في الأفق، وهذا القول أبين وأوسع، والأول أحوط وروي عن محمد أنه قال : اللمعة غير معتبرة في حق الصوم، وحق الصلاة وإنما يعتبر الإنتشار في الأفق. قاله في الشرح، وقدم وقت الصبح لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بدأ به للسائل بالمدينة كما في البناية عن الغاية ولأنه أول الصوات إفتراضاً بإتفاق لأنه . الإسراء، ولم يقضه عليه الصلاة والسلام لتوقف وجوب الأداء على العلم بالكيفية. مجمع صبح ليلة
His statement: 'So there is no sin until it narrows' – meaning he does not sin by delaying from the first part, second, third, etc., like the sin of one who abandons performance within the time. Said by al-Sayyid. And one who abandons prayer carelessly is a sinner and is imprisoned until he prays. Al-Mahbubi said: he is beaten until blood flows, and there is no delegation for it at all. And the Islam of the one who performs it in congregation in the time is judged valid if he follows and completes it, similarly the adhan in time, the prostration of recitation, and the zakat of grazing animals – not if he prays alone or as imam, or outside the time, or corrupts his prayer, or does other acts of worship. His statement: 'Time of the morning prayer' – al-subh is whiteness that Allah creates at the specific time initially, and it is not from the effect of the sun nor from the genus of its light, as in the Tafsir al-Kabir al-Qahistani. His statement: 'From the beginning of the rising of the dawn' – in the narrations, al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary on fasting that the criterion is the first rising, and some said this; so if a spot appears to him, he refrains from breakers of fast. Some said: the criterion is its spreading in the horizon. This latter statement is clearer and broader, and the first is more precautionary. It is narrated from Muhammad that he said: the spot is not considered with respect to fasting or prayer; only the spreading in the horizon is considered. He said it in the commentary. And the time of morning was mentioned first because the Prophet, peace be upon him, began with it for the questioner in Medina, as in al-Binaya from al-Ghaya, and because it is the first of the prayers in terms of obligation by agreement, because it was (the night of) Isra, and he, peace be upon him, did not make it up because the obligation of performance depended on knowledge of the modality. 'Majma' subh laylah' (perhaps a marginal note).
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the time of Fajr prayer. It first clarifies the principle of expanded obligation: a person does not sin by delaying prayer within the time, but becomes sinful if they delay until the time narrows. It then addresses the definition of the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq). The matn states 'from the beginning of the rising of the dawn,' and the commentary explains that there are two views: the first appearance of light (a vertical column) and the spreading light across the horizon. Imam Muhammad is reported to hold that only the spreading (intishar) is considered for both prayer and fasting. This is the clearer and broader opinion, while the first (spot) is more precautionary for fasting. The passage also notes that Fajr is mentioned first because the Prophet began with it in the hadith of the questioner, and because it was the first prayer prescribed (on the night of Isra), and he did not make it up because the obligation depended on learning the method.

Key Terms
صبح (subh): The dawn; specifically the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) which is the white light spreading across the horizon.
استطار (istitara): Spreading; the horizontal spreading of light in the sky indicating true dawn.
لمعة (lam'a): A spot (of light); the first appearance of light vertically, which is not considered for prayer or fasting according to the preferred view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad's reported view in this passage, when does the time for Fajr prayer begin?
A) At the first appearance of a vertical column of light (al-mustatil)
B) When the light spreads across the horizon (al-mustatir)
C) At sunrise
D) When it is dark

Key Takeaway
The time for Fajr prayer begins with the spreading of the true dawn across the horizon, not with the initial vertical column of light.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation of Salah at the Beginning of Its Time (Wujub Musawwa')
Explains the ruling and its cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of wujub musawwa' and identify the sabab that triggers the obligation of salah.

Core Idea
Salah becomes obligatory at the first moment of its time, but performance is flexible until the time narrows.

This passage establishes that when the time for a prayer begins, the prayer becomes fard in a broad sense. You are accountable from the start, but may delay as long as you do not cause the time to become too short. The ruling is tied to the concept of sabab (cause), which Hanafi scholars define as the part of the time with which performance connects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the obligatory prayer (salah). The ruling is that it is fard 'ayn at the beginning of its time with a broad obligation (wujub musawwa').
2
Understand wujub musawwa'
Broad obligation means the prayer is due from the first part of the time, but you have flexibility to perform it at any point before the time becomes too narrow. Sin occurs only if you delay until the time is insufficient.
3
Define the sabab (cause)
The sabab is the part of the time with which performance connects. If you pray at the beginning, that part is the sabab. If you delay, the sabab shifts to the part you actually pray in. If no performance occurs, the last part is the sabab.
This ensures obligation even for those who become obliged at the end of the time (e.g., a child reaching puberty).
4
Note the consequence of delaying
Delaying without excuse until the time becomes narrow is sinful. The one who abandons prayer is a fasiq and may be imprisoned or beaten according to some Hanafi authorities.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that the obligation is tied to the entire time, so delaying until the end is not sinful as long as the prayer is performed within the time.

ترتيب الشهور القبطية فقال : إن رمـــت أقــدام الـزوال فــلــذبــنــا دوح يط زهــج بــاب لــمــصــرنـــا
He said: Command your children to pray at seven, and beat them for it at ten, and separate them in beds. And their causes are their times.) It is obligatory, meaning its performance is fard (at the beginning of the time, with a broad obligation, so there is no sin until it narrows for performance, and the address becomes decisive, and he sins by delaying beyond it. (And the times) for the obligatory prayers (are five), the first of which is the time of the Subh prayer.) According to his capacity is the reason for his saying: And beat them for ten with a hand. His saying: (And beat them for ten) it was objected that the evidence is more general than the claim, and it was answered that the beating is specified with other than a stick due to a presumption, which is that beating with a stick is only mentioned for a crime from a legally responsible person, and there is no crime from a minor, and some traditions indicate that, and this beating is obligatory as in Tanwir al-Absar. His saying: And separate them in beds. He said: in al-Hathr wa al-Ibaha from al-Durr. When a boy or girl reaches ten years, separation between them and between their brother, sister, mother, and father in bed is obligatory due to his saying, peace be upon him: Separate them in beds when they are children of ten. Perhaps the intent is separation such that one cover does not include them while being uncovered. As for sleeping adjacently with each covering his private parts with his own cover, even if the cover is one, there is no objection, and it is recorded. His saying: (And their causes are their times) The general mashayikh hold that the cause is the part with which performance is connected absolutely. If it connects with the beginning of the time, it is the cause; otherwise, it shifts to what it connects with. If performance is not connected with any part at all, then the last part is determined for causality, even if incomplete, so that it becomes obligatory upon an insane person and one unconscious who regain consciousness, a menstruating woman and a woman in post-natal bleeding who become pure, a child who reaches puberty, and an apostate who becomes Muslim at the end of the time. If they pray at its beginning and after its exit, causality is attributed to the whole time to establish the obligatory act with its complete quality, because it is the origin, so that qada is incumbent upon them in its complete form, which is correct as in al-Durr. His saying: (so there is no sin until it narrows) meaning he does not sin by delaying beyond the first, second, third part, etc., like the sin of the one who abandons performance in the time. Said by al-Sayyid. And the abandoner of prayer who is heedless of it is a fasiq who is imprisoned until he prays. And al-Mahbubi said: He is beaten until blood flows. And there is no substitution for it at all. And the one who performs it with the congregation in the time is judged to be a Muslim if he follows the imam and completes it, and likewise with the adhan in the time, and with the prostration of recitation, and with the zakat of grazing livestock, but not if he prays alone or as an imam, or outside the time, or spoils his prayer, or performs other acts of worship. His saying: (Time of Subh prayer) Subh is a whiteness that Allah creates at the specific time initially, not from the effect of the sun nor from the kind of its light, as in al-Tafsir al-Kabir. Qahastani. His saying: from the beginning of the appearance of fajr.) In the narrations, al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary on fasting that the criterion is the first appearance, and some said that. So if a patch appears to him, he refrains from infirmities. And some said: the criterion is its spreading in the horizon, and this opinion is clearer and broader, and the first is more precautionary. And it is reported from Muhammad that he said: The patch is not considered for fasting and for prayer; only the spreading in the horizon is considered. He said it in al-Sharh. And the time of Subh was mentioned first because the Prophet, peace be upon him, began with it for the questioner in Medina, as in al-Binaya from al-Ghaya, and because it is the first prayer obligated by consensus, because it is the Isra', and he did not make it up, peace be upon him, because the obligation of performance depends on knowing the modality. The time is an amount of time prescribed for something. (From) the beginning (of the appearance of fajr) due to Jibril's leading when fajr appeared (the true dawn), which appears horizontally spread, and the false dawn appears vertically then disappears. And the ummah is unanimous that its beginning is the true dawn and its end is just before sunrise) due to his saying, peace be upon him: The time of Fajr prayer is as long as the first horn of the sun has not risen. (And) the second is (the time) of Zuhr prayer from zawal. Conclusion: Some mentioned the explanation of the hours of the day: the first is sunrise, then early morning, then forenoon, then duha, then midday heat, then noon, then afternoon, then asr, then late asr, then evening, then isha, then sunset. And the hours of the night: the first is twilight, then darkness, then gloom, then deep night, then after midnight, then after dawn, then turn, then near dawn, then dawn, then subh. His saying: (the true) true because it is truthful about the morning and manifests it, as said in al-Sharh. His saying: (and the false...) It is called false because it gives light, then darkens, and the light goes and darkness follows, so it is as if it is false, as said in al-Sharh. His saying: (And the ummah is unanimous...) The consensus was contested by what we transmitted at the beginning earlier from Majma' al-Riwayat, and because it is said its end is until the archer sees the place of his arrow. So there is difference in its beginning and end, and it was answered that this difference is not considered due to its weakness. His saying: As long as the horn of the sun has not risen means the duration of the non-rise of the sun's horn. And the complete hadith: The time of Zuhr prayer is when the sun declines from the center of the sky as long as the time of Asr does not come. The time of Asr prayer is as long as the sun has not become yellow and its first horn has not set. The time of Maghrib is when the sun sets as long as the twilight has not vanished. And the time of Isha is until midnight. Narrated by Muslim. His saying: (Time of Zuhr from the decline of the sun from the center of the sky) And the way to know zawal is to plant a straight stick in level ground, and place a mark at the end of its shadow. As long as the shadow decreases from the mark, the sun has not declined. When it stops, that is the time of midday, and the zenith. Then a line is made at the tip of the shadow as a mark for that. So what is from that line to the base of the stick is called the shadow of zawal. If one does not find something to plant, he considers his own height, and the height of every person is seven feet or six and a half feet with his foot. The first is the common saying. And al-Hafiz al-Suyuti composed a sign of zawal for the Coptic months from Tuba to its end in one verse: He said: I composed it شرحه حروفه طزه جبا أبدو وح ١٠٨٦٤٢١ ۱۲۳ ۵۹۷. And these letters indicate the numbers by which zawal is known in the Coptic months. So ط is for Tuba, ز for Amshir, ه for Baramhat, ج for Baramouda, ب for Bishans, the two alifs for Baouna and Abib, ب for Misra, د for Tut, و for Baba, ح for Hatour, ي for Kiahk. And Shaykh al-Suhaymi composed it according to the order of the Coptic months: إن رمـت أقـدام الـزوال فـلـذبـنـا دوح يط زهـج بـاب لـمـصـرنـا
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses the times of the five obligatory prayers and the nature of their obligation. The commentary begins by quoting a hadith about commanding children to pray at seven and beating them at ten, then states the ruling that salah becomes fard at the beginning of its time with a broad obligation (wujub musawwa'). This means the obligation is established from the first moment, but one has the flexibility to delay performance as long as it does not cause the time to become too narrow. Sin only occurs if one delays until the time becomes insufficient for the prayer. The author then explains that the five times are: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. For Fajr, the time begins at the true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq), which spreads horizontally, and ends just before sunrise. The true dawn is distinguished from the false dawn which appears vertically and then disappears. There is a mention of a consensus (ijma') on the beginning of Fajr time, though some contested it. For Zuhr, the time begins when the sun declines (zawal) from the zenith. A method is given for determining zawal by inserting a stick in the ground and observing the shadow. The commentary includes various technical points, such as the attribution of the cause (sabab) of the obligation to the time, and the ruling that the one who abandons prayer is a fasiq and should be imprisoned or beaten. The passage also includes a poetic method for calculating zawal using Coptic months, attributed to al-Suyuti and al-Suhaymi.

Key Terms
وجوب موسع (wujub musawwa'): A broad obligation that becomes incumbent from the beginning of its time, allowing performance at any point before the time becomes too narrow.
سبب (sabab): The part of the time with which the performance of the act is connected; the cause that triggers the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, when does the obligation of a prayer become binding?
A) At the beginning of the time with a broad obligation.
B) At the middle of the time.
C) Only when the time becomes narrow.
D) At the end of the time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling establishes obligation early, giving flexibility but accountability.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Times of Fajr and Zuhr: True Dawn and Zawal
Details the times of Fajr and Zuhr prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the true dawn (subh sadiq), distinguish it from the false dawn, and explain how to determine zawal using the stick method and poetic mnemonics.

Core Idea
Fajr begins with the horizontal true dawn; Zuhr begins when the sun declines (zawal), measurable by shadow changes.

This passage details the specific times for Fajr and Zuhr prayers. For Fajr, the true dawn (subh sadiq) is a horizontal whiteness that spreads across the horizon, while the false dawn (subh kadhib) appears vertically and disappears. For Zuhr, the time begins when the sun passes its zenith (zawal), and the text provides a practical method using a stick to observe shadows, as well as a poetic mnemonic for calculating zawal in Coptic months.

Guided Path
1
Identify the start of Fajr
Fajr time begins with the true dawn (subh sadiq), which appears horizontally spreading across the horizon. This is distinguished from the false dawn.
The false dawn (subh kadhib) appears vertically like a wolf's tail and then disappears.
2
Note the end of Fajr
Fajr time ends just before sunrise, as per the hadith: 'The time of Fajr prayer is as long as the first horn of the sun has not risen.'
3
Understand the dispute on the start of Fajr
Some scholars consider the first appearance of light (lum`a) as the start, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that spreading (intishar) in the horizon is required. This is based on a report from Imam Muhammad.
The more precautionary view is to start at the first lum`a, but the clearer and broader view is spreading.
4
Determine the start of Zuhr
Zuhr time begins with zawal, which is the sun's decline from the zenith. The text describes a method: plant a straight stick and mark its shadow; when the shadow starts increasing after its minimum, that indicates zawal.
The length of the shadow at zawal is the minimum shadow length. After that, the prayer time begins.
5
Learn the poetic method for zawal
Al-Suyuti and al-Suhaymi composed poetic mnemonics using Coptic month letters to indicate the shadow length at zawal for each month.
This is a practical aid for those who need to determine zawal without a stick or when the sky is cloudy.

Source Text

ترتيب الشهور القبطية فقال : إن رمـــت أقــدام الـزوال فــلــذبــنــا دوح يط زهــج بــاب لــمــصــرنـــا
He said: Command your children to pray at seven, and beat them for it at ten, and separate them in beds. And their causes are their times.) It is obligatory, meaning its performance is fard (at the beginning of the time, with a broad obligation, so there is no sin until it narrows for performance, and the address becomes decisive, and he sins by delaying beyond it. (And the times) for the obligatory prayers (are five), the first of which is the time of the Subh prayer.) According to his capacity is the reason for his saying: And beat them for ten with a hand. His saying: (And beat them for ten) it was objected that the evidence is more general than the claim, and it was answered that the beating is specified with other than a stick due to a presumption, which is that beating with a stick is only mentioned for a crime from a legally responsible person, and there is no crime from a minor, and some traditions indicate that, and this beating is obligatory as in Tanwir al-Absar. His saying: And separate them in beds. He said: in al-Hathr wa al-Ibaha from al-Durr. When a boy or girl reaches ten years, separation between them and between their brother, sister, mother, and father in bed is obligatory due to his saying, peace be upon him: Separate them in beds when they are children of ten. Perhaps the intent is separation such that one cover does not include them while being uncovered. As for sleeping adjacently with each covering his private parts with his own cover, even if the cover is one, there is no objection, and it is recorded. His saying: (And their causes are their times) The general mashayikh hold that the cause is the part with which performance is connected absolutely. If it connects with the beginning of the time, it is the cause; otherwise, it shifts to what it connects with. If performance is not connected with any part at all, then the last part is determined for causality, even if incomplete, so that it becomes obligatory upon an insane person and one unconscious who regain consciousness, a menstruating woman and a woman in post-natal bleeding who become pure, a child who reaches puberty, and an apostate who becomes Muslim at the end of the time. If they pray at its beginning and after its exit, causality is attributed to the whole time to establish the obligatory act with its complete quality, because it is the origin, so that qada is incumbent upon them in its complete form, which is correct as in al-Durr. His saying: (so there is no sin until it narrows) meaning he does not sin by delaying beyond the first, second, third part, etc., like the sin of the one who abandons performance in the time. Said by al-Sayyid. And the abandoner of prayer who is heedless of it is a fasiq who is imprisoned until he prays. And al-Mahbubi said: He is beaten until blood flows. And there is no substitution for it at all. And the one who performs it with the congregation in the time is judged to be a Muslim if he follows the imam and completes it, and likewise with the adhan in the time, and with the prostration of recitation, and with the zakat of grazing livestock, but not if he prays alone or as an imam, or outside the time, or spoils his prayer, or performs other acts of worship. His saying: (Time of Subh prayer) Subh is a whiteness that Allah creates at the specific time initially, not from the effect of the sun nor from the kind of its light, as in al-Tafsir al-Kabir. Qahastani. His saying: from the beginning of the appearance of fajr.) In the narrations, al-Halwani mentioned in his commentary on fasting that the criterion is the first appearance, and some said that. So if a patch appears to him, he refrains from infirmities. And some said: the criterion is its spreading in the horizon, and this opinion is clearer and broader, and the first is more precautionary. And it is reported from Muhammad that he said: The patch is not considered for fasting and for prayer; only the spreading in the horizon is considered. He said it in al-Sharh. And the time of Subh was mentioned first because the Prophet, peace be upon him, began with it for the questioner in Medina, as in al-Binaya from al-Ghaya, and because it is the first prayer obligated by consensus, because it is the Isra', and he did not make it up, peace be upon him, because the obligation of performance depends on knowing the modality. The time is an amount of time prescribed for something. (From) the beginning (of the appearance of fajr) due to Jibril's leading when fajr appeared (the true dawn), which appears horizontally spread, and the false dawn appears vertically then disappears. And the ummah is unanimous that its beginning is the true dawn and its end is just before sunrise) due to his saying, peace be upon him: The time of Fajr prayer is as long as the first horn of the sun has not risen. (And) the second is (the time) of Zuhr prayer from zawal. Conclusion: Some mentioned the explanation of the hours of the day: the first is sunrise, then early morning, then forenoon, then duha, then midday heat, then noon, then afternoon, then asr, then late asr, then evening, then isha, then sunset. And the hours of the night: the first is twilight, then darkness, then gloom, then deep night, then after midnight, then after dawn, then turn, then near dawn, then dawn, then subh. His saying: (the true) true because it is truthful about the morning and manifests it, as said in al-Sharh. His saying: (and the false...) It is called false because it gives light, then darkens, and the light goes and darkness follows, so it is as if it is false, as said in al-Sharh. His saying: (And the ummah is unanimous...) The consensus was contested by what we transmitted at the beginning earlier from Majma' al-Riwayat, and because it is said its end is until the archer sees the place of his arrow. So there is difference in its beginning and end, and it was answered that this difference is not considered due to its weakness. His saying: As long as the horn of the sun has not risen means the duration of the non-rise of the sun's horn. And the complete hadith: The time of Zuhr prayer is when the sun declines from the center of the sky as long as the time of Asr does not come. The time of Asr prayer is as long as the sun has not become yellow and its first horn has not set. The time of Maghrib is when the sun sets as long as the twilight has not vanished. And the time of Isha is until midnight. Narrated by Muslim. His saying: (Time of Zuhr from the decline of the sun from the center of the sky) And the way to know zawal is to plant a straight stick in level ground, and place a mark at the end of its shadow. As long as the shadow decreases from the mark, the sun has not declined. When it stops, that is the time of midday, and the zenith. Then a line is made at the tip of the shadow as a mark for that. So what is from that line to the base of the stick is called the shadow of zawal. If one does not find something to plant, he considers his own height, and the height of every person is seven feet or six and a half feet with his foot. The first is the common saying. And al-Hafiz al-Suyuti composed a sign of zawal for the Coptic months from Tuba to its end in one verse: He said: I composed it شرحه حروفه طزه جبا أبدو وح ١٠٨٦٤٢١ ۱۲۳ ۵۹۷. And these letters indicate the numbers by which zawal is known in the Coptic months. So ط is for Tuba, ز for Amshir, ه for Baramhat, ج for Baramouda, ب for Bishans, the two alifs for Baouna and Abib, ب for Misra, د for Tut, و for Baba, ح for Hatour, ي for Kiahk. And Shaykh al-Suhaymi composed it according to the order of the Coptic months: إن رمـت أقـدام الـزوال فـلـذبـنـا دوح يط زهـج بـاب لـمـصـرنـا

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah discusses the times of the five obligatory prayers and the nature of their obligation. The commentary begins by quoting a hadith about commanding children to pray at seven and beating them at ten, then states the ruling that salah becomes fard at the beginning of its time with a broad obligation (wujub musawwa'). Sin only occurs if one delays until the time becomes insufficient for the prayer. The author then explains that the five times are: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. Key Terms
الصبح الصادق (al-subh al-sadiq): The true dawn that appears horizontally spreading across the horizon, marking the beginning of Fajr time.
الزوال (al-zawal): The time when the sun passes its zenith and begins to decline; marks the start of Zuhr prayer.

Checkpoint
What marks the beginning of Fajr time according to the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) The appearance of a vertical beam of light.
B) The horizontal spread of whiteness across the horizon.
C) The first call to prayer in the mosque.
D) The appearance of the sun's disk.

Key Takeaway
Correctly identifying the true dawn and zawal is essential for performing Fajr and Zuhr prayers in their valid times.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Time of Zuhr Prayer: Determining Zawal and Ikhtilaf on Its End
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zuhr time with practical method for zawal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the stick method to determine zawal and state the two Hanafi narrations on when Zuhr time ends, identifying which view is the mufta bihi and why.

Core Idea
Zuhr time ends at mithlayn (shadow twice object) excluding fay' al-zawal, according to the majority Hanafi view.

This lesson presents the classical method to find the time of zawal (sun's zenith) using a simple stick, and then delves into an important intra-Hanafi dispute: when exactly does the time of Zuhr end? The text presents two narrations from Imam Muhammad and al-Hasan, along with the evidence and reasoning that led the majority of Hanafi scholars to adopt the view that Zuhr extends until the shadow reaches twice the height of the object (mithlayn), excluding the initial shadow after zawal (fay' al-zawal).

Guided Path
1
Determine zawal using the stick method
Understand how to plant a stick on level ground, mark its shadow, and observe when the shadow stops decreasing and begins increasing. The initial increase is fay' al-zawal and is excluded from subsequent measurements.
Fay' al-zawal is not counted in the calculation for Zuhr's end.
2
Identify the two narrations on Zuhr's end
First narration (Imam Muhammad, preferred by majority): Zuhr ends 'shortly before' the shadow becomes mithl (i.e., at mithlayn). Second narration (al-Hasan): Zuhr ends when shadow becomes mithl (first mithl).
Both narrations exclude fay' al-zawal.
3
Analyze the conflicting evidence
The hadith 'Cool the Zuhr' suggests delaying Zuhr to mithl, while the hadith of Jibril shows Asr beginning at the first mithl after Zuhr. This creates a conflict on when Zuhr actually ends.
The conflict led to different interpretations.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference) reasoning
The majority argued that since the two hadiths conflict, one must be cautious and not end Zuhr time with doubt. They extended Zuhr to mithlayn to be safe, ensuring the prayer is within its time.
Caution (ihtiyat) is a key principle here.
5
Recognize the practical implication
If someone prays Zuhr after the shadow reaches mithl but before mithlayn, according to the second narration it is valid, but according to the majority (mufta bihi) it is out of time and must be repeated. This difference affects daily practice.
The mufta bihi is the majority view (mithlayn).

عن الإمام. قوله: فبينهما وقت مهمل) اختاره الكرخي وقال شيخ الإسلام إنه الاحتياط كما في السراج.
He said: (The time of Zuhr from the declining of the sun from the middle of the sky). And the method to know zawal: one should plant a straight stick in level ground, and make a mark at the end of its shadow. As long as the shadow decreases from the mark, the sun has not declined; when it stops, that is the time of istiwa' (sun at zenith) and the height of midday. Then a line is made at the top of the shadow as a mark for that, and whatever is from that line to the base of the stick is called the shadow of zawal. If one cannot plant a stick, he uses his own height; every person's height is seven feet, or six and a half feet by his foot; the first is the common saying. Al-Hafiz al-Suyuti composed a verse indicating the shadows of zawal for the Coptic months from Tubah to its end: 'Nazamtuha al-mashruh hurufuhu tazh jab abduh' with numbers 1086421, 123597. These letters indicate the numbers by which zawal is known in the Coptic months: 'ta' for Tubah, 'za' for Amshir, 'ha' for Barmahat, 'jim' for Barmoudah, 'ba' for Bashans, two 'alifs' for Ba'unah and Abib, 'ba' for Misra, 'dal' for Tut, 'waw' for Babah, 'ha' for Hatour, 'ya' for Kiyahk. Al-Shaykh al-Suhaymi composed another verse ordering the Coptic months: 'In ramta aqdam al-zawal fal dhab nitwah...'. Then he said: If one wants to know the entry of Asr time, he adds his height, which is seven feet, to what was taken from the months. When the shadow reaches the sum of both, its time has entered. The person standing must be on level ground, with uncovered head, not leaning. This is from Shubramulisi, abridged. It is narrated from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, that the limit of zawal is that one faces the qiblah; as long as the sun is on his left eyebrow, the sun has not declined; if it goes to his right eyebrow, it has declined. He said: (In a narration: 'until shortly before it becomes' i.e., until the fine moment before the mentioned becoming, and this is Muhammad's narration from the Imam. He said: (The conflict of reports). Its explanation: the hadith agreed upon: 'Cool the Zuhr prayer, for the intensity of heat is from the heat of Hell' necessitates delaying Zuhr to the time of mithl (shadow equal to object) because the most intense heat in their lands is at the time of mithl. The hadith of Jibril's imamate on the first day necessitates the end of Zuhr time at the exit of mithl, because he led Asr at the beginning of the second mithl. So there is a conflict between them, so Zuhr time does not end due to doubt, and its completion is in the longer works. He said: (And it is the correct one) The majority of the madhhab authenticated it, and the saying of al-Tahawi 'and we take by their saying' indicates it is the madhhab. In al-Burhan, their saying is the most apparent; so the tarjih differs. He said: (And the second narration) is the narration of al-Hasan from him. He said: (Except the shadow of istiwa') which is what was referred to earlier as fay' al-zawal. He said: (And al-fay') it is called fay' because it returns from the west to the east, i.e., goes back, from His statement: 'until they return to the command of Allah' [49:9] i.e., return. Sometimes what is after zawal is also called 'zill', but what is before zawal is never called 'fay''. So in al-Siraj. He said: (And it is the saying of the sahibayn) i.e., Zufar and the three imams. He said: ('Asr in it' – the 'it' is deleted because the imamate was only at the beginning of the second mithl. He said: (The release of the dhimmah) is the cause for the caution, and his saying 'since offering prayer before its time' is a cause for the causality. He said: (Since offering prayer before its time) and here it is Asr. He said: (How, while the time remains) i.e., the time of Asr after the second mithl. He said: (And in Asad's narration) i.e., Ibn Amr, and al-Hasan also narrated from the Imam. He said: (Then between them is a wasted time) al-Karkhi chose this, and Shaykh al-Islam said it is the precaution, as in al-Siraj.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: how to determine the time of zawal (declination of the sun), and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the end of Zuhr time. The method: plant a stick on level ground, mark the shadow's end; when it stops decreasing and starts increasing, that is zawal; the initial increase is the fay' (shadow after zawal). The commentary includes a practical method using Coptic months (a lunar calendar system) and a person's height for approximation. The key dispute: The first narration (from Imam Muhammad) states Zuhr time ends 'shortly before' the shadow becomes like the object (excluding the fay' al-zawal). The second narration (from al-Hasan) says it ends when the shadow becomes twice the object. The text discusses the conflict between the hadith of 'cooling the Zuhr' (which suggests delaying to mithl) and the hadith of Jibril (which indicates Asr at the first mithl after Zuhr). The majority (including Abu Hanifa) authenticated the first narration (until mithlayn), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (sahibayn) and others preferred the second (until mithl). The commentator notes the tarjih is disputed. Additionally, a third view (Asad's narration) posits a 'wasted time' between the end of Zuhr and the start of Asr. The text emphasizes caution and that the reliable (mufta bihi) for fatwa is the majority view.

Key Terms
الزوال (al-zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith (midday), indicated by the shadow stopping its decrease and beginning to increase.
الفيء (al-fay'): The shadow after zawal; specifically the increase from the shadow at zawal (fay' al-zawal). Excluded from calculations for Zuhr end.
المثل (al-mithl): The shadow becoming equal in length to the object's height (including or excluding fay' al-zawal depending on context).
الفيء الزوال (fay' al-zawal): The initial shadow that appears right after zawal, which is not counted in the calculation for the end of Zuhr time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (mufta bihi), when does Zuhr time end?
A) When the shadow is equal to the object's height (mithl) excluding fay' al-zawal
B) When the shadow is twice the object's height (mithlayn) excluding fay' al-zawal
C) When the sun sets
D) When the shadow is one and a half times the object

Key Takeaway
Zuhr time begins at zawal and, according to the majority Hanafi view, ends when the shadow reaches twice the object's height (mithlayn) excluding the initial shadow after zawal (fay' al-zawal).

Start and End Time of Asr Prayer: Ruling and Proof
Clarifies start and end of Asr time with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the start and end times of Asr prayer, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the start time, and identify the end time based on the hadith.

Core Idea
Asr time begins when a shadow exceeds the object's length; the end is sunset, proven by the hadith about catching a rak'ah before sunset.

The time of Asr prayer is a matter of precision and legal reasoning. The Hanafi school determines its start based on shadow length, with a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. The end time is clearly set by the Prophet's hadith as sunset. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the relied-upon position within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Asr is a fard ayn prayer; its time is a condition for validity. The passage does not discuss other conditions or pillars.
2
State the start time according to the relied-upon Hanafi view
The matn begins by noting the difference: Abu Hanifa says Asr starts when the shadow of an object is twice its height; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say when it is once. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's 'twice' view, as indicated by 'ala al-mashhur'.
3
Identify the proof for the end time
The end of Asr time is sunset (ghurub al-shams). The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' This hadith is sahih and establishes the time window until sunset.
The commentator clarifies that sunset means the complete disappearance of the sun's disk from the apparent horizon, considering ease of obligation.
4
Understand the exception of waqt al-ikhtiyar
Hasan ibn Ziyad's statement that Asr exits when the sun becomes yellow is interpreted as the end of the 'time of choice' (ikhtiyar), not the permissible time. The time of necessity extends until actual sunset.
5
Note the special case of the sun returning
If the sun sets and then reappears due to atmospheric conditions, the time for Asr returns as well, based on the hadith of Ali (RA) where the sun was returned for him to pray Asr. This indicates apparent sunset governs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثله لا يدخل وقت العصر حتى يصير ظل كل شيء مثليه فبينهما وقت مهمل فالإحتياط أن يصلي الظهر قبل أن يصير الظل مثله والعصر بعد مثليه ليكون مؤدياً بالإتفاق كذا في المبسوط (و) أول (وقت العصر من ابتداء الزيادة على المثل أو المثلين) لما قدمناه من الخلاف إلى غروب الشمس على المشهور لقوله له من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر، وقال الحسن بن زياد إذا اصفرت الشمس خرج وقت العصر، وحمل على وقت الإختيار.
ثم قال المحشي: قوله: (وأول وقت العصر الخ) سمي عصراً لأنه أحد طرفي النهار، والعرب تسمي كل طرف من النهار عصراً، فالغداة والعشي عصران قوله: إلى غروب الشمس) أي جرمها بالكلية عن الأفق الحسي أي الظاهري لا الحقيقي لأن في الإطلاع عليه عسراً كما في مجمع الأنهر، والتكليف بحسب الوسع حتى قال في الخلاصة: لا يفطر من على المنارة بالاسكندرية، وقد رأى الشمس ويفطر من بالاسكندرية وقد غابت عنه. اهـ. وهذا إذا ظهر الغروب وإلا فإلى وقت إقبال الظلمة من المشرق كما في التحفة ولو غربت الشمس، ثم عادت هل يعود الوقت الظاهر: نعم كما في الدر لما روي أنه نام في حجر علي رضي الله عنه حتى غربت الشمس فلما استيقظ ذكر له أنه فاتته العصر، فقال: اللهم إنه كان في طاعتك وطاعة رسولك فارددها عليه فردت حتى صلى العصر أخرجه الطبراني بسند حسن، وصححه الطحاوي، والقاضي عياض، وأخطأ من جعله موضوعاً كابن الجوزي كما في النهر. قوله: (وحمل) أي قوله بخروج وقت العصر. قوله على وقت الإختيار أي الوقت الذي يخير المكلف في ا فيه من غير كراهة.
Similarly, the time of Asr does not enter until the shadow of everything becomes twice its length, so between them there is an idle time, so the precaution is to pray Dhuhr before the shadow becomes like it and Asr after twice it to be performing (the prayer) by agreement, as in al-Mabsut. (And) the beginning (of the time of Asr is from the start of the increase over the like or the two likes) due to the difference we mentioned previously, until sunset according to the well-known, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' And al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: When the sun becomes yellow, the time of Asr exits. And it is interpreted as the time of choice.
Then the commentator said: His statement: (And the beginning of the time of Asr etc.) It is called Asr because it is one of the two ends of the day, and the Arabs call each end of the day Asr, so the morning and the afternoon are two Asrs. His statement: (until sunset) i.e., its disk completely from the apparent horizon, not the real, because observing it is difficult, as in Majma' al-Anhur, and obligation is according to capacity, until it is said in al-Khulasa: The one on the minaret in Alexandria does not break his fast while he sees the sun, and the one in Alexandria breaks his fast while the sun has set for him. This is if the sunset appears, otherwise until the time of darkness approaching from the east, as in al-Tuhfah. And if the sun sets, then returns, does the apparent time return? Yes, as in al-Durr, due to what was narrated that he slept in the lap of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) until the sun set, and when he woke up, he was told that he had missed Asr, so he said: 'O Allah, he was in Your obedience and the obedience of Your Messenger, so return it to him,' and it was returned until he prayed Asr. Al-Tabarani narrated it with a good chain, and al-Tahawi and Qadi Iyad declared it authentic, and Ibn al-Jawzi was wrong in declaring it fabricated, as in al-Nahr. His statement: (and interpreted) i.e., his statement of the exit of Asr time. His statement: (as the time of choice) i.e., the time in which the responsible person is given a choice to pray without dislike.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the time of Asr prayer. The matn states that Asr time begins when the shadow of an object exceeds twice its length, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, or once according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The end time is sunset, based on the hadith: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr.' The commentator explains that sunset means the complete disappearance of the sun's disk from the apparent horizon, and obligation is based on what is visible. He cites the ruling that a person on a high minaret who sees the sun after it has set for those on the ground does not break his fast until his own sunset. The hadith of the sun returning for Ali (RA) is adduced to show that if the sun sets and then returns, the time for Asr returns as well. The commentator also clarifies that the statement of Hasan ibn Ziyad about yellowing refers to the time of choice (ikhtiyar), not the end of the permissible time.

Key Terms
عصر ('Asr): The afternoon prayer, one of the two ends of the day.
غروب الشمس (ghurub al-shams): Complete disappearance of the sun's disk from the apparent horizon.
وقت الإختيار (waqt al-ikhtiyar): Time in which prayer is performed without dislike (karahah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, when does Asr time end?
A) When the sun becomes yellow.
B) When the shadow is twice the object's height.
C) At sunset, meaning the complete disappearance of the sun's disk from the apparent horizon.
D) When the shadow is equal to the object's height.

Key Takeaway
Asr time begins at shadow twice (Abu Hanifa) and ends at apparent sunset; the hadith of catching a rak'ah before sunset is the proof for the end time.

Definition of Shafaq: Red or White Twilight?
Resolves the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether shafaq is red or white twilight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi definition of shafaq in the Hanafi school and explain why Imam Abu Hanifa's view is preferred over that of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi: shafaq is the red twilight; the white twilight is atmospheric whiteness, not shafaq.

Determining the end of Maghrib time hinges on the correct definition of shafaq (twilight). This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, over whether shafaq is the red or white twilight after sunset. The relied-upon position is Imam Abu Hanifa's view that shafaq is the red twilight, as supported by evidence and preferred by later Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the mufta bihi definition of shafaq according to the Hanafi school. The passage explicitly states that the red twilight is the mufta bihi, based on a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa.
This position determines the end of Maghrib time.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that shafaq is the white twilight that appears after the redness. This view is also attributed to many companions and some linguists.
Their view would delay the start of Isha.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing view relies on reports from Abu Bakr, Aisha, Anas, Mu'adh, Abu Hurayra, and others, as well as the opinion of linguists like al-Mubarrad and Tha'lab.
These reports suggest the white twilight is the true shafaq.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The commentary argues that the observed whiteness is atmospheric (beyond the shafaq), not the shafaq itself. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is clear, and as the imam of the madhhab, his view must be followed. The claim that he retracted is weak.
The tarjih in al-Bahr favours Imam Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If shafaq is red, Maghrib time ends earlier and Isha begins sooner. If white, Maghrib extends longer. The mufta bihi (red) leads to earlier Maghrib expiry.
This affects daily prayer timing.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) أول وقت (المغرب منه أي غروب الشمس (إلى) قبيل غروب الشفق الأحمر على المفتى (به) وهو رواية عن الإمام وعليها الفتوى وبها قالا الأداء.
ثم قال المحشي: قوله: (إلى غروب الشفق الأحمر) وقيل هو البياض الذي بعد الحمرة، وهو قول الصديق والصديقة وأنس ومعاذ وأبي هريرة، ورواية عن ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهم أجمعين، وبه قال عمر بن عبد العزيز والأوزاعي وداود الظاهري وغيرهم، واختاره من أهل اللغة المبرد، وثعلب، وصحح كل من القولين وأفتى به ورجح في البحر قول الإمام قال: ولا يعدل عنه إلى قولهما، ولو بموجب من ضعف أو ضرورة تعامل لأنه صاحب المذهب فيجب إتباعه، والعمل بمذهبه حيث كان دليله واضحاً ومذهبه ثابتاً ولا يلتفت إلى جعل بعض المشايخ الفتوى على قولهما اهـ وقوى الكمال قول الإمام أيضاً بما حاصله أن الشفق يطلق على البياض، والحمرة وأقرب الأمر أنه إذا تردد في أن الحمرة أو البياض، لا ينقضي الوقت بالشك، ولا صحة لصلاة قبل وقتها فالاحتياط في التأخير، وقال العلامة الزيلعي، وما روي عن الخليل أنه قال: راعيت البياض بمكة كرمها الله ليلة فما ذهب إلا بعد نصف الليل محمول على بياض الجوّ، وذلك يغيب آخر الليل وأما بياض الشفق وهو رقيق الحمرة، فلا يتأخر عنها إلا قليلاً قدر ما يتأخر طلوع الحمرة عن البياض في الفجر. قوله: (وهو مروي عن أكابر الصحابة) قد علمت أن مذهب الإمام مروي عن أكبر الصحابة أجمعين نساء ورجالاً. قوله: (وعليه اطباق أهل اللسان) قد علمت ما اختاره المبرد وثعلب وهما من أكبر أهله. قوله: (ونقل رجوع الإمام إليه) هذه الصيغة للضعف فلا جزم بها.
(And) the first time (of Maghrib is from it, i.e., sunset, to just before the disappearance of the red twilight according to the mufta bihi, and it is a narration from Imam and upon it is the fatwa, and both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is the time of performance.
Then the commentator said: His statement: (to the disappearance of the red twilight) and it is said it is the whiteness after the redness, and it is the saying of al-Siddiq (Abu Bakr), al-Siddiqa (Aisha), Anas, Mu'adh, and Abu Hurayra, and a narration from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them all), and with it said Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, al-Awza'i, Dawud al-Zahiri, and others, and chosen from the linguists by al-Mubarrad and Tha'lab, and each of the two sayings was declared authentic and fatwa was given with it, and in al-Bahr he preferred the saying of Imam (Abu Hanifa). He said: 'One should not deviate from it to their saying, even if there is a cause of weakness or necessity, because he is the imam of the madhhab, so it is obligatory to follow him and act on his madhhab where his evidence is clear and his madhhab is established, and no attention is paid to some shaykhs giving fatwa on their saying.' Al-Kamal also strengthened the saying of Imam with the summary that shafaq is applied to both whiteness and redness, and the closest matter is that if one is uncertain whether it is the redness or whiteness, the time does not pass with doubt, and no prayer before its time is valid, so precaution is to delay. Al-Zayla'i said: What is narrated from al-Khalil that he said: I observed the whiteness in Mecca, may Allah honor it, and it did not disappear until after half the night, is interpreted as the whiteness of the atmosphere, which disappears at the end of the night. But the whiteness of the shafaq, which is a thin redness, does not delay from it except a little, the amount that the appearance of redness is delayed from whiteness at dawn. His statement: (and it is narrated from the great companions) you have known that the madhhab of Imam is narrated from the greatest of the companions, men and women. His statement: (and upon it is the consensus of the people of language) you have known what al-Mubarrad and Tha'lab chose, and they are among the greatest of them. His statement: (and the return of Imam to it is narrated) this wording is weak, so it should not be asserted.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute over the definition of shafaq (twilight) which determines the end of Maghrib time and the beginning of Isha time. The matn states the mufta bihi is the red twilight, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. The hashiya explains that there is a view that shafaq is the whiteness after the redness, attributed to many companions and linguists. However, the relied-upon position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as preferred in al-Bahr. The commentator argues that Imam's view is supported by clear evidence and must be followed. He also cites al-Kamal's strengthening: since the term shafaq can apply to both, if uncertain, one should delay until certainty. The report of al-Khalil about whiteness in Mecca is interpreted as atmospheric whiteness, not shafaq. The claim that Imam later retracted is weak and not confirmed.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; disputed whether red or white.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon position for giving fatwa.
أهل اللسان (ahl al-lisan): The experts in the Arabic language (linguists).
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of giving preference to one evidence or opinion over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what marks the end of Maghrib time?
A) Disappearance of the red twilight.
B) Disappearance of the white twilight.
C) When the sun sets.
D) When the sky becomes completely dark.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that shafaq is the red twilight; Maghrib time ends with its disappearance, and Isha begins immediately after.

Salah — Prayer

Time for Isha and Witr and Ruling for Abnormal Regions
Ruling on prayer times and exceptional cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for Isha and Witr, explain why Witr must follow Isha, and apply the ruling for places where the time is not evident.

Core Idea
Isha and Witr share the same time window; Witr must be after Isha; if time is absent, the prayer is not obligatory.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the prayer times for Isha and Witr, grounding them in the hadith of Jibril and the explicit command to pray Witr between Isha and dawn. It also addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: whether Witr is wajib (Imam Abu Hanifa) or sunnah (the two Sahibayn), and the practical consequences of that difference. Finally, it tackles the extraordinary case of regions like Bulghar where the sun may not set for extended periods, ruling that if the time for Isha and Witr cannot be determined, the prayers are not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined time for Isha and Witr
Locate where the matn states that Isha time begins after the disappearance of twilight (shafaq) and ends at dawn. Witr shares this time window. Note the hadith cited: 'Pray Witr between the last Isha and the rise of dawn.'
The hadith of Jibril also supports this, as he led Isha at one-third of the night.
2
Understand the order requirement (tartib)
The text explicitly forbids praying Witr before Isha. This is based on the hadith that Witr is to be prayed 'between' Isha and dawn, implying a sequence, and on the principle that a wajib (Witr) must follow a fard (Isha) when their times coincide.
This order is binding according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of Witr
Imam Abu Hanifa considers Witr a wajib (practical fard). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a sunnah mu'akkadah. The text uses the phrase 'wajib of Witr' indicating the Imam's view is the mufta bihi.
The practical consequence: if one prays Witr before Isha forgetfully, it is valid according to Imam but not according to the Sahibayn.
4
Examine the special case of Bulghar
The passage discusses places like Bulghar (modern-day Bulgaria/region in the far north) where during summer the sun sets for only about an hour, making it impossible to distinguish Isha time. The ruling: 'Whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory upon him.'
The cause (sabab) for obligation is the presence of a valid time period; without it, obligation falls away.
5
Apply the analogy from the Dajjal hadith
The commentator mentions the hadith of the Dajjal where a day is like a year, and the Prophet instructed to estimate prayer times. By analogy, in places with continuous daylight, one should estimate the times based on a standard 24-hour cycle, but the obligation remains if time can be approximated.
The text distinguishes: in Bulghar, time is entirely absent; in the Dajjal scenario, time exists but is extended.

Source Text

ثم قال المحشي: قوله: (وحديث إمامة جبريل الخ) فإنه أم به الليلة الثانية في العشاء ثلث الليل الأول وهذا جواب عما أورده على قول المصنف، والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح وقوله، وقال: إن الله الخ دليل لوقت الوتر. قوله: (لهذا الحديث) فإن قوله: فصلوها ما بين العشاء الأخيرة إلى طلوع الفجر صريح في تعيين وقت صلاته. قوله: (وواجب الوتر المراد به الفرض العملي فإنه فرض عملي عند الإمام كما في البحر، وقالا أول وقته بعد العشاء بناء على أنه سنة مؤكدة عندهما فصار كركعتي العشاء والثمرة تظهر فيما لو صلى الوتر ناسياً للعشاء، أو صلاهما فظهر فساد العشاء دون الوتر أجزأه عند الإمام لسقوط الترتيب بمثل هذا العذر لا عندهما لأنه تبع لها فلا يصح قبلها وفيما لو صلى الفجر قبل الوتر عمداً أو كان صاحب ترتيب أعاده بعد صلاة الوتر عنده لا عندهما لأنه لا ترتيب بين الفرائض والسنن قاله السيد قوله (كبلغار) قال في القاموس: بلغر كقرطق يعني بضم فسكون، والعامة تقول بلغار مدينة الصقالبة ضاربة في الشمال شديدة البرد اهـ. قوله: (في أقصر ليالي السنة) وهو أربعون ليلة في أول الصيف عند حلول الشمس رأس السرطان فإن الشمس تمكث عندهم على وجه الأرض ثلاثاً وعشرين ساعة، وتغرب ساعة واحدة، على حسب عرض البلد قوله: ( وليس مثل اليوم الخ) روى مسلم عن النواس بن سمعان. قال: ذكر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الدجال ولبثه في الأرض أربعين يوماً يوم: كسنة، ويوم كشهر ويوم كجمعة وسائر أيامه كأيامكم قلنا فذلك اليوم الذي كسنة يكفينا فيه صلاة يوم؟ قال: لا قدروا له قدره اهـ. قال الأسنوي: ويقاس عليه اليومان التاليان واستظهر الكمال وجوب القضاء استدلالاً بحديث الدجال، وتبعه ابن الشحنة فصححه في ألغازه وذكر في المنح أنه المذهب، ولا ينوي القضاء لفقد وقت الأداء، وفرق في النهر بأن الوقت موجود حقيقة في يوم الدجال، والمفقود
And the beginning of the time of Isha prayer and Witr is from it, i.e., from the disappearance of the twilight according to the difference that preceded, to just before the rise of the true dawn, due to the consensus of the Salaf and the hadith of the imamate of Jibril does not negate what is beyond the time of his imamate, and Allah said: 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer, which is Witr, so pray it between the last Isha and the rise of dawn.' (And do not advance) Witr prayer before (Isha prayer) due to this hadith and the necessary order between the fard of Isha and the wajib of Witr according to Imam. (And whoever does not find their time) i.e., Isha and Witr (they are not obligatory upon him) such as if he is in a country like Bulghar, or in the far east where dawn rises before the twilight disappears in the shortest nights of the year, due to the absence of the cause, which is time.
Then the commentator said: His statement: (and the hadith of the imamate of Jibril etc.) He led him in prayer on the second night at Isha at one third of the first part of the night, and this is a response to what was raised against the author's statement that Isha and Witr are from that (disappearance of twilight) until dawn. His statement: 'And Allah said...' is evidence for the time of Witr. His statement: (due to this hadith) Indeed his saying: 'Pray it between the last Isha and the rise of dawn' is explicit in specifying its prayer time. His statement: (and wajib of Witr) what is meant is the practical fard, for it is a practical fard according to Imam as in al-Bahr. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said its beginning time is after Isha based on it being mu'akkadah sunnah with them, so it became like the two rak'ahs of Isha. The fruit (practical consequence) appears in the case where one prays Witr forgetting Isha, or prays both and then Isha is found invalid but Witr is not, it suffices him according to Imam due to the order being dropped with such an excuse, but not according to them because it is a follower of Isha so it is not valid before it. Also, if one prays Fajr before Witr intentionally or if he is a person of order, he repeats it after praying Witr according to Imam, not according to them because there is no order between obligatory prayers and sunnah prayers, as said by al-Sayyid. His statement: (like Bulghar) al-Qamus says: Bulghar like qurtuq, i.e., with dammah and sukun, and the common people say Bulghar, a city of the Saqaliba, extending into the north, extremely cold. His statement: (in the shortest nights of the year) which is forty nights at the beginning of summer when the sun is at the Tropic of Cancer, for the sun remains with them on the face of the earth for twenty-three hours and sets for one hour, according to the latitude of the country. His statement: (and it is not like the day etc.) Muslim narrated from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an: He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) mentioned the Dajjal and his stay on earth for forty days: a day like a year, a day like a month, a day like a week, and the rest of his days like your days. We said: 'That day which is like a year, is one day's prayer sufficient for us?' He said: 'No, estimate for it its measure.' Al-Asnawi said: The two following days are analogous to it, and al-Kamal expressed the opinion of obligation of qada' based on the hadith of the Dajjal, and Ibn al-Shihnah followed him and declared it correct in his puzzles, and it is mentioned in al-Minh that it is the madhhab. And he does not intend qada' because the time for performance is lost. And in al-Nahr, he distinguished that time actually exists in the day of the Dajjal, and what is lost...
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage covers the time for Isha and Witr prayers, their relationship, and special circumstances where time is abnormal. The matn states that Isha time begins after the disappearance of the twilight (shafaq) according to the earlier difference, and ends at dawn. Witr time is the same, and Witr cannot be prayed before Isha due to the order between the fard of Isha and the wajib of Witr according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If one is in a place like Bulghar in the far north where the sun does not set properly for part of the year, and there is no distinct time for Isha and Witr, they are not obligatory because the cause (time) is missing. The commentator elaborates: The hadith of Jibril shows that Isha time extends to dawn, and the hadith 'Pray Witr between Isha and dawn' specifies its time. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr's obligation: Imam considers it a practical fard (wajib), while the two companions consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. The practical consequence is that if one prays Witr before Isha due to forgetfulness, it is valid for Imam but not for them. The commentator also discusses the analogy from the hadith of the Dajjal for places with very long days, concluding that one must estimate prayer times.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer prayed after Isha; wajib according to Imam, sunnah according to Sahibayn.
بلغار (bulghar): A city in the far north where the day is very long in summer, causing prayer times to be ambiguous.
الترتيب (al-tartib): The order between obligatory prayers; here specifically between Isha (fard) and Witr (wajib).

Key Takeaway
Isha and Witr share the same time window; Witr must follow Isha; if the time is not present, the prayers are not obligatory.

Time of Isha and Witr: The Shafaq Debate and Extreme Latitudes
Explaining the beginning of Isha time, the shafaq debate, and the ruling for places like Bulghar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the beginning of Isha time, explain the internal dispute over shafaq, and apply the rule for places where the twilight is absent.

Core Idea
Isha begins when the red twilight disappears; if the twilight never disappears, the obligation falls away.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a classic Hanafi problem: when exactly does Isha begin? The answer hinges on defining 'shafaq' (twilight). The text also wrestles with extreme northern latitudes like Bulghar, where the sun barely sets. Understanding how the school handles this reveals important principles about the relationship between cause (sabab) and legal obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses two prayers: Isha (fard) and Witr (wajib). Their times are defined by the disappearance of shafaq until dawn.
Isha is fard; Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Locate the dalil for the definition of shafaq
The text cites the statement of Ibn Umar defining shafaq as redness, and the hadith of Jibril establishing prayer times. It also invokes consensus of the Salaf and philologists.
The hadith of Jibril does not negate times beyond his imamate.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Abu Hanifa holds shafaq is redness; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is whiteness. The text notes a weak narration of Abu Hanifa's return to the whiteness view.
Mufta bihi is the redness view.
4
Apply the rule for places with absent twilight
In places like Bulghar where the twilight never disappears (e.g., summer in far north), the obligation of Isha and Witr is lifted because the cause (time) is absent.
This applies only to Isha and Witr, not to other prayers.
5
Distinguish from the Dajjal day
On the Dajjal day, times are estimated because the day is supernaturally long. That is a special command, not analogized to normal extreme latitudes.
The Dajjal day has a sign but it is extended; here the sign is missing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
لقول ابن عمر : الشفق الحمرة وهو مروي عن أكابر الصحابة وعليه أطباق أهل اللسان، ونقل رجوع الإمام إليه (و) إبتداه وقت صلاة العشاء) والوتر منه) أي من غروب الشفق على الإختلاف الذي تقدم (إلى) قبيل طلوع (الصبح) الصادق لإجماع السلف وحديث إمامة جبريل لا ينفي ما وراء وقت إمامته ، وقال الله: إن الله زادكم صلاة الا وهي الوتر فصلوها بین العشاء الأخيرة إلى طلوع الفجر» (ولا يقدم) صلاة الوتر على) صلاة (العشاء) لهذا الحديث واللترتيب اللازم بين فرض العشاء وواجب الوتر عند الإمام (ومن لم يجد وقتهما) أي العشاء والوتر (لم يجبا عليه بأن كان في بلد كبلغار، وبأقصى المشرق يطلع فيها الفجر قبل مغيب الشفق في أقصر ليالي السنة لعدم وجود السبب، وهو الوقت وليس مثل اليوم الذي كسنة من أيام الدجال للأمر فيه بتقدير الأوقات وكذا الآجال في البيع والإجارة والصوم والحج والعدة كما بسطنا في أصل هذا المختصر والله الموفق
العلامة فقط بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإن الوقت لا وجود له أصلاً، ورد بأن الوقت موجود قطعاً والمفقود هو العلامة فقط فإذن لا فرق وتمامه في تحفة الأخيار قوله: (للأمر فيه بتقدير الأوقات) أي أوقات الصلاة أي على خلاف القياس، فلا يقاس غيره عليه لأنا لو وكلنا إلى الاجتهاد لم نصل فيه إلا صلاة يوم واحد كما قاله القاضي عياض قوله: (وكذا الآجال في البيع الخ) وينظر ابتداء اليوم فيقدر كل فصل من الفصول الأربعة بحسب ما يكون لكل يوم من الزيادة، والنقص كما في كتب الشافعية وقواعد المذهب لا تأباه
The Book of Prayer. Due to the saying of Ibn Umar: 'The twilight is the redness', and it is narrated from the senior Companions, and the people of language agree upon it, and the return of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) to it is reported. (And) the beginning of the time of Isha prayer (and Witr) is from the disappearance of the twilight according to the difference mentioned (until) just before the dawn (the true dawn) due to the consensus of the Salaf and the hadith of the imamate of Jibril does not negate what is beyond the time of his imamate. And Allah said: 'Indeed Allah has added for you a prayer, namely Witr, so pray it between the last Isha and the break of dawn.' (And) Witr prayer is not performed before Isha prayer because of this hadith and the necessary order between the obligatory Isha and the obligatory Witr according to Imam Abu Hanifa. (And whoever does not find the time for them), i.e., Isha and Witr, (they are not obligatory upon him), such as in a place like Bulghar, and in the far east where dawn appears before the sunset of the previous twilight in the shortest nights of the year due to the absence of the cause, which is the time. And it is not like the day that is like a year from the days of the Dajjal because of the command to estimate the times, and likewise the terms in sale, lease, fasting, Hajj, and waiting period as we have elaborated in the original of this abridgement. And Allah is the Granter of success. Only the sign (is missing) contrary to our case where the time has no existence at all. It was responded that the time definitely exists, only the sign is missing, so there is no difference. Its completion is in Tuhfat al-Akhyar. His saying: 'For the command to estimate the times' meaning the prayer times, i.e., contrary to analogy, so nothing else is analogized to it because if we were to refer to ijtihad, we would only pray one day's prayer in it, as al-Qadi Iyad said. His saying: 'And likewise the terms in sale etc.' And the beginning of the day is considered, and each season is estimated according to the increase and decrease of each day, as in the Shafi'i books, and the principles of the school do not reject it.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya discusses the time for Isha and Witr prayers and the problem of determining times in extreme latitudes. The author first clarifies that the start of Isha is when the red twilight disappears, citing the authority of Ibn Umar, the agreement of the Companions, and philologists. Abu Hanifa's opinion is that the twilight is the redness, and the time for Isha and Witr extends until just before true dawn. The hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer on successive nights is not exhaustive. The author then addresses the case of places like Bulghar (a northern city) where in summer the dawn comes before the previous sunset, making the usual signs of time absent. In such places, the obligation of Isha and Witr is lifted because the cause (time) is not found. However, this is distinguished from the day of the Dajjal which is supernaturally long, where the Prophet commanded to estimate the prayer times, and by analogy, terms for contracts, fasting, Hajj, and iddah are likewise estimated. The commentator then defends this view against an objection: some say that in our case time is nonexistent while in the Dajjal case it exists but the sign is missing; he rebuts that in both cases the time exists, only the sign is absent, so there is no difference. He adds that estimation is contrary to normal qiyas but is sanctioned by the command of the Prophet, and thus other situations are not analogized to it. The Hanafi school accepts this estimation method, as do the Shafi'is.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight; according to Abu Hanifa, it is the redness in the sky after sunset.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer (witr) performed after Isha; it is wajib at Imam, sunnah muakkadah at Sahibayn.
تغيب الشفق (taghayyub al-shafaq): The disappearance of the twilight, marking the beginning of Isha time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what marks the beginning of the time for Isha prayer?
A) The disappearance of the white twilight
B) The disappearance of the red twilight
C) The appearance of true dawn
D) The sunset

Key Takeaway
The time for Isha begins with the disappearance of the red twilight (shafaq); if this sign is absent in extreme latitudes, the obligation of Isha and Witr is lifted entirely, distinguishing it from the estimated times of the Dajjal day.

Combining Prayers: The Hanafi Restriction and Its Proof
Prohibition of combining prayers except for Hajj and its proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two obligatory prayers in one time and explain the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
Combining prayers is impermissible except for Hajj at Arafat and Muzdalifah.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi explains that the Hanafi school strictly limits combining two obligatory prayers in a single time window to the Hajj pilgrim at Arafat and Muzdalifah. The author cites clear hadith evidence to support this position, including the report of Ibn Umar who saw the Prophet pray each prayer at its appointed time even during travel, and the explicit exception from Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on combining
From the text, determine what the Hanafi school permits and prohibits regarding praying two prayers in one time. Look for the exception clause.
The exception is only for the Hajj pilgrim at specific locations.
2
Examine the apparent combining (jam' suwari)
The text distinguishes between true combining (both in one time) and apparent combining (first at end, second at start). Understand why the latter is permissible.
This is not considered jam' in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the hadith of Ibn Umar
Read the hadith from Ibn Hibban. Note that Ibn Umar delayed Maghrib to the end of its time and then prayed Isha at its beginning, proving each was in its proper time.
This refutes the claim that the Prophet combined in a single time window.
4
Analyze the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
Read the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim. Note that it explicitly limits combining to two occasions during Hajj.
This establishes the only exception in the Hanafi school.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The text mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i allows combining for travel and illness. Briefly note the difference.
The full Shafi'i conditions are discussed in the next lesson.
