His saying: '(in one time)' He is careful about praying both in the same actual time, while each is in its own time, such that he prays the first at the end of its time and the second at the beginning of its time; that is permissible as in al-Tabyin. His saying: '(with an excuse like travel)'; the 'kaaf' includes illness. Imam al-Shafi'i allowed it (combining) both by advancing and delaying. The better is the first for those who are settled, and the second for the traveler, on condition that he prays the first and intends the combination before completing it, and there is no separation between them that is considered a separation customarily. This is for combining by advancing. For combining by delaying, only the intention of combination before the exit of the first is required. The traveler is often tried with this, especially the Hajj pilgrim. There is no harm in taqlid, as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr, but on condition that he adheres to all that that Imam requires, because a patched ruling (hukm mulaffaq) is invalid by consensus, as in the preface of al-Durr. So he says: if he is a follower, and he does not mention it, and no woman after wudu, and he protects from even a small amount of impurity. And the narration of consensus on the invalidity of patched rulings is subject to consideration, for the most correct view in the Maliki school is its permissibility, and the prohibited is following the licenses (takhayyur) of the schools. His saying: '(And the interpretation of what is narrated on combination, etc.)' The evidence for the correctness of this interpretation is what Ibn Hibban narrated from Nafi': I went out with Ibn Umar on a journey and the sun set. When it became dark, I said, 'Prayer, may Allah have mercy on you.' He turned to me and continued until when it was the last of the twilight, he dismounted and prayed Maghrib, then he stood for Isha while the twilight had disappeared, and he prayed with us, then he faced us and said: 'The Messenger of Allah, when he was in a hurry during travel, would do this.' This is a sahih hadith. Abd al-Haqq said: This is a clear text that he prayed each prayer in its time. And Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'By Him besides whom there is no god, the Messenger of Allah never prayed a prayer except at its time, except two prayers: he combined Zuhr and Asr at Arafah, and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. His saying: '(not for others)' He returned the pronoun in the plural form considering that the intended meaning of 'the Hajj pilgrim' is the genus realized in many individuals. His saying: 'both Zuhr and Asr' then he caught...
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya deals with the ruling on combining two obligatory prayers (jam') in one time. The author first clarifies that if each prayer is performed in its actual time (first at the end of its time, second at the beginning of its time), it is permissible and not true combining. The main discussion is about combining due to an excuse like travel or illness. While the Hanafi school generally does not allow combining two prayers in one time except at Arafat and Muzdalifah for the Hajj pilgrim, Imam al-Shafi'i permits it for travel. The author explains the Shafi'i conditions: for jam' taqdim, one must pray the first first, intend combination before finishing it, and not separate them customarily; for jam' ta'khir, only intention before the first's time ends. The author notes that travelers, especially Hajj pilgrims, may be confronted with this and are permitted to follow the Shafi'i view through taqlid, provided they adhere consistently to all rulings of that madhhab (not patch together). He warns that a patched ruling (hukm mulaffaq) is invalid by consensus, but then notes that the Maliki school actually allows patching. The author supports the Hanafi position by citing the hadith of Ibn Umar, who delayed Maghrib to just before the twilight disappeared and then prayed both Maghrib and Isha each in its time, proving that the Prophet did not combine in time but performed each at its proper time. The only exception in the Hanafi school is for the Hajj pilgrim at Arafat and Muzdalifah, as attested by Ibn Mas'ud. The author concludes by clarifying the pronoun usage in the matn.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): The act of praying two obligatory prayers in the same time window (e.g., Zuhr and Asr in Zuhr time).
تقديم (taqdim): Combining by advancing the later prayer to the time of the earlier one (e.g., Asr with Zuhr).
تأخير (ta'khir): Combining by delaying the earlier prayer to the time of the later one (e.g., Zuhr with Asr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Travel with a valid excuse
B) Arafat and Muzdalifah for the Hajj pilgrim
C) illness
D) Heavy rain

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits true combining of prayers except for the Hajj pilgrim at Arafat and Muzdalifah, supported by clear hadith evidence.

Taqlid and Combining Prayers: Following Another Madhhab
Conditions for taqlid of Shafi'i ruling on combining and invalidity of patched rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions for a Hanafi to follow the Shafi'i ruling on combining prayers and identify why a patched ruling (hukm mulaffaq) is invalid.

Core Idea
Taqlid of Shafi'i for combining is allowed, but requires full adherence to Shafi'i conditions.

The previous lesson established the Hanafi prohibition on combining prayers. However, the text acknowledges that travelers, especially Hajj pilgrims, often face difficulty and may wish to follow the Shafi'i position. In this lesson, we explore the conditions for such taqlid: the necessity of adhering to all requirements of the Shafi'i school, and the prohibition of patching together rulings from different schools to create a new ruling. The text also notes that the Maliki school allows patching, but the author warns against it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on taqlid for combining
Read the text where it says 'لا بأس بالتقليد كما في البحر والنهر'. What does the author permit?
Taqlid is allowed for the traveler, especially the Hajj pilgrim.
2
State the condition for valid taqlid
The text says 'بشرط أن يلتزم جميع ما يوجبه ذلك الإمام'. What does this condition require?
The follower must adhere to all rulings of the madhhab he follows, not just the convenient one.
3
Define 'hukm mulaffaq' and why it is invalid
Text: 'لأن الحكم الملفق باطل بالإجماع'. Define a patched ruling and explain why it is invalid.
A patched ruling is one that combines parts of different schools arbitrarily.
4
Note the exception (Maliki view)
The text mentions that the Maliki school allows patching. How does this affect the claim of consensus?
The author argues that the consensus claim is not absolute because Malikis allow it.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a Hanafi traveler who wants to combine prayers, what must he do if he follows the Shafi'i view?
He must fulfill all Shafi'i conditions: intention before completing the first, no customarily long separation, etc.

The Hanafi Ruling: No True Combining of Prayers Except at Arafah
States the ruling and evidence for prohibition of combining prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that true combining of two obligatory prayers is not allowed and explain the school's interpretation of the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
True combining of prayers is invalid; reported 'combining' is actually praying each in its own time.

This lesson explores a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh: the prohibition of combining two obligatory prayers in a single time. While some hadiths report the Prophet combining prayers during travel, the Hanafi school interprets these as a virtual combination within each prayer's proper time. We will examine the evidence and the reasoning behind this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State the Hanafi position: one may not combine two fard prayers in one time. Offering a prayer before its time is invalid, and delaying is not allowed.
The ruling is based on the principle that each prayer has a fixed time.
2
Understand the Hanafi interpretation of hadith
The commentator explains that what is reported as combining is actually praying the first at the end of its time and the second at the beginning of its time. This is a virtual combination, not a true one.
This interpretation respects the fixed times while accommodating travel.
3
Examine the primary evidence
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar (recorded by Ibn Hibban) shows that he prayed Maghrib at the end of twilight and 'Isha' at its disappearance, and stated the Prophet did similarly. This is a clear text that each prayer was in its own time.
Ibn Mas'ud's hadith confirms that the only true combining was at Arafah and Muzdalifah.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i permits true combining during travel and rain, based on the same hadiths but with a different interpretation.
The Hanafi school strictly limits true combining to the Hajj exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين فرضين في وقت إذ لا تصح التي قدمت عن وقتها ولا يحل تأخير الوقتية إلى دخول وقت آخر (بعذر) كسفر ومطر وحمل المروي في الجمع على تأخير الأولى إلى قبيل آخر وقتها وعند فراغه دخل وقت الثانية فصلاها فيه إلا في عرفة للحاج لا لغيرهم بشرط أن يصلي الحاج مع الإمام الأعظم أي السلطان أو نائبه كلا من الظهر والعصر ولو سبق فيهما العلامة فقط بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإن الوقت لا وجود له أصلاً، ورد بأن الوقت موجود قطعاً والمفقود هو العلامة فقط فإذن لا فرق وتمامه في تحفة الأخيار قوله: (للأمر فيه بتقدير الأوقات) أي أوقات الصلاة أي على خلاف القياس، فلا يقاس غيره عليه لأنا لو وكلنا إلى الاجتهاد لم نصل فيه إلا صلاة يوم واحد كما قاله القاضي عياض قوله: (وكذا الآجال في البيع الخ) وينظر ابتداء اليوم فيقدر كل فصل من الفصول الأربعة بحسب ما يكون لكل يوم من الزيادة، والنقص كما في كتب الشافعية وقواعد المذهب لا تأباه قوله: (في وقت) احترز عن الجمع بينهما فعلاً، وكل واحدة منهما في وقتها بأن يصلي الأولى في آخر وقتها، والثانية في أول وقتها فذلك جائز كما في التبيين. قوله : (بعذر كسفر) أدخلت الكاف المرض، وجوزه الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه تقديماً وتأخيراً والأفضل الأول للمنازل، والثاني للسائر بشرط أن يقدم الأولى وينوي الجمع قبل الفراغ منها، وعدم الفصل بينهما بما يعد فاصلاً عرفاً هذا في جمع التقديم، ولم يشترط في جمع التأخير سوى نية الجمع قبل خروج الأولى، وكثيراً ما يبتلى المسافر بمثله لاسيما الحاج ولا بأس بالتقليد كما في البحر والنهر لكن بشرط أن يلتزم جميع ما يوجبه ذلك الإمام لأن الحكم الملفق باطل بالإجماع كما في ديباجة الدر فيقرأ إن كان مؤتماً ولا ذكره، ولا أمرأة بعد وضوء ويحترز عن إصابة قليل النجاسة وحكاية الإجماع يمس على بطلان الملفق منظور فيها فإن الأصح من مذهب الإمام مالك رضي الله عنه جوازه والمنهي تتبع الرخص من المذاهب. قوله : (وحمل المروي في الجمع الخ) الدليل على صحة هذا التأويل ما روى ابن حبان عن نافع قال: خرجت مع ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما في سفرة وغابت الشمس فلما أبطأ قلت الصلاة يرحمك الله فالتفت إلي ومضى حتى إذا كان في آخر الشفق نزل فصلى المغرب، ثم أقام العشاء وقد توارى الشفق فصلى بنا، ثم أقبل علينا فقال : إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا أعجل به السير صنع هكذا وهذا حديث صحيح. قال عبد الحق : وهذا نص على أنه صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها وقال عبد الله بن مسعود: والذي لا إله غيره ما صلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة قط إلا لوقتها إلا صلاتين جمع بين الظهر والعصر بعرفة وبين المغرب والعشاء بجمع رواه الشيخان قوله : (لا) لغيرهم أعاد الضمير بلفظ الجمع نظراً إلى أن المراد بالحاج الجنس المتحقق في أفراد كثيرة. قوله كلا من الظهر والعصر) فإن أدرك إحدى الصلاتين لا يجوز له الجمع (و) بشرط (الإحرام) بحج لا عمرة حال صلاة كل من الظهر والعصر ولو أحرم بعد الزوال في الصحيح، وصحة الظهر فلو تبين فساده أعاده ويعيد العصر إذا دخل وقته المعتاد فهذه أربعة شروط لصحة الجمع عند الإمام وعندهما يجمع الحاج، ولو منفرداً قال في البرهان : وهو الأظهر (فيجمع) الحاج بين الظهر والعصر جمع تقديم في ابتداء وقت الظهر بمسجد نمرة كما هو العادة فيه بأذان واحد وإقامتين ليتنبه للجمع ولا يفصل بينهما بنافلة ولا سنة الظهر
And one does not combine two obligatory prayers in one time, for the one offered early is not valid from its time, and it is not permissible to delay the time-bound prayer until the entry of another time, even with an excuse like travel or rain. The reported narration about combining is interpreted as delaying the first to near the end of its time, and when he finishes, the time of the second has entered, so he prays it in its time. Except at 'Arafah for the pilgrim, not for others, on condition that the pilgrim prays with the supreme imam, i.e., the sultan or his deputy, both Dhuhr and 'Asr, even if he only caught the sign [of the time] in them. This is unlike our case, for the time has no existence at all. It was responded that the time exists definitely; what is lost is only the sign, so there is no difference. Its completion is in Tuhfat al-Akhyar. His saying: (For the command therein of estimating the times) i.e., the times of prayer, i.e., contrary to analogy, so nothing else is analogized to it, for if we delegated to ijtihad we would only pray one day's prayer in it, as al-Qadi 'Iyad said. His saying: (And similarly the terms in sale, etc.) and the beginning of the day is considered, and each of the four seasons is estimated according to what each day has of increase and decrease, as in the books of the Shafi'is, and the principles of the school do not reject it. His saying: (In a time) is a precaution against actually combining, and each one of them in its time, such that one prays the first at the end of its time and the second at the beginning of its time, that is permissible as in al-Tabyin. His saying: (With an excuse like travel) the kaf includes illness. Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, permitted it, both advance and delay. The better is the first for those staying overnight and the second for the traveler, on condition that he advances the first and intends the combination before finishing it, and there be no separation between them that is customarily considered a separator. This in advance combination; in delay combination, only the intention of combination before the exit of the first is stipulated. And often the traveler is afflicted with this, especially the pilgrim, and there is no harm in taqlid, as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr, but on condition that he adheres to all that that imam obligates, because the patched-up ruling is invalid by consensus, as in the introduction of al-Durr. He recites if he is following and does not mention it, nor a woman after wudu, and he avoids touching minor impurity. The quote of consensus on the invalidity of the patched-up is subject to scrutiny, for the more correct in the madhhab of Imam Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, is its permissibility, and what is prohibited is the pursuit of concessions from different schools. His saying: (And the reported narration about combining, etc.) The evidence for the validity of this interpretation is what Ibn Hibban narrated from Nafi' who said: I went out with Ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, on a journey, and the sun set. When it became late, I said: Prayer, may Allah have mercy on you. He turned to me and went on until when he was at the end of twilight, he dismounted and prayed Maghrib. Then he called the iqamah for 'Isha' when twilight had disappeared, and he prayed with us. Then he faced us and said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, used to do this when travel hurried him. This is a sound hadith. 'Abd al-Haqq said: This is a clear text that he prayed each one in its time. 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: By Him besides whom there is no god, the Messenger of Allah never prayed any prayer except at its time, except two prayers: combining Dhuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafah, and Maghrib and 'Isha' at Muzdalifah. Narrated by the two shaykhs. His saying: (not for others) - he returned the pronoun in plural form considering that what is meant by 'the pilgrim' is the genus realized in many individuals. His saying: both Dhuhr and 'Asr, if he catches one of the two prayers, he is not permitted to combine. (And) on condition of (ihram) for Hajj, not 'Umrah, at the time of each of Dhuhr and 'Asr, even if he assumed ihram after zawal according to the sound position, and the validity of Dhuhr - if its invalidity becomes apparent he repeats it and repeats 'Asr when its usual time enters. These are four conditions for the validity of combination according to the Imam. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the pilgrim combines even if alone. He said in al-Burhan: And it is the stronger view. (So he combines) the Hajj pilgrim between Dhuhr and 'Asr as an advance combination at the beginning of the time of Dhuhr in the mosque of Namira as is customary, with one adhan and two iqamahs to draw attention to the combination, and he does not separate between them with a supererogatory prayer nor the sunnah of Dhuhr.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: one may not combine two obligatory prayers in a single time. The reason given is that a prayer offered before its time is invalid, and it is not permissible to delay a prayer until the next prayer time without a valid excuse. The commentator explains that what is reported in some hadiths about the Prophet combining prayers during travel is actually not true combination (jam' haqiqi) but rather a virtual combination: the first prayer is delayed to the end of its time and the second is prayed at the beginning of its time. The only exception to this rule is for the Hajj pilgrim at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah. The text then details the conditions for combining at 'Arafah: the pilgrim must pray behind the supreme imam (or his deputy), must be in the state of ihram for Hajj (not 'Umrah), must have a valid Dhuhr prayer, and must be at 'Arafah. There is a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the condition of praying with the imam; the text states that according to the companions, the pilgrim may combine even if praying alone, and this is considered the stronger view (al-azhar). The passage then describes the practical method: the pilgrim combines Dhuhr and 'Asr at the beginning of Dhuhr time in the mosque of Namira with one adhan and two iqamahs, and does not pray any sunnah or nafl between them.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): The act of combining two obligatory prayers, either by advancing the second to the time of the first (jam' taqdim) or delaying the first to the time of the second (jam' ta'khir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith is used by the Hanafi school to support the interpretation that reported combining is actually praying each prayer in its own time?
A) Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
B) Hadith of Ibn 'Umar (Nafi' narration)
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not permit true combining of prayers except for the Hajj pilgrim at Arafah and Muzdalifah; all other reports of combining are interpreted as virtual combination within each prayer's own time.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Combining Prayers at Arafah: The Hanafi Exception
Details conditions and dispute for combining at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four conditions for combining Dhuhr and 'Asr at Arafah according to Imam Abu Hanifa and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding praying with the imam.

Core Idea
The only true combining of prayers is for the pilgrim at Arafah; conditions vary between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

While the general rule prohibits true combining, there is one exception: the Hajj pilgrim at Arafah may combine Dhuhr and 'Asr. This lesson details the specific conditions required, including the requirement of praying behind the supreme imam according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the alternative view of his companions that allows combining even when alone. The relied-upon view is that the pilgrim may combine even if alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exceptional case
The exception is for the Hajj pilgrim at Arafah to combine Dhuhr and 'Asr in advance (jam' taqdim). This is the only true combination in the Hanafi school.
The exception also applies at Muzdalifah for Maghrib and 'Isha' as per hadith.
2
List the conditions according to Imam Abu Hanifa
The text mentions four conditions: (1) praying behind the supreme imam (sultan or his deputy), (2) being present at Arafah, (3) being in ihram for Hajj (not 'Umrah), (4) having a valid Dhuhr prayer (if Dhuhr is invalid, the combination is not valid).
The condition of praying with the imam is disputed.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the pilgrim may combine even if praying alone, and this is considered the stronger view (al-azhar) as stated in al-Burhan.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn.
4
Describe the practical method
The combination is performed at the mosque of Namira at the beginning of Dhuhr time, with one adhan and two iqamahs, and no sunnah or nafl prayers between them.
This draws attention to the fact that it is a combination.

Source Text

ولا يجمع بين فرضين في وقت إذ لا تصح التي قدمت عن وقتها ولا يحل تأخير الوقتية إلى دخول وقت آخر (بعذر) كسفر ومطر وحمل المروي في الجمع على تأخير الأولى إلى قبيل آخر وقتها وعند فراغه دخل وقت الثانية فصلاها فيه إلا في عرفة للحاج لا لغيرهم بشرط أن يصلي الحاج مع الإمام الأعظم أي السلطان أو نائبه كلا من الظهر والعصر ولو سبق فيهما العلامة فقط بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإن الوقت لا وجود له أصلاً، ورد بأن الوقت Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: one may not combine two obligatory prayers in a single time. The reason given is that a prayer offered before its time is invalid, and it is not permissible to delay a prayer until the next prayer time without a valid excuse. The commentator explains that what is reported in some hadiths about the Prophet combining prayers during travel is actually not true combination (jam' haqiqi) but rather a virtual combination: the first prayer is delayed to the end of its time and the second is prayed at the beginning of its time. The only exception to this rule is for the Hajj pilgrim at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah. The text then details the conditions for combining at 'Arafah: the pilgrim must pray behind the supreme imam (or his deputy), must be in the state of ihram for Hajj (not 'Umrah), must have a valid Dhuhr prayer, and must be at 'Arafah. The passage then describes the practical method: the pilgrim combines Dhuhr and 'Asr at the beginning of Dhuhr time in the mosque of Namira with one adhan and two iqamahs, and does not pray any sunnah or nafl between them.

Key Terms
الجمع (al-jam'): The act of combining two obligatory prayers; here, specifically the true combination at Arafah (jam' taqdim).
الإمام الأعظم (al-imam al-a'zam): The supreme imam, i.e., the ruling sultan or his deputy who leads the Hajj.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), is it necessary for the pilgrim to pray behind the supreme imam to combine prayers at Arafah?
A) Yes, it is required
B) No, the pilgrim may combine even if alone
C) It is recommended but not required
D) Only if the imam is present

Key Takeaway
The only true combination of prayers in the Hanafi school is for the Hajj pilgrim at Arafah, and according to the stronger view, combining is valid even if praying alone.

Combining Prayers at Muzdalifah and Prohibition of Maghrib on the Way
Specifies the method of combining Maghrib and 'Isha' at Muzdalifah and prohibits praying Maghrib on the road.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for combining Maghrib and 'Isha' at Muzdalifah and explain why praying Maghrib on the road is invalid.

Core Idea
Maghrib must be delayed to Muzdalifah; praying it on the road nullifies it.

During Hajj, the pilgrim enters a special zone where the routine prayer schedule is overridden by the needs of the ritual. Muzdalifah is the only site where Maghrib and 'Isha' are combined as a delay combination (jam' ta'khir). This lesson breaks down the ruling, its proof, and the consequences of violating it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the pilgrim required to do regarding Maghrib and 'Isha' on the night of Muzdalifah? Identify that he must delay Maghrib and combine it with 'Isha' in the time of 'Isha'.
This is a delay combination (jam' ta'khir), not a forward combination.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the text cite? The hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told a man praying Maghrib on the road: 'al-salat amamak' (the prayer is ahead of you). Understand that this hadith is the evidence for the prohibition.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), so its authority is zanni al-thubut.
3
Understand the condition of place
The combination is valid only at Muzdalifah and while in ihram. The text emphasizes that 'road' is incidental; even in 'Arafat, praying Maghrib at its own time is not valid for a pilgrim who must be at Muzdalifah.
The place itself (Muzdalifah) is a condition for the delay combination.
4
Apply the consequence of violation
If someone prays Maghrib on the road before arriving at Muzdalifah, that prayer is invalid (batil). He must repeat it at Muzdalifah combined with 'Isha'.
The invalidity is because the proper time for Maghrib for the pilgrim is at Muzdalifah.
5
Note the exception and remedy
If the pilgrim does repeat Maghrib (and 'Isha') at Muzdalifah before dawn, the prayer becomes valid. If dawn breaks without repeating, he must make up the prayers later.
The remedy shows that the ruling is not absolute but tied to the time window.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجمع الحاج بين المغرب والعشاء جمع تأخير فيصليهما بمزدلفة بأذان واحد وإقامة واحدة لعدم الحاجة للتنبيه بدخول الوقتين، ولا يشترط هنا سوى المكان والإحرام (ولم تجز المغرب في طريق مزدلفة) يعني الطريق المعتاد للعامة لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم للذي رآه يصلي المغرب في الطريق الصلاة أمامك فإن فعل ولم يعده حتى طلع الفجر، أو خاف طلوعه قوله: (ولم تجز المغرب في طريق مزدلفة) التقييد بالطريق اتفاقي لأنه لو صلاها في وقتها في عرفات لم تجز منلا مسكين . قوله : (يعني الطريق المعتاد) لا فائدة في التقييد بالمعتاد، بل ذكر الطريق اتفاقي كما علمت. قوله: (الصلاة أمامك) بالنصب أي صلها أمامك وبالرفع مبتدأ وخبر أي موضعها أمامك قوله : (فإن فعل ولم يعده) أي لم يعد ما صلى، وهو المغرب أي مع العشاء، ولو قدم العشاء على المغرب يعيدهما على الترتيب فإن لم يصل العشاء حتى طلع الفجر أعاد العشاء إلى الجواز ذكره السيد. قوله: (أو خاف طلوعه) أي لو أعادهما مجموعتين
And the pilgrim combines Maghrib and 'Isha' as a delay combination, praying them at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah because there is no need for alerting to the entry of the two times. Nothing is stipulated here except the place and ihram. (And Maghrib is not valid on the road to Muzdalifah) meaning the usual road of the common people, because of his saying, peace be upon him, to the one he saw praying Maghrib on the road: 'Prayer is ahead of you.' If he does it and does not repeat it until dawn rises, or fears its rising. His saying: (And Maghrib is not valid on the road to Muzdalifah) the restriction by 'road' is incidental, for if he prayed it at its time in 'Arafat it would not be valid, as in Manla Miskin. His saying: (meaning the usual road) there is no benefit in restricting to 'usual', rather the mention of road is incidental as you know. His saying: (Prayer is ahead of you) in the accusative means pray it ahead of you, and in the nominative is a nominal sentence meaning its place is ahead of you. His saying: (If he does it and does not repeat it) i.e., he does not repeat what he prayed, which is Maghrib along with 'Isha'. If he advanced 'Isha' over Maghrib, he repeats them in order, and if he did not pray 'Isha' until dawn rose, he repeats 'Isha' until it becomes permissible. Mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: (or fears its rising) i.e., if he repeats them as a combined pair.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of combining prayers during Hajj, now focusing on Muzdalifah. The pilgrim combines Maghrib and 'Isha' as a delay combination (jam' ta'khir), meaning he prays both in the time of 'Isha'. This is done with one adhan and one iqamah, as there is no need for two iqamahs because the time of Maghrib has already exited. The only conditions for this combination are the place (Muzdalifah) and the state of ihram; praying behind an imam is not required. The text then addresses a practical issue: if a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the road before reaching Muzdalifah, that prayer is invalid. The Prophet told someone he saw doing this: 'The prayer is ahead of you' — meaning you should wait until Muzdalifah. If someone does pray Maghrib on the road and does not repeat it in Muzdalifah before dawn, he must make it up later. The commentator clarifies that the mention of 'road' is incidental; even in 'Arafat, praying Maghrib at its own time (without combining at Muzdalifah) is not valid. The hadith 'al-salat amamak' is explained grammatically: it can be read nasban meaning 'pray it ahead of you' or raf'an meaning 'the prayer is ahead of you'.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (muzdalifah): A location between 'Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after 'Arafah, and where they combine Maghrib and 'Isha'.
جمع تأخير (jam' ta'khir): A type of combination where the first prayer (Maghrib) is delayed to the time of the second ('Isha').

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer is valid if done in its time
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated at Muzdalifah
C) The prayer is valid but makruh
D) The prayer is valid only if he intended Hajj

Key Takeaway
The pilgrim must delay Maghrib until Muzdalifah and combine it with 'Isha'; otherwise, Maghrib is invalid and must be repeated.

Recommendation to Delay Fajr Prayer (Isfar)
States the recommendation to delay Fajr prayer until daylight (isfar) and provides evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on isfar and identify the evidence from the hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Delaying Fajr until brightness increases reward and congregation, and is the established Hanafi position.

Timing of Fajr prayer is a matter of some discussion among schools. The Hanafi school, as presented in this passage, recommends delaying the prayer until the sky is well-lit (isfar). This lesson unpacks the evidence: a direct hadith commanding isfar for greater reward, a report of Companion consensus on tanwir (illumination), and a practical benefit of increasing the congregation. We will also note an intra-Hanafi difference and a cross-madhhab difference to clarify the strength of the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage opens with 'يستحب الأسفار' — isfar is mustahab (recommended). Note that isfar means delaying until illumination (الإضاءة). The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
The text uses the term 'يستحب' which is a clear indicator of recommendation.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' (Delay Fajr until brightness, for it is greater in reward). This is a direct command from the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم).
The hadith is from the authors of Sunan and declared hasan by al-Tirmidhi. Its transmission is zanni, but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the secondary dalil and hikmah
A second narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i reports that the Companions agreed on tanwir (illumination). Additionally, the passage gives a rationale: isfar allows more people to join the congregation, especially those who sleep heavily.
The rationale (علة) is 'توسيع الحال على النائم' — making it easier for the sleeping person to wake and join.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage mentions a variant view: some say to begin Fajr in darkness (ghalas) and conclude with isfar. However, the 'zahir al-riwayah' (apparent transmitted position) is to start with isfar.
This shows that within the school there is a difference, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) is to start with isfar.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school prefers isfar, while the Shafi'i school prefers praying in the dark (ghalas) to be cautious about entering the time early. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different interpretations of the same evidence.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that Hanafis delay Fajr until brightness, whereas Shafi'is pray earlier in the dim light.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يستحب الأسفار وهو التأخير للإضاءة بالفجر بحيث لو ظهر فسادها أعادها بقراءة مسنونة قبل طلوع الشمس لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر، وقال عليه السلام: «نوروا بالفجر يبارك لكم ولأن في الأسفار تكثير الجاعة لما فيه من توسيع الحال على النائم قوله: (وهو التأخير للإضاءة) في المصباح الأسفار الإضاءة يقال : أسفر الفجر إذا أضاء وأسفر الرجل بالصلاة إذا صلاها في الأسفار اهـ. قوله : (أسفروا بالفجر الخ) رواه أصحاب السنن، وحسنه الترمذي، وروى الطحاوي بإسناده إلى إبراهيم النخعي: ما اجتمع أصحاب رسول الله على شيء ما اجتمعوا على التنوير بالفجر وإسناده صحيح، ويستحب البداءة بالأسفار ، وهو ظاهر الرواية، وقيل : يدخل بغلس، ويختم بالأسفار بحر عن العناية . قوله ولأن في الأسفار تكثير (الجماعة لما فيه من توسيع الحال على النائم
Isfar (delay until brightness) is recommended, which is the delay for illumination in Fajr, such that if its invalidity becomes apparent, he repeats it with a sunnah recitation before sunrise, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Delay Fajr until brightness, for it is greater in reward.' And he said, peace be upon him: 'Illuminate Fajr, it will bless you.' And because in isfar there is increase of congregation due to widening the state for the sleeping person. His saying: (and it is the delay for illumination) in al-Misbah: al-isfar is illumination; it is said: 'asfara al-fajr' when it brightens, and 'asfara al-rajul bi al-salah' when he prays it in isfar. His saying: ('Delay Fajr until brightness, etc.') narrated by the authors of the Sunan, and al-Tirmidhi declared it good. Al-Tahawi narrated with his chain to Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'The companions of the Messenger of Allah never agreed on anything as they agreed on illuminating Fajr.' Its chain is sahih. It is recommended to start with isfar, and that is the apparent narration. It is said: enter with darkness and conclude with isfar. From al-Bahr via al-'Inayah. His saying: 'And because in isfar there is increase of congregation because of widening the state for the sleeping person.'
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended time for Fajr prayer. The Hanafi position, as stated here, is that it is mustahab (recommended) to delay Fajr until the sky is well-lit (isfar), meaning the light is bright enough to distinguish objects. The reasoning is that this increases the reward and allows more people to join the congregation, especially those who find it difficult to wake up early. The text provides two hadiths: 'Delay Fajr until brightness, for it is greater in reward' and 'Illuminate Fajr, it will bless you.' It also cites a saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions unanimously agreed on 'illuminating' (tanwir) Fajr. The commentator notes that according to the 'zahir al-riwayah' (the established transmission), it is recommended to start with isfar, though some say one should begin in the dark (ghalas) and finish in light. The practical benefit is that if the prayer is found to be invalid, it can be repeated with sunnah recitation before sunrise.

Key Terms
الأسفار (al-isfar): The act of delaying Fajr prayer until the sky is bright and illuminated.
التنوير (al-tanwir): Synonym for isfar; lighting up or illuminating the Fajr prayer by delaying it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pray as soon as dawn breaks (ghalas)
B) Delay until the sky is bright (isfar)
C) Delay until just before sunrise
D) There is no preference

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Fajr until the sky is bright (isfar) for greater reward and congregation, based on hadith and Companion practice.

Four Conditions for Combining Prayers During Hajj
States the four conditions for combining prayers during Hajj and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for combining Dhuhr/Asr and Maghrib/Isha during Hajj and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imam condition.

Core Idea
Four conditions must be met for a pilgrim to combine prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah, but the imam requirement is disputed.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi that outlines the four prerequisites (shurut) for a pilgrim to combine prayers at Arafat and Muzdalifah. The text also highlights a disagreement within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa requires the presence of the imam or his deputy, while the Sahibayn allow combining even if one prays alone. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to differentiate between conditions that are strictly necessary and those that are recommended but not essential.

Guided Path
1
List the four conditions
Identify the four conditions from the text: being at Arafat (for advance combination), validity of Dhuhr prayer, presence of the imam or his deputy (according to Imam Abu Hanifa), and being in ihram for Hajj.
These are the shurut for the combination to be valid according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Distinguish advance and delayed combination
Note that Dhuhr and Asr are combined in advance (jam' taqdim) at Arafat, while Maghrib and Isha are combined in delay (jam' ta'khir) at Muzdalifah.
Each combination has its own procedure regarding adhan and iqama.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on the imam condition
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa insists on the imam as a condition, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) allow combination even if the pilgrim is alone. Al-Burhan considers the Sahibayn's view as more apparent (al-azhar).
This affects whether the combination is valid for a solitary pilgrim.
4
Explain the adhan and iqama procedure
For advance combination: one adhan and two iqamas; for delayed combination: one adhan and one iqama. The text also mentions the consequence of praying a voluntary between the two prayers.
If one prays a voluntary, the iqama must be repeated; Zufar adds that even the adhan is repeated.
5
Note the exception regarding the sunnah of Dhuhr
Allama Miskeen allowed praying the sunnah of Dhuhr between the combined prayers, unlike the majority view. The practical effect: if the sunnah is prayed, according to one view the adhan for Asr is repeated, according to another it is not.
The dominant (zahir al-riwaya) view is that the sunnah should not be prayed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) بشرط (الإحرام) بحج لا عمرة حال صلاة كل من الظهر والعصر ولو أحرم بعد الزوال في الصحيح، وصحة الظهر فلو تبين فساده أعاده ويعيد العصر إذا دخل وقته المعتاد فهذه أربعة شروط لصحة الجمع عند الإمام وعندهما يجمع الحاج، ولو منفرداً قال في البرهان : وهو الأظهر (فيجمع) الحاج بين الظهر والعصر جمع تقديم في ابتداء وقت الظهر بمسجد نمرة كما هو العادة فيه بأذان واحد وإقامتين ليتنبه للجمع ولا يفصل بينهما بنافلة ولا سنة الظهر (ويجمع) الحاج ( بين المغرب والعشاء جمع تأخير فيصليهما (بمزدلفة) بأذان واحد وإقامة واحدة لعدم الحاجة للتنبيه بدخول الوقتين، ولا يشترط هنا . سوی المكان والإحرام صح إحدى الصلاتين لا يجوز له الجمع قوله : (فهذه أربعة شروط) أولها عرفة، وثانيها صحة الظهر، وثالثها الإمام أو نائبه ورابعها الإحرام بالحج. قوله : (ولا سنة الظهر) استثنى العلامة مسكين سنة الظهر تبعاً للذخيرة والمحيط والكافي، وأثر الخلاف يظهر فيما لو صلي سنة الظهر فعلى الأول يعاد الأذان للعصر لا على الثاني، وظاهر الرواية هو الأول نهر قاله السيد. قوله : (ولا يشترط هنا سوى المكان والإحرام فلا يشترط الجماعة لهذا الجمع وكذا الإمام ليس بشرط لهذا الجمع أيضاً ولا يتطوع بينهما ولو اشتغل بشيء، أو تطوع أعاد الإقامة، وعند زفر يعيد الآذان أيضاً منلا مسكين ذكره السيد
(And) conditioned by (ihram) for Hajj not Umrah during the time of each of Dhuhr and Asr, even if he assumes ihram after zawal according to the sound view, and the validity of Dhuhr; if its invalidity becomes apparent he repeats it and repeats Asr if its usual time enters. These are four conditions for the validity of combining according to Imam Abu Hanifa; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the pilgrim combines even if alone. He said in al-Burhan: and it is the more apparent. (So the pilgrim combines) between Dhuhr and Asr as an advance combination at the beginning of Dhuhr time at the mosque of Namira as is customary, with one adhan and two iqamas to alert to the combination, and he does not separate between them with a nafl or the sunnah of Dhuhr. (And the pilgrim combines) between Maghrib and Isha as a delayed combination, praying them (at Muzdalifah) with one adhan and one iqama because there is no need for alerting as both times have entered. And nothing is required here except the place and ihram. (Commentary:) The soundness of one of the two prayers does not permit him to combine. He said: (These are four conditions) first: Arafat, second: validity of Dhuhr, third: the imam or his deputy, fourth: ihram for Hajj. He said: (and not the sunnah of Dhuhr) Allama Miskeen excepted the sunnah of Dhuhr following al-Dhakhira, al-Muhit, and al-Kafi, and the effect of the difference appears if one prays the sunnah of Dhuhr; according to the first the adhan for Asr is repeated, not according to the second. The apparent narration is the first (according to) al-Nahr, said al-Sayyid. He said: (And nothing is required here except the place and ihram) So congregation is not required for this combination, nor is the imam a condition for this combination, and he does not pray a voluntary between them; if he busies himself with something or prays a voluntary, he repeats the iqama; according to Zufar he also repeats the adhan. (Mulla Miskeen mentioned it) al-Sayyid quoted.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute. The text begins with the conditions for combining prayers during Hajj. Four conditions are listed: (1) being in Arafat, (2) the validity of Dhuhr prayer, (3) having the imam or his deputy leading the combination, and (4) being in ihram for Hajj. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, all four must be present; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the pilgrim may combine even if alone. The text then describes how to combine: for Dhuhr and Asr, they are prayed in advance at the beginning of Dhuhr time at Masjid Namira with one adhan and two iqamas, and no voluntary prayers are offered between them, including the sunnah of Dhuhr – though some scholars like Allama Miskeen except this sunnah. For Maghrib and Isha, they are combined at Muzdalifah as a delayed combination with one adhan and one iqama. Congregation and the presence of the imam are not conditions for this combination. If one busies himself or prays a voluntary between the two prayers, he must repeat the iqama; Zufar adds that the adhan is also repeated. The relied-upon position is the first according to al-Nahr.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, including the intention and wearing of ihram garments
جمع تقديم (jam' taqdim): Combining Dhuhr and Asr at the beginning of Dhuhr time
جمع تأخير (jam' ta'khir): Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah after Isha time begins

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The four conditions for combining prayers during Hajj according to Abu Hanifa are: being at Arafat (or Muzdalifah), validity of Dhuhr, presence of imam, and ihram for Hajj, with the Sahibayn allowing combination even without an imam.

Ruling on Maghrib Prayer on the Road to Muzdalifah
Prohibits Maghrib on the road to Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Maghrib prayer is invalid on the road to Muzdalifah and identify the Prophet's command as the proof.

Core Idea
Maghrib must be prayed at Muzdalifah; praying on the road invalidates it.

During Hajj, the journey from Arafat to Muzdalifah is a unique time for worship. The Prophet instructed that Maghrib and Isha be combined at Muzdalifah. This lesson explains why praying Maghrib on the road is invalid and the consequence if one does so.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Maghrib on the road to Muzdalifah. The ruling is that it is not valid (la tajuz).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's statement to a man he saw praying on the road: 'الصلاة أمامك' (the prayer is ahead of you), meaning pray at Muzdalifah.
This is a command, which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation.
3
Understand the consequence
If one prays on the road and does not repeat it until dawn or fears dawn, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
The ruling is based on the explicit prophetic command.
4
Note the practical implication
During Hajj, the pilgrim must delay Maghrib until reaching Muzdalifah and pray it there with Isha.
This is a unique ruling for the Hajj journey.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولم تجز المغرب في طريق مزدلفة) يعني الطريق المعتاد للعامة لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم للذي رآه يصلي المغرب في الطريق الصلاة أمامك فإن فعل ولم يعده حتى طلع الفجر، أو خاف طلوعه (و) لما بين أصل الوقت بين المستحب منه بقوله (يستحب الأسفار) وهو التأخير للإضاءة (بالفجر) بحيث لو ظهر فسادها أعادها بقراءة مسنونة قبل طلوع الشمس لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر، وقال عليه السلام: «نوروا بالفجر يبارك لكم ولأن في الأسفار تكثير الجماعة وفي التغليس تقليلها، وما يؤدي إلى التكثير أفضل وليسهل تحصيل ما ورد عن أنس قال : قال رسول الله : من صلى الفجر في جماعة ثم قعد يذكر الله تعالى حتى تطلع الشمس ثم صلى ركعتين كانت له كأجر حجة تامة وعمرة تامة حديث حسن، وقال : من قال صلاة الصبح وهو ثان رجليه قبل أن يتكلم لا إله إلا الله دبر وحده لا شريك له له الملك وله الحمد يحيي ويميت وهو على كل شيء قدير عشر مرات كتب له عشر حنسات ومحى عنه عشر سيات ورفع له عشر درجات وكان يومه ذلك في حرز من كل مكروه وحرس من الشيطان ولم يتبع بذنب أن يدركه في ذلك اليوم إلا الشرك بالله تعالى قال الترمذي هذا حديث حسن وفي بعض النسخ حسن صحيح ذكره النووي، وقال : من مكث في مصلاه بعد الفجر إلى طلوع الشمس كان كمن أعتق أربع رقاب من ولد اسمعيل وقال عليه السلام من مكث في مصلاه بعد العصر إلى غروب الشمس ، والضعيف فيدركان الجماعة. قوله : ( في جماعة) ظاهره ولو مع أهل بيته. قوله : (ثم قعد يذكر الله تعالى أفاد العلامة القاري في شرح الحصن الحصين أن القعود ليس بشرط وإنما المدار على الاشتغال بالذكر هذا الوقت . قوله : (ثم صلى ركعتين) ويقال لهما ركعتا الإشراق، وهما غير سنة الضحى. قوله : (تامة) أي كل منهما أي غير ناقص ثوابهما بارتكاب نحو محظور إحرام أو فساد، والمراد الحج النفل والتأكيد يفيد أن له ذلك الأجر حقيقة، وليس من قبيل الترغيب. قوله: (وهو ثان رجليه) أي قبل أن يتربع، فلا يضر افتراش رجليه تحت أليتيه، أو تغيير هيئة الجلوس إلى صفة يقول بها إمام كهيئة الجلوس التي يقول بها مالك قوله : (قبل أن يتكلم الظاهر في أمثاله ان المراد يتكلم بكلام الدنيا، فلا يضر الفصل بذكر آخر . قوله : (لا شريك له تأكيداً، وتأسيس إن أريد بالوحدة وحدة الذات والصفات وبالثاني نفي الشريك في الأفعال قوله: (ومحى عنه عشر سيئات المشهور إرادة الصغائر وبعض أهل العلم يطلقون فيعم الكبائر في هذا ونظائره ولا حرج على الفاعل المختار الذي لا يسئل عما يفعل. قوله : ورفع له عشر درجات) أي في الجنة أي على من لم يقلها . قوله : (وحرس) أي حفظ. قوله : (ولم يتبع بذنب) بأن يقع مغفوراً أو يوفق للتوبة منه فقوله أن يدركه أي إثمه. قوله: (إلا الشرك بالله تعالى) أي فإنه لو وقع منه يدركه، وليس بواقع منه لقوله سابقاً كان يومه ذلك في حرز من كل مكروه اللهم إلا أن يخصص المكروه بمكروه الدنيا . قوله من ولد إسمعيل) أي من العرب فإن عتق العرب أفضل من عتق العجم، وظاهر الحديث أن هذا الثواب يحصل بمجرد نفسه في مصلاه وإن لم يذكر فإذا ذكر حصل له ذلك الثواب المتقدم، وعتق العرب مع يقول به الإمام الشافعي، وأما عندنا فلا يرقون فيحمل نحو هذا الحديث على الفرض والتقدير. قوله : (وزاد (الثواب) أي في المنتظر بعد العصر لأنه كمن أعتق ثمانياً من الرقاب. قوله : حبس
He said: (And Maghrib is not valid on the road to Muzdalifah) meaning the usual road for the common people, due to his saying ﷺ to the one he saw praying Maghrib on the road: 'The prayer is ahead of you.' If he does it and does not repeat it until dawn appears, or he fears its appearance. (And) because he distinguished between the original time and the recommended time by his saying (Isfar is recommended) which is delaying until illumination (for Fajr) such that if its invalidity appears he repeats it with a sunnah recitation before sunrise, due to his saying ﷺ: 'Delay Fajr until light, for it is greater in reward.' And he said: 'Illuminate for Fajr, it will be blessed for you.' And because in isfar there is multiplication of the congregation, and in taghlis (praying in darkness) there is reduction of it, and what leads to multiplication is better. And to facilitate attaining what is narrated from Anas who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever prays Fajr in congregation, then sits remembering Allah until the sun rises, then prays two rak'ahs, will have the reward of a complete Hajj and complete Umrah' – a hasan hadith. And he said: 'Whoever says at Fajr prayer while he is bending his legs before speaking: La ilaha illa Allah wahdahu la sharika lahu, lahu al-mulk wa lahu al-hamd, yuhyi wa yumit, wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadir, ten times, will have ten good deeds written for him, ten bad deeds erased, ten degrees raised, and that day he will be in protection from every disliked thing and guarded from shaytan, and no sin will overtake him that day except shirk with Allah' – al-Tirmidhi said this is a hasan hadith, and in some copies hasan sahih, mentioned by al-Nawawi. And he said: 'Whoever stays in his prayer place after Fajr until sunrise is like one who freed four slaves from the children of Isma'il.' And he said: 'Whoever stays in his prayer place after Asr until sunset...' and the weak attain the congregation. He said: (in congregation) its apparent meaning is even with his family. He said: (then sits remembering Allah) Allama Qari in Sharh al-Hism al-Hasin said that sitting is not a condition, rather the point is engagement in dhikr at that time. He said: (then prays two rak'ahs) they are called rak'at al-ishraq, and they are other than the duha sunnah. He said: (complete) meaning each of them, i.e. not deficient in reward due to committing something like a prohibition of ihram or corruption, and the intended meaning is supererogatory Hajj, and the emphasis indicates that he actually gets that reward, and it is not just encouragement. He said: (and he is bending his legs) meaning before he sits cross-legged, so it does not harm if he spreads his legs under his buttocks, or changes the sitting posture to a manner practiced by an imam like the sitting posture practiced by Malik. He said: (before speaking) the apparent in such examples is that it means speaking about worldly matters, so separation with another dhikr does not harm. He said: (La sharika lahu) is for emphasis, and for establishment if by unity is meant unity of essence and attributes, and by the second is meant negation of partner in actions. He said: (and ten bad deeds erased) the well-known (view) is that minor sins are intended, but some scholars apply it generally to include major sins in this and similar contexts, and there is no harm from the Free Agent who is not questioned about what He does. He said: (and ten degrees raised) i.e. in Paradise, i.e. over one who did not say it. He said: (and guarded) i.e. protected. He said: (and no sin overtakes him) meaning he will be forgiven or enabled to repent from it, so his saying 'that it overtakes him' means its sin. He said: (except shirk with Allah) i.e. if it occurs from him it will overtake him, but it will not occur from him because of his earlier saying 'that day he will be in protection from every disliked thing' unless he specifies the disliked thing as worldly disliked things. He said: (from the children of Isma'il) i.e. from Arabs, because freeing Arabs is better than freeing non-Arabs, and the apparent meaning of the hadith is that this reward is attained simply by his staying in his prayer place even if he does not remember, and if he remembers he gets that previous reward. Freeing Arabs is held by Imam al-Shafi'i; as for us (Hanafis), they (Arabs) cannot be enslaved, so this hadith is interpreted as a hypothetical and estimative. He said: (and he increased (the reward)) i.e. the awaited after Asr, because he is like one who freed eight slaves. He said: (Habs – meaning detention?)
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling with proof. The text gives two distinct rulings. First: The prohibition of praying Maghrib on the road to Muzdalifah during Hajj. The proof is the Prophet's statement to a man: 'The prayer is ahead of you' (i.e., pray at Muzdalifah). If someone prays on the road and does not repeat it until dawn, or fears dawn, he must repeat it. Second: The recommendation (istihbab) of isfar – delaying Fajr until daylight appears rather than praying in deep darkness. The proof is the hadith 'Delay Fajr until light, for it is greater in reward' and 'Illuminate for Fajr, it will be blessed for you'. The rationale is that it increases the congregation, as more people can attend. Then the text lists several rewards for those who pray Fajr in congregation and then stay in the mosque until sunrise, reciting specific adhkar. The commentary clarifies that the sitting is not a condition; rather, the key is engaging in dhikr. The two rak'ahs prayed after sunrise are the ishraq prayer, distinct from duha. The rewards include forgiveness of minor sins, lifting of degrees, protection from shaytan, and reward like freeing slaves. The Hanafi school holds that Arabs cannot be enslaved, so the hadith about freeing Arab slaves is treated as hypothetical. The passage concludes with a note about staying after Asr for a similar reward.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after Arafat, and where Maghrib and Isha are prayed together.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the road to Muzdalifah and does not repeat it until after dawn?
A) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid but the pilgrim is sinful.
D) The prayer is makruh and repetition is optional.

Key Takeaway
Maghrib prayer on the road to Muzdalifah is invalid due to the Prophet's command to pray at Muzdalifah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Recommendation of Isfar for Fajr and Rewards of Post-Fajr Dhikr
Recommends delaying Fajr until light and expounds on related rewards

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi recommendation of isfar (delaying Fajr until light) and list the rewards for those who engage in dhikr after Fajr.

Core Idea
Isfar for Fajr is recommended because it increases congregation and reward.

Praying Fajr when there is light is a recommended practice in the Hanafi school. This lesson examines the proof and wisdom behind isfar, along with the great rewards for those who engage in dhikr after Fajr. The text also clarifies that these rewards are genuine, not just encouragement.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on isfar
Isfar (praying Fajr when daylight appears) is mustahabb (recommended).
It is not obligatory.
2
Identify the proofs
The hadith 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' (Delay Fajr until light, for it is greater in reward) and 'نوروا بالفجر يبارك لكم'.
The imperative here indicates recommendation, not obligation, due to other considerations.
3
Understand the wisdom
Isfar increases the congregation (تكثير الجماعة), while taghlis (praying in darkness) reduces it.
Larger congregation is better for reward.
4
Recognize the rewards for post-Fajr dhikr
The text lists rewards: whoever prays Fajr in congregation, then sits remembering Allah until sunrise, then prays two rak'ahs (ishraq), gets reward of complete Hajj and Umrah. Also, specific dhikr brings forgiveness, protection, and elevation of degrees.
These rewards are real, not just figurative.
5
Distinguish ishraq from duha
The two rak'ahs after sunrise are called ishraq, and they are different from the duha prayer.
Ishraq is performed shortly after sunrise, duha later.

Source Text

Commentary
Passage type: Ruling with proof. The text gives two distinct rulings. First: The prohibition of praying Maghrib on the road to Muzdalifah during Hajj. The proof is the Prophet's statement to a man: 'The prayer is ahead of you' (i.e., pray at Muzdalifah). If someone prays on the road and does not repeat it until dawn, or fears dawn, he must repeat it. The proof is the hadith 'Delay Fajr until light, for it is greater in reward' and 'Illuminate for Fajr, it will be blessed for you'. The rationale is that it increases the congregation, as more people can attend. Then the text lists several rewards for those who pray Fajr in congregation and then stay in the mosque until sunrise, reciting specific adhkar. The commentary clarifies that the sitting is not a condition; rather, the key is engaging in dhikr. The two rak'ahs prayed after sunrise are the ishraq prayer, distinct from duha. The rewards include forgiveness of minor sins, lifting of degrees, protection from shaytan, and reward like freeing slaves. Key Terms
الأسفار (al-isfar): Delaying Fajr prayer until daylight appears (illumination) rather than praying in darkness
التغليس (al-taghlis): Praying Fajr in deep darkness before dawn breaks

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school recommend isfar for Fajr?
A) Because it is easier to recite Quran in daylight.
B) Because it allows more people to join the congregation.
C) Because the Prophet always prayed at sunrise.
D) Because it avoids the sin of praying in darkness.

Key Takeaway
Isfar for Fajr is recommended because it enlarges the congregation and brings greater reward, as evidenced by the Prophet's command and the wisdom of community worship.

intermediate

Isfar for Fajr and the Virtue of Post-Sunrise Worship
States ruling on isfar and provides hadith proofs for virtues of Fajr congregation and post-sunrise worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on isfar for Fajr, explain the dalil from the hadith of Anas, and identify the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Isfar increases congregation; the hadith promises Hajj and Umrah reward for prayer, dhikr, and ishraq.

In this passage, the commentator explains why the Hanafi school prefers delaying Fajr until the light is clear (isfar) rather than praying in deep darkness (taghlis). The key rationale is maximizing the congregation, which brings greater reward. The passage then provides several hadiths that highlight the immense virtues of praying Fajr in congregation, engaging in dhikr until sunrise, and performing the two rak'ahs of ishraq. We will examine the ruling, the proofs, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is isfar? What is the Hanafi ruling on it for Fajr? Identify the rationale given: increasing congregation.
Isfar is mustahab; taghlis is makruh tanzihan if it reduces congregation.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof is the hadith from Anas recorded by Tirmidhi. Identify its content: the reward for Fajr in congregation, then dhikr until sunrise, then two rak'ahs.
The hadith is classified as hasan (good) by Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith support isfar? It shows the virtue of congregation and post-sunrise worship, implying that delaying Fajr to allow more people to participate is better.
The hadith does not explicitly mention isfar, but the reasoning is that isfar enables more people to be part of the congregation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Compare with the Shafi'i school, which prefers taghlis (praying in darkness) because it follows the Prophet's usual practice and is more humble.
The Hanafi response is that the Prophet also performed isfar at times, and the benefit of congregation outweighs the darkness.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is isfar the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school? The authority is zahir al-riwayah and the emphasis on collective worship.
The later Hanafi masters (e.g., al-Tahtawi) uphold isfar as mustahab.

اسمعيل وزاد الثواب الإنتظار فرض وفي الأول لنفل
Book of Prayer. Isfar (delaying until light) increases congregation, and taghlis (praying in darkness) decreases it, and what leads to greater congregation is better, and to facilitate attaining what is reported from Anas who said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever prays Fajr in congregation then sits remembering Allah until the sun rises then prays two rak'ahs, for him is the reward of a complete Hajj and a complete Umrah – a hasan hadith. And he said: Whoever says after the Fajr prayer, while still folding his legs before speaking: 'La ilaha illallah wahdahu la sharika lahu, lahu al-mulku wa lahu al-hamdu yuhyi wa yumit wa huwa 'ala kulli shay'in qadir' ten times, for him are written ten good deeds, ten sins are erased, ten degrees are raised, and that day he will be in protection from every disliked thing and protected from the devil, and no sin will overtake him that day except shirk with Allah. At-Tirmidhi said this is a hasan hadith, and in some copies hasan sahih, mentioned by an-Nawawi. And he said: Whoever remains in his prayer place after Fajr until the sun rises is like one who freed four slaves from the children of Isma'il. And he said: Whoever remains in his prayer place after Asr until the sun sets... And the weak person can catch the congregation. Commentary: (In congregation) apparently even with his family. (Then sits remembering Allah) Al-Qari explained that sitting is not a condition, rather the focus is on being occupied with dhikr at that time. (Then prays two rak'ahs) called rak'at al-ishraq, and they are different from the duha sunnah. (Complete) meaning each of them, i.e., their reward is not deficient by committing something prohibited during ihram or invalidating, and the intended is supererogatory Hajj, and the emphasis shows that he actually gets that reward, not just encouragement. (Folding his legs) i.e., before sitting cross-legged, so it does not harm to spread his legs under his buttocks or change the sitting posture to one held by an imam like Malik's posture. (Before speaking) apparently in such instances it means speaking worldly talk, so pausing with other dhikr does not harm. (No partner for Him) as emphasis and foundation; if oneness of essence and attributes is meant by the first, and by the second negation of partner in actions. (Erase ten sins) the well-known is that small sins are intended, but some scholars make it general including major sins in this and similar cases, and there is no constraint on the free agent who is not questioned about what He does. (Raise ten degrees) in Paradise, i.e., over those who did not say it. (Protection) i.e., preservation. (No sin overtake him) that it be forgiven or he be guided to repentance from it, so his saying 'overtake' means its punishment. (Except shirk with Allah) i.e., if it occurs from him, it overtakes, but it does not occur from him because earlier he said 'that day he will be in protection from every disliked thing', unless the disliked is specified as worldly disliked. (From the children of Isma'il) meaning Arabs, for freeing Arabs is better than freeing non-Arabs, and the apparent meaning of the hadith is that this reward is obtained merely by sitting in his prayer place even if he does not mention, but if he mentions, he gets that earlier reward, and freeing Arabs is held by Imam ash-Shafi'i, while according to us they are not enslaved, so such hadith is interpreted as hypothetical. (Increased reward) i.e., in waiting after Asr because he is like one who freed eight slaves. Commentary: (He said) was like one who freed eight slaves from the children of Isma'il, and the reward increased because the waiting is for a fard, while in the first it is for a nafl.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, where the commentator begins by stating the ruling that isfar (delaying the Fajr prayer until the light is clear) is preferred over taghlis (praying in deep darkness) because it allows for a larger congregation, and anything that increases the congregation is better. The commentator then provides hadith proofs to support the virtue of congregation and associated acts. The first hadith from Anas radi Allahu 'anhu promises the reward of a complete Hajj and Umrah for one who prays Fajr in congregation, then sits in dhikr until sunrise, and then prays two rak'ahs (ishraq). The commentator clarifies that sitting is not strictly necessary; what matters is being occupied with dhikr during that time. The two rak'ahs are called ishraq and are distinct from the duha prayer. The term 'complete' indicates that the reward is not diminished by any deficiency in the acts themselves. The second hadith prescribes a dhikr to be said after Fajr while still in the sitting posture before any worldly speech, promising numerous rewards. The commentator explains that the silence before speaking refers to avoiding worldly talk, not interrupting dhikr. The third hadith equates sitting in the prayer place after Fajr until sunrise to freeing four Arab slaves, and after Asr until sunset to freeing eight slaves. The commentator notes that freeing Arab slaves is considered more virtuous, though in the Hanafi school non-Muslim Arabs are not enslaved, so such hadiths are taken as hypothetical. The overall message encourages maximizing congregation at Fajr and engaging in worship after the prayer until sunrise.

Key Terms
إسفار (isfār): Delaying the Fajr prayer until the light is clear and the sky is bright.
تغليس (taghlīs): Praying Fajr in the darkness before dawn becomes clear.
ركعتا الإشراق (rakʿatā al-ishrāq): Two rak'ahs prayed after sunrise, after sitting in dhikr since Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in the passage, what is the reward for one who prays Fajr in congregation, sits remembering Allah until sunrise, and then prays two rak'ahs?
A) The reward of a complete Hajj and Umrah
B) The reward of freeing four slaves
C) The reward of ten good deeds
D) The reward of a fard Hajj

Key Takeaway
Isfar is preferred for Fajr to maximize congregation, and the hadiths promise immense rewards for post-Fajr worship including dhikr and ishraq prayer.

Preferred Times for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr
Lists mustahab timings for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr with conditions and commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred times for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr according to the Hanafi school, explain the evidence, and identify exceptions such as Muzdalifah and cloudy days.

Core Idea
Delay Fajr until light but hurry it in Muzdalifah; delay Zuhr in summer, hasten it in winter; always delay Asr.

This passage from the matn and its commentary clarifies the mustahab (recommended) timings for the daily prayers. While all prayers have a permissible window, certain times earn greater reward. The Hanafi school relies on explicit hadith, such as the command to delay Zuhr in extreme heat, and balances this with communal obligations like congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine which prayer is being discussed and whether the ruling is mustahab, makruh, etc. The passage explicitly states 'mustahab' for each timing.
Mustahab means recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the textual evidence cited. For Zuhr in summer, the hadith 'Abridu bi al-Zuhr' is quoted.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith supports the ruling. The imperative 'abridu' indicates recommendation, and the stated reason ('intense heat from Hell') provides wisdom.
Hanafi usul: al-amr li al-nadb when accompanied by a reason.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify areas of disagreement, such as the definition of ibrad's limit or whether women should always pray in darkness. The commentary addresses these.
Some later scholars differed on seasonal application.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine the relied-upon position. The matn represents the madhhab; the commentary confirms it, though it notes debates.
The mufta bihi is as stated in the matn.

النهر عن القنية قوله: (ويستحب الإبراد بالظهر في الصيف) وحده أن يتمكن الماشون إلى الجماعات من المشي في ظل الجدران كما الإيضاح عن الحقائق وقال في السراج : بحيث يصلي قبل بلوغ الظل مثلاً اهـ وفي الخزانة الوقت المكروه في الظهر ان يدخل في حد الإختلاف، وإذا أخره حتى صار ظل كل شيء مثله فقد دخل في حد الاختلاف حموي قوله : ( في كل البلاد أي سواء كانت حارة أم لا، وسواء إشتد الحر أم لا، وسواء فيه المنفرد والإمام وسواء قصد الناس الجماعة من مكان بعيد أم لا، فالحاصل أن الإبراد أفضل مطلقاً. وجزم في السراج بأن التخصيص بهذه الأشياء مذهب أصحابنا، وردّه في البحر بأنه مخالف للمعتبرات والظاهر أن محل الاستحباب ان لم تفته الجماعة أول الوقت وإلا قدّمه لأنها إما سنة أكيدة أو واجبة فلا تترك لمستحب إلا أن الإمام حينئذ فاته المستحب قوله : (فإن شدة الحر من قيح جهنم) عن أبي هريرة مرفوعاً أن النار اشتكت إلى ربها قالت: يا رب أكل بعضي بعضاً فأذن لي أتنفس، فأذن لها بنفسين نفس في الشتاء، ونفس في الصيف، فما وجدتم من برد أو زمهرير فمن نفس جهنم، وما وجدتهم من حر أو حرور و فمن نفس جهنم متفق عليه واللفظ لمسلم وفي الاسبيجابي قوله : ( وفي الربيع والخريف) كذا في القهستاني وبه صرح في مجمع الروايات فما في البحر من قوله : ينبغي الحاق الخريف بالصيف، والربيع بالشتاء وجرى عليه المؤلف في حاشية الدرر مخالف لهذا المنقول، وفي القهستاني عن المستصفى : الصلاة أول الوقت أفضل عندنا إلا إذا تضمن التأخير فضيلة اهـ، وفي الخلاصة آخر الإيمان إن كان عندهم حساب يعرفون به الشتاء والصيف فهو على حسابهم، وإن لم يكن
And isfar for Fajr is mustahab in travel and residence (for men) except in Muzdalifah for the pilgrim, then taghlis is better for them due to the obligatory standing after it there, just as it is always the case for women because it is closer to concealment. And for other than Fajr, waiting until the men finish the congregation is mustahab. And it is mustahab to delay Zuhr in summer in all regions due to his saying: Delay Zuhr, for intense heat is from the blaze of Hell. And Jumu'ah is like Zuhr. And it is mustahab to hasten Zuhr in winter and in spring and autumn because he (peace be upon him) used to hasten Zuhr in cold. Except on a cloudy day, fearing it occurs before its time, then it is mustahab to delay it, for there is no dislike in its time, so delaying does not harm. And it is mustahab to delay Asr in summer and winter because (waiting for a fard) is the cause of the increase. Commentary: (In travel and residence) meaning winter and summer, alone, as a follower, and as an imam. (The obligatory standing after it) meaning to have leisure for the obligatory standing. (As it is always the case for women) and it is said the best for them is to wait in all prayers absolutely, as in an-Nahr from al-Qunyah. (It is mustahab to delay Zuhr in summer) its limit is that those walking to congregations can walk in the shade of walls, as in al-Idah from al-Haqa'iq; and as-Siraj said: such that he prays before the shadow becomes equal to the object. In al-Khazanah: the disliked time for Zuhr is when it enters the time of ikhtilaf, and if he delays until every object's shadow is like it, then it enters the time of ikhtilaf. (In all regions) whether hot or not, whether the heat is intense or not, whether one is alone or an imam, and whether people intend congregation from a far place or not; so the conclusion is that delay is absolutely better. As-Siraj asserted that specification with these things is the madhhab of our companions, but al-Bahr rejected that as contrary to reliable sources; the apparent is that the place of istihbab is if he does not miss the congregation of the first time, otherwise he should pray early, because congregation is either strongly sunnah or obligatory, so it should not be left for a mustahab unless the imam thereby misses the mustahab. (For the intense heat is from the blaze of Hell) from Abu Hurairah marfu' that the fire complained to its Lord saying: O Lord, parts of me devour other parts, so permit me to breathe, so He permitted it two breaths: a breath in winter and a breath in summer, so whatever cold or chill you find is from the breath of Hell, and whatever heat or hot wind you find is from the breath of Hell. Agreed upon, and the wording is Muslim's, and in a narration of Bukhari: The most severe heat you find is from its deadly heat, and the most severe cold you find is from its extreme cold. (And Jumu'ah is like Zuhr) in origin and istihbab regarding the two times, mentioned by al-Isbijabi. (In spring and autumn) as in al-Qahistani and he stated it clearly in Majma' ar-Riwayat; what is in al-Bahr recommending joining autumn with summer and spring with winter is contrary to this transmitted view, and in al-Qahistani from al-Mustasfa: Prayer at the beginning of the time is better according to us unless the delay includes a virtue. End. In al-Khulasah: if they have a calculation with which they know winter and summer, it is based on their calculation, otherwise...
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the matn and its commentary on the preferred times for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr prayers. The matn states that isfar (delay until light) for Fajr is mustahab for men in all situations except for pilgrims in Muzdalifah, where taghlis (praying in darkness) is better because they need to proceed to 'Arafat for the essential standing. Women are recommended to pray in darkness always for concealment. For other prayers, waiting until men finish the congregational prayer is mustahab. For Zuhr, it is mustahab to delay (ibrad) in summer in all regions, supported by the hadith that intense heat is from the blaze of Hell. Jumu'ah follows the same ruling as Zuhr. In winter, spring, and autumn, it is mustahab to pray Zuhr early, as the Prophet used to do in cold weather. On cloudy days, one should delay Zuhr to ensure it is not prayed before its time. Asr is always mustahab to delay, both in summer and winter, because waiting for the next fard prayer increases reward. The commentary clarifies various points: the ruling applies in all circumstances; the limit of ibrad is when one can walk in shade; the general principle is that delaying Zuhr in summer is absolutely better unless it causes one to miss the congregational prayer of the first time, in which case congregation takes priority. The commentary also cites disagreements among later scholars regarding the seasons and calculation of times.

Key Terms
إبراد (ibrād): Delaying the Zuhr prayer until the intensity of the heat subsides.
تغليس (taghlīs): Praying Fajr in darkness before dawn breaks.
وقت الاختيار (waqt al-ikhtiyār): The preferred time for prayer as opposed to the allowed (jawaz) time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which situation is taghlis (praying in darkness) recommended for Fajr according to the Hanafi school?
A) For all men in winter
B) For pilgrims in Muzdalifah
C) For women in all prayers
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school carefully balances textual evidence and practical considerations to determine preferred prayer times, ensuring reward without compromising communal obligations.

Rulings on the Time of Asr Prayer
Ruling on Asr timing with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on delaying Asr prayer until the sun changes color and identify when hastening is recommended.

Core Idea
Delaying Asr until the sun changes is prohibitively disliked; hastening on a cloudy day is recommended.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the timing of Asr prayer. Drawing from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, we will explore the hadith condemning the 'prayer of the hypocrites' and understand why delaying until the sun's colour changes is makruh tahriman, while a slight delay before change is permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of delaying Asr prayer until a specific time. The ruling is that delaying until the sun changes is makruh tahriman.
Note that performing Asr at that time is not disliked because it is commanded.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'That is the prayer of the hypocrites...' which strongly condemns delaying until the sun becomes yellow.
This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but its dalala is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'sits until the sun becomes yellow' indicates the disliked time, and the comparison to hypocrisy indicates strong dislike.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars held that performing Asr at that time is also disliked, but the correct view is that it is not disliked because it is commanded.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied upon position is that delaying until change is makruh tahriman, but performing it then is not disliked. Hastening on a cloudy day is mustahabb.
