الناهي في صلاة الفجر، وترجيح المحرم على المبيح إنما هو عند عدم ورود القياس أما عنده فالترجيح له على أنه أجاب في الأسرار بأن حديث النهي متأخر لأنه أبداً يطرأ على الأصل الثابت ولأن الصحابة رضي الله
The Book of Prayer. (Entering into them) i.e., the disliked times: first (at sunrise until it rises) and becomes white the measure of a spear or two spears; (and) the second (at its zenith in the middle of the sky until it declines) i.e., inclines towards the west; (and) the third (at its yellowness and weakness until the eye can look at it until it sets) due to the saying of Uqba ibn Amir, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Three times the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, forbade us to pray in them and to bury our dead: at sunrise until it rises, at its zenith until it declines, and when it inclines to set until it sets' narrated by Muslim. What is meant by his saying 'to bury our dead' is the funeral prayer, for burial is not disliked, so it is a metaphor for it due to the association between them. And it has been interpreted by the Sunnah: the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, forbade us to pray over our dead at three times: at sunrise, etc. And if the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer, it becomes invalid, and his ablution is not broken by loud laughter after it. And according to the view that it turns invalidating, we do not forbid lazy commoners from Fajr prayer at the time of sunrise, because they might abandon it altogether, and validity according to a mujtahid's opinion is preferable to abandonment. (And it is valid to perform what was obligatory) ... peace, and he is required to prostrate for forgetfulness but he does not prostrate for forgetfulness, and it is dropped because it was obligatory complete so it is not performed in an incomplete [prayer]. And in al-Qunyah: the prostration of thanks is disliked at a time when supererogatory prayer is disliked, not otherwise. And in al-Mi'raj: what is done after prayer of prostration is disliked by consensus, because the common people believe it is obligatory or sunnah. His saying: (the measure of a spear) estimated with it originally. In al-Idah: the limit of the first and third is that the eye is not dazzled by the eye, that is correct. And the meaning of the third is the time of sunset. His saying: (and the second at its zenith) and its sign is that the shadow stops shortening and does not begin lengthening. If it happens that he begins at that time an obligatory makeup prayer or before it, and this small part coincides with something of the prayer before the sitting of the amount of tashahhud, it becomes invalid. His saying: (and to bury our dead) i.e., in them. His saying: (and at its zenith) i.e., near its zenith, which is the time of its being overhead, so the meaning is at its zenith until it declines. His saying: (and when it inclines to set) the meaning of 'tudeef' is 'it inclines'; it is with a double-topped letter and a dotted dad, both open, and a heavy ya under, originally 'tatadayyaf', one of the two ta's was dropped for lightness. His saying: (and what is meant, etc.) Abu Dawud interpreted it in the literal sense, and the prohibition is not due to a deficiency in the time, but it is like other times; the deficiency is only in performing the pillars because doing so in it entails imitation of the worship of the disbelievers, and this is not like leaving a wajib in it, for that does not affect a deficiency in the pillars, nor like praying on another's land, because the connection of the action with time is stronger, unlike place. His saying: (and has been interpreted) i.e., this meaning according to the sunnah, and the narrator is the same. His saying: (becomes invalid) And from Abu Yusuf it does not become invalid, but he waits until the sun rises and completes it. Hamawi from Kashf al-Usul mentioned by al-Sayyid. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf also the permissibility of Fajr if delaying it until sunrise was not intentional. His saying: (and according to the view that it turns invalid, etc.) is the statement of the Imam and Abu Yusuf, may Allah be pleased with them, as in al-Burhan. They said: sending blessings upon the Prophet, supplication, and glorification in the disliked times are better than reciting the Qur'an, and perhaps because recitation is a pillar of prayer and it is disliked, so it is better to leave what is a pillar for it. Bahar. His saying: (with karahah) i.e., tahrimiyyah, because it is known that a prohibitory ruling from a zanni al-thubut [source]...

The Book of Prayer: In them, i.e., the three times, but with karahah (according to the apparent narration) like a funeral prayer that has arrived and a prostration of a verse that has been recited in them, and a supererogatory prayer that one has begun, or a vow that one intends to pray in them; he cuts off and makes up fully according to the apparent narration. But if it (the time) passes, it is valid just as the Asr of the day is valid by performing it (at the time of sunset) due to the persistence of its cause, which is the part. The funeral prayer is permissible with... what is diverted from its requirement indicates karahah tahrimiyyah as in al-Minhah. And in al-Bahr from al-Tuhfah: it is better to pray over a funeral that has arrived in those times and not delay it. Rather, in al-Idah and al-Tabyin, delaying is disliked due to his saying: 'Three things should not be delayed: a funeral that has come, a debt when you find what to pay it with, and a bachelor when a suitable match is found.' His saying: (according to the apparent narration) not as some thought and negated it. Said in al-Sharh: and you have known what is in al-Bahr from al-Tuhfah and what is in al-Idah and al-Tabyin. His saying: (like a funeral etc.) Said in al-Bahr: The apparent equality between the funeral prayer and the prostration of recitation is that if the funeral had arrived outside the disliked time and he delayed it until he prayed in the disliked time, then it is not valid and must be repeated like the prostration of recitation. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that the prayer is valid with karahah and he does not repeat it, unlike the prostration of recitation. His saying: (and a supererogatory prayer he began) because performing it is obligatory due to having begun it. His saying: (he cuts off and makes up fully) its apparent meaning is that it is obligatory, because it is in contrast to karahah tahrimiyyah. His saying: (the persistence of its cause, which is the part, etc.) i.e., the effect is established according to the establishment of the cause: if it is complete, then it is complete; if it is incomplete, then it is incomplete. His saying: (with karahah for delaying) As for the act, it is not disliked because it is not correct to establish karahah for something while it is commanded. And its analogy is that making up is not disliked after the time; rather, only missing it is forbidden as in al-Durar. And it was said that performing it is also disliked, and it was supported in al-Bahr by transmission and reasoning. If you ask: why is the Fajr of the day not permissible just as the Asr of the day is permissible? Sadr al-Shari'ah answered: It is mentioned in the principles that the part concurrent with the performance is the cause for the obligation of prayer, and the last part of Asr is incomplete because it is the time of sun worship, so it became obligatory incomplete, and when he performs it as it became obligatory, then if invalidation occurs due to sunset, it is not invalid because it is a time of completion. And Fajr is entirely complete because the sun is not worshipped before its sunrise, so it became obligatory complete. Then if invalidation occurs due to sunrise, it becomes invalid because the time of sunrise is an incomplete time, so he did not perform it as it became obligatory. And his saying 'invalidity' means what is likely to cause invalidity; and his saying 'by sunset' means the state of setting; and his saying 'because it is a time of completion' means sunset in the sense of its complete disappearance, so there is a wordplay. If it is said: this is reasoning in opposition to the text, which is his saying: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the morning prayer before sunrise has caught the morning prayer, and whoever catches a rak'ah of the afternoon prayer before sunset has caught the afternoon prayer' narrated by the two Shaykhs and al-Tahawi. The answer is that when there is a conflict between this hadith and the hadith prohibiting prayer in the three times, we return to analogy as is the rule of conflict. So the analogy favored the ruling of the hadith of the two Shaykhs for Asr prayer, and favored the ruling of the prohibiting hadith for Fajr prayer. And giving preference to the prohibitor over the permissive is only when there is no analogy; but with it, the preference is for it. Moreover, he answered in al-Asrar that the prohibiting hadith is later because it always occurs upon the established principle, and because the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them)...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of prayers during the three disliked times. The author (al-Tahtawi) is explaining the text of Maraqi al-Falah. He begins by defining the three times: when the sun is rising until it rises about a spear's length, when it is at its zenith until it declines, and when it becomes yellow and weak until it sets. The proof is the hadith of 'Uqba ibn Amir recorded by Muslim. The commentator clarifies that the phrase 'bury our dead' in the hadith actually refers to the funeral prayer, and that the prohitition is not due to a deficiency in the times themselves but because performing certain prayers in them resembles the worship of disbelievers. He then discusses various rulings: if the sun rises while one is in Fajr prayer, it becomes invalid according to the Imam and Abu Yusuf; commoners should still be encouraged to pray Fajr even if it is at sunrise to avoid total abandonment. He also notes that performing wajib prayers in these times is valid but with karahah tahrimiyyah in the apparent narration. For funeral prayers and sajdah tilawah, they are also valid but with karahah, and there is a difference of opinion on whether they must be repeated if delayed. Jumu'ah and other time-bound prayers that are delayed may be performed. A supererogatory prayer begun in a disliked time must be cut off and made up later, but if the time passes while in it, it may be valid if the cause (the part of time) is complete. The commentary concludes with a detailed comparison between Asr and Fajr: Asr performed at sunset is valid because the last part of Asr is incomplete (due to sun worship) and thus the prayer was performed as it became obligatory, while Fajr performed at sunrise becomes invalid because Fajr was obligatory complete and the time of sunrise is incomplete. This is defended against the hadith about catching a rak'ah by preferring analogy, and also by the claim that the prohibiting hadith is later.

Key Terms
الأوقات المكروهة (al-awqat al-makruhah): The three specific times when prayer is disliked: sunrise, zenith, and sunset as defined in the hadith.
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer that is performed over the deceased. In this passage it is considered valid but makruh during the disliked times.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran. The ruling during disliked times is similar to funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the source text, what is the Hanafi ruling on a supererogatory prayer (nafil) that a person begins during the sunrise time?
A) The prayer is valid and may be completed.
B) The prayer must be cut off and made up later.
C) The prayer is invalid and no make-up is required.
D) The prayer is valid but disliked.

Key Takeaway
Prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset is generally makruh tahrimi, but Fajr becomes invalid if sunrise occurs, while supererogatory prayers begun must be cut off and made up.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
The Fajr vs Asr Dispute: Catching a Rak'ah at Edge of Time
Madhhab dispute and its resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between Fajr and Asr when sunrise/sunset occurs, identify the conflicting hadith, and apply the principle of tarjih using analogy.

Core Idea
Hadith conflict resolved: Asr valid if rak'ah before sunset; Fajr invalid if sunrise occurs.

A hadith says whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught it, implying validity. Yet another hadith prohibits prayer at sunrise. The Hanafi school resolves this apparent contradiction by analyzing the nature of the time periods and giving preference to the prohibitive hadith for Fajr through analogy. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the two conflicting hadiths
One hadith (Uqba ibn Amir) prohibits prayer at sunrise. Another (the two Shaykhs) says whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught the prayer. Identify the apparent conflict.
The conflict is between a general prohibition and a specific allowance.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule for conflicting evidence
When texts conflict, resort to analogy (qiyas) to resolve. Identify the effective cause (illah) in each case.
The principle: prefer the prohibitor over the permissive when supported by analogy.
3
Analyze the analogy for Asr
The last part of Asr time is incomplete because it overlaps with sunset (a time of sun worship). Thus, the obligation becomes incomplete, and performing it as such is valid. The hadith of the two Shaykhs is upheld for Asr.
Incomplete obligation accepts incomplete performance.
4
Analyze the analogy for Fajr
Fajr time is entirely complete (no sun worship before sunrise). If sunrise occurs, the prayer moves into the incomplete time of sunrise, so it is not performed as it was obligated. Hence it becomes invalid. The prohibitive hadith prevails for Fajr.
Complete obligation requires complete time.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If you start Fajr and sunrise occurs before salam, prayer is invalid and must be repeated. For Asr, if you catch one rak'ah before sunset, the prayer is valid even if the sun sets during later rak'ahs.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

The Book of Prayer. (Entering into them) i.e., the disliked times: first (at sunrise until it rises) and becomes white the measure of a spear or two spears; (and) the second (at its zenith in the middle of the sky until it declines) i.e., inclines towards the west; (and) the third (at its yellowness and weakness until the eye can look at it until it sets) due to the saying of Uqba ibn Amir, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Three times the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, forbade us to pray in them and to bury our dead: at sunrise until it rises, at its zenith until it declines, and when it inclines to set until it sets' narrated by Muslim. What is meant by his saying 'to bury our dead' is the funeral prayer, for burial is not disliked, so it is a metaphor for it due to the association between them. And it has been interpreted by the Sunnah: the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, forbade us to pray over our dead at three times: at sunrise, etc. And if the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer, it becomes invalid, and his ablution is not broken by loud laughter after it. And according to the view that it turns invalidating, we do not forbid lazy commoners from Fajr prayer at the time of sunrise, because they might abandon it altogether, and validity according to a mujtahid's opinion is preferable to abandonment. (And it is valid to perform what was obligatory) ... peace, and he is required to prostrate for forgetfulness but he does not prostrate for forgetfulness, and it is dropped because it was obligatory complete so it is not performed in an incomplete [prayer]. And in al-Qunyah: the prostration of thanks is disliked at a time when supererogatory prayer is disliked, not otherwise. And in al-Mi'raj: what is done after prayer of prostration is disliked by consensus, because the common people believe it is obligatory or sunnah. His saying: (the measure of a spear) estimated with it originally. In al-Idah: the limit of the first and third is that the eye is not dazzled by the eye, that is correct. And the meaning of the third is the time of sunset. His saying: (and the second at its zenith) and its sign is that the shadow stops shortening and does not begin lengthening. If it happens that he begins at that time an obligatory makeup prayer or before it, and this small part coincides with something of the prayer before the sitting of the amount of tashahhud, it becomes invalid. His saying: (and to bury our dead) i.e., in them. His saying: (and at its zenith) i.e., near its zenith, which is the time of its being overhead, so the meaning is at its zenith until it declines. His saying: (and when it inclines to set) the meaning of 'tudeef' is 'it inclines'; it is with a double-topped letter and a dotted dad, both open, and a heavy ya under, originally 'tatadayyaf', one of the two ta's was dropped for lightness. His saying: (and what is meant, etc.) Abu Dawud interpreted it in the literal sense, and the prohibition is not due to a deficiency in the time, but it is like other times; the deficiency is only in performing the pillars because doing so in it entails imitation of the worship of the disbelievers, and this is not like leaving a wajib in it, for that does not affect a deficiency in the pillars, nor like praying on another's land, because the connection of the action with time is stronger, unlike place. His saying: (and has been interpreted) i.e., this meaning according to the sunnah, and the narrator is the same. His saying: (becomes invalid) And from Abu Yusuf it does not become invalid, but he waits until the sun rises and completes it. Hamawi from Kashf al-Usul mentioned by al-Sayyid. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf also the permissibility of Fajr if delaying it until sunrise was not intentional. His saying: (and according to the view that it turns invalid, etc.) is the statement of the Imam and Abu Yusuf, may Allah be pleased with them, as in al-Burhan. They said: sending blessings upon the Prophet, supplication, and glorification in the disliked times are better than reciting the Qur'an, and perhaps because recitation is a pillar of prayer and it is disliked, so it is better to leave what is a pillar for it. Bahar. His saying: (with karahah) i.e., tahrimiyyah, because it is known that a prohibitory ruling from a zanni al-thubut [source]...

The Book of Prayer: In them, i.e., the three times, but with karahah (according to the apparent narration) like a funeral prayer that has arrived and a prostration of a verse that has been recited in them, and a supererogatory prayer that one has begun, or a vow that one intends to pray in them; he cuts off and makes up fully according to the apparent narration. But if it (the time) passes, it is valid just as the Asr of the day is valid by performing it (at the time of sunset) due to the persistence of its cause, which is the part. The funeral prayer is permissible with... what is diverted from its requirement indicates karahah tahrimiyyah as in al-Minhah. And in al-Bahr from al-Tuhfah: it is better to pray over a funeral that has arrived in those times and not delay it. Rather, in al-Idah and al-Tabyin, delaying is disliked due to his saying: 'Three things should not be delayed: a funeral that has come, a debt when you find what to pay it with, and a bachelor when a suitable match is found.' His saying: (according to the apparent narration) not as some thought and negated it. Said in al-Sharh: and you have known what is in al-Bahr from al-Tuhfah and what is in al-Idah and al-Tabyin. His saying: (like a funeral etc.) Said in al-Bahr: The apparent equality between the funeral prayer and the prostration of recitation is that if the funeral had arrived outside the disliked time and he delayed it until he prayed in the disliked time, then it is not valid and must be repeated like the prostration of recitation. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that the prayer is valid with karahah and he does not repeat it, unlike the prostration of recitation. His saying: (and a supererogatory prayer he began) because performing it is obligatory due to having begun it. His saying: (he cuts off and makes up fully) its apparent meaning is that it is obligatory, because it is in contrast to karahah tahrimiyyah. His saying: (the persistence of its cause, which is the part, etc.) i.e., the effect is established according to the establishment of the cause: if it is complete, then it is complete; if it is incomplete, then it is incomplete. His saying: (with karahah for delaying) As for the act, it is not disliked because it is not correct to establish karahah for something while it is commanded. And its analogy is that making up is not disliked after the time; rather, only missing it is forbidden as in al-Durar. And it was said that performing it is also disliked, and it was supported in al-Bahr by transmission and reasoning. If you ask: why is the Fajr of the day not permissible just as the Asr of the day is permissible? Sadr al-Shari'ah answered: It is mentioned in the principles that the part concurrent with the performance is the cause for the obligation of prayer, and the last part of Asr is incomplete because it is the time of sun worship, so it became obligatory incomplete, and when he performs it as it became obligatory, then if invalidation occurs due to sunset, it is not invalid because it is a time of completion. And Fajr is entirely complete because the sun is not worshipped before its sunrise, so it became obligatory complete. Then if invalidation occurs due to sunrise, it becomes invalid because the time of sunrise is an incomplete time, so he did not perform it as it became obligatory. And his saying 'invalidity' means what is likely to cause invalidity; and his saying 'by sunset' means the state of setting; and his saying 'because it is a time of completion' means sunset in the sense of its complete disappearance, so there is a wordplay. If it is said: this is reasoning in opposition to the text, which is his saying: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the morning prayer before sunrise has caught the morning prayer, and whoever catches a rak'ah of the afternoon prayer before sunset has caught the afternoon prayer' narrated by the two Shaykhs and al-Tahawi. The answer is that when there is a conflict between this hadith and the hadith prohibiting prayer in the three times, we return to analogy as is the rule of conflict. So the analogy favored the ruling of the hadith of the two Shaykhs for Asr prayer, and favored the ruling of the prohibiting hadith for Fajr prayer. And giving preference to the prohibitor over the permissive is only when there is no analogy; but with it, the preference is for it. Moreover, he answered in al-Asrar that the prohibiting hadith is later because it always occurs upon the established principle, and because the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them)...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of prayers during the three disliked times. The author (al-Tahtawi) is explaining the text of Maraqi al-Falah. He begins by defining the three times: when the sun is rising until it rises about a spear's length, when it is at its zenith until it declines, and when it becomes yellow and weak until it sets. The proof is the hadith of 'Uqba ibn Amir recorded by Muslim. The commentator clarifies that the phrase 'bury our dead' in the hadith actually refers to the funeral prayer, and that the prohitition is not due to a deficiency in the times themselves but because performing certain prayers in them resembles the worship of disbelievers. He then discusses various rulings: if the sun rises while one is in Fajr prayer, it becomes invalid according to the Imam and Abu Yusuf; commoners should still be encouraged to pray Fajr even if it is at sunrise to avoid total abandonment. He also notes that performing wajib prayers in these times is valid but with karahah tahrimiyyah in the apparent narration. For funeral prayers and sajdah tilawah, they are also valid but with karahah, and there is a difference of opinion on whether they must be repeated if delayed. Jumu'ah and other time-bound prayers that are delayed may be performed. A supererogatory prayer begun in a disliked time must be cut off and made up later, but if the time passes while in it, it may be valid if the cause (the part of time) is complete. The commentary concludes with a detailed comparison between Asr and Fajr: Asr performed at sunset is valid because the last part of Asr is incomplete (due to sun worship) and thus the prayer was performed as it became obligatory, while Fajr performed at sunrise becomes invalid because Fajr was obligatory complete and the time of sunrise is incomplete. This is defended against the hadith about catching a rak'ah by preferring analogy, and also by the claim that the prohibiting hadith is later.

Key Terms
الأوقات المكروهة (al-awqat al-makruhah): The three specific times when prayer is disliked: sunrise, zenith, and sunset as defined in the hadith.
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer that is performed over the deceased. In this passage it is considered valid but makruh during the disliked times.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran. The ruling during disliked times is similar to funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the source text, why does the Hanafi school rule that Fajr is invalid if sunrise occurs, while Asr is valid if a rak'ah is caught before sunset?
A) Because the prohibition hadith is stronger in transmission for Fajr.
B) Because the last part of Asr time is incomplete due to sun worship, making the obligation incomplete, while Fajr's time is entirely complete.
C) Because the hadith of the two Shaykhs is only applicable to Asr.
D) Because Abu Yusuf ruled that Fajr is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the conflict between the prohibition hadith and the 'catching a rak'ah' hadith by using analogy: Asr's incomplete time allows validity, while Fajr's complete time makes it invalid if sunrise occurs.

Funeral Prayer and Nafl in Makruh Times
Rulings on specific prayers during prohibited times with qiyas resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing funeral prayer, sajdat al-tilawa, and voluntary prayers during the three disliked times, and explain the qiyas-derived distinction between Asr and Fajr when performed at their boundaries.

Core Idea
A voluntary prayer started in a disliked time must be cut and completed later; funeral prayer and sajda are allowed but disliked.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies the Hanafi position on which prayers are valid during the prohibited times of sunrise, sunset, and zenith. It distinguishes between obligatory duties (funeral prayer) and voluntary acts, and resolves an apparent conflict between two hadiths through qiyas. Understanding this will refine your ability to apply usul al-fiqh when textual evidence appears contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
List the rulings for: (1) funeral prayer, (2) sajdat al-tilawa, and (3) voluntary prayer (nafl) when these are performed during the three disliked times. Note whether they are permissible, disliked, or invalid.
The passage mentions these in sequence.
2
Trace the dalil for each ruling
For funeral/sajda, the proof is the general permissibility with karahah from the texts. For nafl, the proof is that starting a nafl makes it wajib to complete, but the prohibition-level dislike of the time overrides, so it must be cut and made up. Confirm the hadith of 'catching a rak'ah' for Asr.
The hadith is cited in the resolution.
3
Analyze the qiyas resolution of the conflict
Examine the apparent conflict between the hadith allowing prayer caught at the boundary and the hadith prohibiting prayer at those times. The Hanafi response uses qiyas based on the nature of the time (complete vs. deficient) to give preference to one hadith over the other.
This demonstrates the principle: when texts conflict, qiyas is used for tarjih.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Recall al-Asbijabi's view that funeral prayer in a disliked time is not repeated, unlike sajda. Understand that the mufta bihi position is that both are valid with karahah and not repeated.
This is a minor difference within the school.
5
Summarize the practical application
Consolidate: If a funeral arrives during a disliked time, pray it immediately (makruh but better than delay). If you start a nafl, cut it and complete it later as a complete prayer. If you perform Asr at sunset, it is valid; if you perform Fajr at sunrise, it is invalid.
This summarizes the practical outcomes.

الجنازة تجوز مع المصروف عن مقتضاه يفيد كراهة التحريم كما في المنح، وفي البحر عن التحفة الأفضل ان يصلي على جنازة حضرت في تلك الأوقات ولا يؤخرها بل في الإيضاح والتبيين التأخير مكروه لقوله : «ثلاث لا يؤخرن جنازة أتت ودين وجدت ما يقضيه وبكر وجد لها كفء . قوله : (في ظاهر الرواية) لا كما ظنه بعضهم فنفاها قاله في الشرح وقد علمت ما في البحر عن التحفة وما في الإيضاح والتبيين. قوله : (كجنازة الخ) قال في البحر، وظاهر التسوية بين صلاة الجنازة، وسجدة التلاوة أنه لو حضرت الجنازة في غير وقت مكروه فأخرها حتى صلى في الوقت المكروه فإنها لا تصح وتجب إعادتها كسجدة التلاوة، وذكر الأسبيجابي أن صلاة الكراهة ولا يعيدها بخلاف سجدة التلاوة قوله: (ونافلة شرع فيها) فإن أداءها واجب بسبب الشروع فيها. قوله : فيقطع ويقضي في (كامل) ظاهره أنه على سبيل الوجوب لأنه في مقابلة الكراهة التحريمية قوله : (البقاء سببه وهو الجزء الخ) أي والمسبب يثبت بحسب ثبوت السبب إن كان كاملاً فكامل وإن كان ناقصاً فناقص. قوله: (مع الكراهة للتأخير) وأما الفعل، فلا يكره لعدم إستقامة إثبات الكراهة للشيء مع كونه مأموراً به ونظيره القضاء لا يكره فعله بعد الوقت، وإنما يحرم تفويته كما في الدرر ، وقيل الأداء مكروه أيضاً، وأيده في البحر بالنقل والاستدلال، فإن قلت: لم لا يجوز فجر يومه كما جاز عصر يومه أجاب عنه صدره الشريعة بأنه ذكر في الأصول أن الجزء المقارن للأداء هو السبب لوجوب الصلاة، وآخر وقت العصر ناقص إذ هو وقت عبادة الشمس فوجب ناقصاً فإذا أداه أداء كما وجب فإذا اعترض الفساد بالغروب لا تفسد لأنه وقت كمال والفجر كله وقت كامل لأن الشمس لا تعبد قبل وقت طلوعها فوجب كاملاً، فإذا اعترض الفساد بالطلوع تفسد لأن وقت الطلوع وقت ناقص، فلم يؤدها كما وجبت وقوله الفساد أي ما شأنه الفساد وقوله : بالغروب المراد به حال السقوط، وقوله لأنه وقت كمال أي الغروب بمعنى تمامه ففيه استخدام، فإن قيل هذا تعليل في مقابلة النص وهو قوله : (من أدرك ركعة من الصبح قبل أن تطلع الشمس فقد أدرك الصبح ومن أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر» رواه الشيخان، والطحاوي أجيب بأنه لما وقع التعارض بين هذا الحديث، وبين حديث النهي عن الصلاة في الأوقات الثلاثة رجعنا إلى القياس كما هو حكم التعارض فرجح القياس حكم حديث الشيخين في صلاة العصر، ورجح حكم الحديث الناهي في صلاة الفجر، وترجيح المحرم على المبيح إنما هو عند عدم ورود القياس أما عنده فالترجيح له على أنه أجاب في الأسرار بأن حديث النهي متأخر لأنه أبداً يطرأ على الأصل الثابت ولأن الصحابة رضي الله
المتصل به الأداء من الوقت (مع الكراهة) للتأخير المنهي عنه لا لذات الوقت بخلاف عصر مضى للزومه كاملاً بخروج وقته فلا يؤدي في ناقص
The book of prayer: In these three times, (it is permissible) but with dislike (karahah) in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah): (like a funeral that has arrived, and a prostration of a verse recited therein). And a voluntary prayer that one has commenced, or vowed to pray in these times, he should cut it and complete it as a complete prayer in the apparent transmission. If it passes by him, it is valid, just as the Asr of the day is valid by its performance (at sunset) due to the remaining of its cause, which is the part... The funeral prayer is permissible with the diverted from its requirement, which indicates prohibition-level dislike (karahah tahrim) as in al-Manh. And in al-Bahr from al-Tuhfa: the better is to pray the funeral prayer that arrives in those times and not delay it; rather in al-Idah and al-Tabyin, delaying is disliked because of his statement: 'Three things should not be delayed: a funeral that arrives, a debt that one finds means to pay, and an unmarried woman who finds a compatible match.' His statement: (in the apparent transmission) not as some thought and denied it, as stated in the commentary. And you have known what is in al-Bahr from al-Tuhfa and what is in al-Idah and al-Tabyin. His statement: (like a funeral...) He said in al-Bahr: the apparent equality between the funeral prayer and the prostration of recitation is that if a funeral arrives at a non-disliked time and one delays it until praying it in the disliked time, it is not valid and must be repeated, like the prostration of recitation. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that the prayer with dislike is not repeated, unlike the prostration of recitation. His statement: (and a voluntary prayer that one has commenced) because its performance becomes obligatory due to commencing it. His statement: (he should cut it and complete it as a complete prayer) its apparent meaning is that it is obligatory, because it is in contrast to the prohibition-level dislike. His statement: (the cause remains, which is the part...) i.e., the effect is established according to the establishment of the cause: if it is complete, then complete; if it is deficient, then deficient. His statement: (with dislike for the delay) as for the act itself, it is not disliked because it is not suitable to establish dislike for something that is commanded. Its parallel is that making up a prayer after its time is not disliked, only missing it is forbidden, as in al-Durar. And it is said that the performance is also disliked, and this was supported in al-Bahr by transmission and proof. If you say: why is the Fajr of the same day not valid like the Asr of the same day? Sadr al-Shariah answered that it is mentioned in al-Usul that the part contemporaneous with performance is the cause for the obligation of prayer. The end of Asr time is deficient because it is the time of worship of the sun, so it is obligatory deficiently. When one performs it as it was obligated, if corruption (sunset) occurs, it does not become invalid because it is a time of completeness. Fajr is entirely a complete time because the sun is not worshipped before its rising, so it is obligatory completely. If corruption (sunrise) occurs, it becomes invalid because the time of sunrise is a deficient time, so one has not performed it as it was obligated. And his word 'corruption' means that which is characterized by corruption. His word 'at sunset' means at the moment of setting. His word 'because it is a time of completeness' means sunset in the sense of its completion, so there is use of the same word in different senses. If it is said: this is reasoning in opposition to the text, which is his statement: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr' (narrated by al-Shaykhan and al-Tahawi). The answer is that when there is conflict between this hadith and the hadith prohibiting prayer in the three times, we resort to analogy (qiyas), as is the rule for conflicting proofs. The analogy gave preference to the ruling of the hadith of al-Shaykhan for Asr prayer, and gave preference to the ruling of the prohibiting hadith for Fajr prayer. Preference of the prohibitor over the permitter is only when there is no analogy; here there is analogy, so preference is for it. Moreover, he answered in al-Asrar that the prohibiting hadith is later, because it always arises upon the established principle, and because the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) acted upon it. The part connected to it is the performance from the time (with dislike) for the delayed prohibited action, not for the time itself. Unlike the Asr that has passed, because it becomes due completely at the exit of its time, so it is not performed in a deficient time.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah. It addresses the permissibility of funeral prayer (salat al-janaza) and prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa) during the three disliked times (sunrise, sunset, zenith). These prayers are allowed with karahah (dislike), and in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) this is a ruling. The commentary clarifies that the better view is to not delay the funeral prayer even in these times, as delaying is itself disliked. There is a dispute: some say such prayers are invalid if delayed until the disliked time, while others say they are valid but disliked. The passage then discusses voluntary prayers (nawafil) started in these times: it is wajib to cut them and complete them as complete prayers later. If one does not cut them and continues, the prayer becomes valid (like the Asr of the same day performed at sunset). The reason for the validity of Asr at sunset is that the cause—a part of the time—remains, though with karahah. The passage then contrasts this with Fajr: if one performs Fajr at sunrise, it becomes invalid because the entire time of Fajr is complete, and sunrise is a defective time for prayer. This explanation is based on qiyas (analogy) and resolves a conflict between two hadiths: the hadith of 'catching a rak'ah' and the hadith prohibiting prayer at these times. For Asr, the catching hadith is given preference; for Fajr, the prohibition is given preference. This is a key Hanafi jurisprudential ruling demonstrating the use of qiyas when texts conflict.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahrim): A level of dislike that is near to prohibition, requiring cutting of the action and making it up completely.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, forming the primary authoritative source within the Hanafi school.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer; here, completing the cut nafl as a complete prayer (kamil) outside the disliked time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what should a person do if they start a voluntary prayer during the time of sunrise?
A) Continue the prayer as normal, as it is permissible.
B) Cut the prayer immediately and complete it later as a complete prayer.
C) Finish the prayer quickly before the sun fully rises.
D) Cancel the prayer entirely without any make-up.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawa in disliked times with karahah, but a voluntary prayer started therein must be cut and completed later; conflicting hadiths on the boundary times are resolved by qiyas based on the nature of the time.

Voluntary Prayers in Prohibited Times: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Friday Noon
General rule with intra-Hanafi exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers during the three prohibited times and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Friday noon.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayers are makruh tahrimi in the three prohibited times, even with a cause—except Friday noon according to Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi presents a clear rule: all voluntary prayers are prohibited in the three disliked times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). However, an intra-Hanafi dispute arises over Friday noon. Some scholars, including Abu Yusuf, make an exception based on a hadith variant. This lesson will clarify the ruling, its basis, and the practical implication of the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited times and the general ruling
The three times are sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The ruling is that voluntary prayers (nawafil) are makruh tahrimi (prohibition-level disliked) during these times.
The ruling applies even if the prayer has a specific cause (sabab).
2
Include all types of voluntary prayers
The text explicitly includes prayers with a cause: vowed prayers, tawaf rak'ahs, wudu rak'ahs, greeting of the mosque, and regular sunan. None are exempt.
This reinforces the generality of the prohibition.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's exception for Friday noon
Abu Yusuf held that voluntary prayers at Friday noon (the time of zenith) are not disliked, based on an exception found in some chains of the hadith of Uqba.
Al-Kamal and al-Hawi al-Qudsi strengthen this view, and the fatwa is upon it.
4
Understand the dispute and the tarjih
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider the exception a strange addition (ziyada ghariba) and thus reject it. However, the text gives tarjih to Abu Yusuf's opinion for fatwa.
This shows how hadith authenticity and usul principles interact within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأوقات الثلاثة) المذكورة (يكره فيها النافلة كراهة تحريم ولو كان لها سبب كالمنذور، وركعتي الطواف وركعتي الوضوء وتحية المسجد والسنن الرواتب وفي مكة، وقال أبو يوسف لا تكره النافلة حال الإستواء يوم الجمعة لأنه استثنى في حديث عقبة قواه الكمال وفي الحاوي القدسي، وعليه الفتوى قوله: (لأنه استثنى في حديث عقبة) الوارد في الأوقات المنهية وقد تقدم والمراد أنه ورد في بعض طرقه إستنثاء يوم الجمعة من المنهيات، ولهما أنها زيادة غريبة، فلا يعتد بها اهـ
(And the three times) mentioned, (voluntary prayer is disliked in them with prohibition-level dislike), even if it has a cause, such as the vowed prayer, the two rak'ahs of tawaf, the two rak'ahs of wudu, the greeting of the mosque, the regular sunan, and in Mecca. And Abu Yusuf said: voluntary prayer is not disliked at the time of zenith on Friday, because an exception was made in the hadith of Uqba. Al-Kamal strengthened it, and in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, and the fatwa is upon it. His statement: (because an exception was made in the hadith of Uqba) which came in the prohibited times and has preceded. The meaning is that in some of its chains, an exception for Friday from the prohibited times occurs. But for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is a strange addition, so it is not to be considered. End.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage states a general rule: voluntary prayers (nawafil) are makruh tahrim (prohibition-level dislike) in the three prohibited times—sunrise, sunset, and zenith. This includes all voluntary prayers, even those with a specific cause (sabab) like a nazr (vow), the two rak'ahs of tawaf, the two rak'ahs after wudu, tahiyyat al-masjid, the regular sunan (rawatib), and even in Mecca. The only exception mentioned is from Abu Yusuf, who held that at noon on Friday, voluntary prayer is not disliked, based on an exception in the hadith of Uqba (which lists the prohibited times but excludes Friday noon). The commentator notes that this opinion is supported by Kamal and in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, and the fatwa is given accordingly. However, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) consider this exception a strange (gharib) addition to the hadith and therefore not reliable. This intra-Hanafi dispute shows the difference in accepting hadith variants. The relied-upon position for fatwa according to this text is that of Abu Yusuf, but the school's major position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that all voluntary prayers are disliked at these times, including Friday noon.

Key Terms
نافلة (nafila): Voluntary supererogatory prayer, excluding obligatory prayers (fard) and funeral prayer.
سبب (sabab): A specific reason that normally makes a prayer recommendable, such as a vow, tawaf, wudu, or mosque entry.
زيادة غريبة (ziyada ghariba): A strange addition to a hadith text (matn) that is not accepted as reliable by the majority of hadith scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), is it permissible to pray tahiyyat al-masjid during the time of sunset?
A) Yes, it is permissible because it has a cause.
B) No, it is makruh tahrimi and must not be performed.
C) Yes, but only if one has not prayed Asr yet.
D) No, it is haram and invalid.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayers are makruh tahrimi in the three prohibited times, with the exception of Friday noon according to Abu Yusuf, and the fatwa follows his view.

Ruling on Voluntary Prayers After Fajr and After Asr
Prohibition of voluntary prayers after Fajr (beyond sunnah) and after Asr, with exception for Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr, identify the exceptions, and state the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayers after Fajr (beyond its sunnah) and after Asr are makruh tanzihi, with only the two sunnah of Fajr as an exception.

This passage clarifies a common point of confusion: when can one perform voluntary prayers after the fard prayers? The ruling is based on a clear hadith and the wisdom of prioritizing the fard. The Hanafi school classifies it as makruh tanzihi, not haram, because an exception exists. Understanding this ruling helps avoid disliked actions and ensures proper reverence for the obligatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? State the hukm level (makruh tanzihi) for voluntary prayers after Fajr time (beyond the two sunnah) and after Asr prayer.
The ruling applies to any voluntary prayer, including those with a cause like tahiyyat al-masjid.
2
Locate the dalil
What is the evidence cited? Identify the hadith: 'لا صلاة بعد الصبح إلا ركعتين' (no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs).
The hadith is ahad, providing zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit exception of two rak'ahs (the sunnah of Fajr) implies that any other prayer is not allowed. The Hanafi school interprets this as dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah) rather than prohibition.
The use of 'لا صلاة' (no prayer) is general but the exception shows the ruling is advisory.
4
Understand the hikmah
Why is this disliked? To ensure the time is occupied with the fard in effect, and to lighten the sunnah so the fard is not delayed.
The wisdom reinforces the priority of the obligatory prayer.
5
Apply the exception
What is the exception? The two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr are allowed before the fard. After the fard, no voluntary prayer is allowed, even if one missed the sunnah with an excuse.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding: making up missed sunnah after fard is still disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويكره التنقل بعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر من سنته) قبل أداء الفرض لقوله : ليبلغ شاهدكم غائبكم ألا لا صلاة بعد الصبح إلا ركعتين وليكون جميع الوقت مشغولاً بالفرض حكماً، ولذا تخفف قراءة سنة الفجر (و) يكره التنفل (بعد صلاته أي فرض الصبح ولو سنة سواء تركها بعذر أو بدونه قوله : (وبعد صلاة فرض العصر) ولو المجموعة بعرفة كما نقله الكمال عن بعضهم ونقله الزاهدي في القنية عن مجد الأئمة
His statement: (And voluntary movement after dawn [Fajr time] beyond its sunnah is disliked) before performing the obligatory prayer, because of his statement: 'Let the present convey to the absent: there is no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs.' And so that all the time is occupied with the obligatory prayer in effect. Hence the recitation in the sunnah of Fajr is lightened. (And) voluntary movement is disliked (after his prayer, i.e., the obligatory Fajr prayer, even if a sunnah, whether one leaves it with an excuse or without). His statement: (And after the obligatory Asr prayer), even if it is the combined prayer at Arafah, as al-Kamal transmitted from some, and al-Zahidi in al-Qunyah transmitted from Majd al-Aimmah.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and after Asr. It is makruh (disliked) to perform voluntary prayers (tanafful) after the time of Fajr begins (i.e., after true dawn) except for the two sunnah rak'ahs of Fajr itself. This applies before performing the Fajr fard. The proof is the hadith: 'Let the present convey to the absent: there is no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs' (i.e., the sunnah of Fajr). The wisdom is to ensure that the time is effectively occupied with the fard prayer, and to make the sunnah light (by shortening its recitation) so that the fard is not delayed. After performing the Fajr fard, it is also makruh to pray any voluntary prayer (including the two sunnah if one missed them), whether one has an excuse or not. Similarly, after Asr prayer, it is makruh to pray voluntary prayers, even if the Asr was performed in combination at Arafah (as during Hajj). The exception is the two sunnah of Asr? Actually, the text does not explicitly exempt the two sunnah of Asr here, but there is a known exception for the two rak'ahs before Asr? In the Hanafi school, the two sunnah of Asr are also performed before Asr, not after. So after Asr, there is no sunnah. The text mentions 'after his prayer' meaning after the fard. So the ruling is that no voluntary prayer is allowed after Asr, whether it has a cause or not, except for the two sunnah of Fajr (which are before Fajr, not after). This is a clear application of the prohibition of praying after the fard prayers of Fajr and Asr.

Key Terms
التنقل (al-tanafful): Performing voluntary prayers (nawafil). In this context, it refers to any voluntary prayer other than the two sunnah of Fajr.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah that are prayed before the Fajr fard; these are the exception to the prohibition.
المجموعة بعرفة (al-majmu'a bi-Arafah): The combined prayers (Zuhr and Asr) performed at Arafah during Hajj. Even in this case, the ruling applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the ruling on performing two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid after performing the Fajr prayer?
A) Permissible because tahiyyat al-masjid has a cause.
B) Disliked (makruh) because no voluntary prayers are allowed after Fajr except the sunnah of Fajr before it.
C) Recommended, as it is a sunnah to enter the mosque.
D) Haram, as it is strictly prohibited.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that voluntary prayers after Fajr (except the two sunnah) and after Asr are makruh tanzihi, based on the hadith and the principle of prioritizing the fard.

Disliked Times for Nawafil and Abu Yusuf's Exception for Jumu'ah
Explanation of the three disliked times and the ruling on nawafil with sabab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three disliked times for supererogatory prayers and explain the Hanafi ruling, including the intra-madhhab difference on Friday at zenith, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Nawafil are makruh tahriman at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, except at zenith on Friday according to the mufta bihi view.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah explains the ruling on supererogatory prayers during the three prohibited times. It clarifies that the prohibition is due to resemblance to disbelievers' worship, not the time itself, and presents an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf exempts Friday at zenith based on an exception in a hadith, and this view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three disliked times and the ruling
Locate the times: sunrise (tulū‘), zenith (istiwā’), and sunset (ghurūb). Note the ruling: nawafil are makruh tahrimi (prohibited dislike).
The text says 'nawafil are disliked with karāha taḥrīmiyya'.
2
Understand the reason for prohibition
The prohibition is not intrinsic to the time but because performing the prayer's actions at these times resembles the worship of sun-worshippers (tashabbuh bi-‘ibādat al-kuffār).
This is mentioned in the commentary (Fath).
3
Analyze the application to regular sunan (rawātib)
The text notes that the regular sunnah of Fajr can be performed at sunrise, but there are no rawātib at zenith or sunset. Missed fard prayers can be made up at these times.
The prohibition applies to nawafil that are not fard or qadā’.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's exception for Friday
Abu Yusuf holds that the prohibition is lifted at the time of zawal (zenith) on Friday, based on an exception in the hadith of ‘Uqbah. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider this addition weak (gharība).
The fatwa (mufta bihi) follows Abu Yusuf, as strengthened by al-Kamal and in al-Ḥāwī al-Qudsī.
5
Determine the operative ruling for practice
According to the relied-upon view, it is not disliked to perform supererogatory prayers at zenith on Friday. At other times (sunrise and sunset), nawafil remain makruh tahrimi.
This is the conclusion of the passage.

Source Text

وعنهم عملت: ظاهر الصحة في به فعلم أنه لاحق قوله : (لا) لذات الوقت فانه وقت كسائر الأوقات إنما النقص أداء الأركان المستلزم فعلها فيه التشبه بعبادة الكفار فتح. قوله : (بخلاف عصره مضى الخ) جواب سؤال حاصله أن ينبغي يجوز بعد الإصفرار قضاء عصر أمس مثلاً لأن الوجوب لما كان في آخر الوقت كان السبب ناقصاً فإذا قضاه في ذلك الوقت من اليوم الثاني فقد أداه كما وجب. قوله : يكره فيها النافلة كراهة تحريم فيجب قطعها والأداء في كامل في الرواية، وقيل: يصح التنفل فيها كالفرائض لأن الدليل يفيد المنع مطلقاً دون عدم البعض بخصوصه قوله : (والسنن الرواتب) كأن يصلي سنة الفجر وقت الطلوع، ولا يظهر في غيرها لأن وقت الإستواء والغروب ليس فيه سنن رواتب وإن كان الفرض قضاء فلا سنة له، ولو أطلق السنن ليشمل الكسوف لكان أولى قوله : (وقال أبو يوسف الخ) قواه الكمال وفي الحاوي القدسي، وعليه الفتوى قوله: (لأنه استثنى في حديث عقبة) الوارد في الأوقات المنهية وقد تقدم والمراد أنه ورد في بعض طرقه إستنثاء يوم الجمعة من المنهيات، ولهما أنها زيادة غريبة، فلا يعتد بها اهـ.
And they acted upon it: apparent correctness in it, so it is known that it is not for the time itself; it is a time like other times; rather, the deficiency is performing the pillars, which requires imitation of the worship of disbelievers. (Fath). His saying: (Unlike the asr that passed, etc.) is an answer to a question: that it should be permissible after yellowing to make up the asr of yesterday, for example, because since the obligation was at the end of the time, the cause was deficient; so if he makes it up at that time on the second day, he performs it as it was obligated. His saying: 'Nafil is disliked there with karahah tahrimiyyah, so it is obligatory to stop it and perform it fully in the narration; and it is said: nafil is valid in them like obligatory prayers because the evidence indicates prohibition absolutely, not the lack of something specific.' His saying: (and the regular sunan) like performing the sunnah of fajr at sunrise, and it does not appear in other than it because there are no regular sunnan at the time of zawal and sunset; and if the obligatory prayer is missed, there is no sunnah for it; and if he had made the sunnah absolute to include eclipse, it would have been better. His saying: (and Abu Yusuf said, etc.) al-Kamal strengthened it, and in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, and the fatwa is upon it. End.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) discussing the ruling on supererogatory prayers during the three disliked times: sunrise, zenith (when the sun is at its meridian), and sunset. The commentator clarifies that the prohibition is not intrinsic to the time itself but because performing the prayer's actions at those times resembles the worship of sun-worshippers. He addresses a potential question about making up a missed asr prayer when the sun has turned yellow: it is permissible because the obligation at that time was deficient. He then states that nafil is disliked with tahrimi prohibition at these times, and if one starts such a prayer, it must be stopped. There is a differing view that it is valid but sinful. The commentator notes that regular sunnah prayers associated with fard prayers (like sunnah of fajr) are only relevant at sunrise; there are no regular sunnan at zawal or sunset. He then presents Abu Yusuf's opinion that the prohibition does not apply on Friday at the time of zawal, based on an exception in the hadith of Uqbah, and notes that this view is relied upon for fatwa, though Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider the exception weak.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريم (karāha taḥrīmiyya): A level of dislike that is close to prohibition; one must stop the action if started, and it is sinful to perform it.
السنن الرواتب (al-sunan al-rawātib): The regularly performed sunnah prayers associated with the five daily obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, it is makruh tahriman because the prohibition is absolute.
B) Yes, it is permissible because of an exception in the hadith of Uqbah.
C) Only if the prayer is for a specific reason like tahiyyat al-masjid.
D) It is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
Nawafil are makruh tahrimi at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, but the mufta bihi exempts Friday at zenith due to a hadith exception.

Dislike of Nafil After Fajr and After Asr
Ruling on supererogatory prayers after Fajr and Asr with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supererogatory prayers after Fajr and Asr, identify the dalil, and explain the Hanafi interpretation of the prohibition.

Core Idea
Supererogatory prayers after Fajr and Asr are makruh tahrimi, but missed obligatory prayers may be made up at those times.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between supererogatory (nafil) prayers and obligatory (fard) prayers when it comes to the times after Fajr and Asr. While the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly forbade prayer at these times, the Hanafi scholars interpret this prohibition as applying only to voluntary prayers, allowing the making up of missed fard prayers. This lesson explores the evidence and the reasoning behind this nuanced position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is: supererogatory prayers after Fajr (beyond the two-rak'ah sunnah) and after Asr are disliked (makruh tahrimi).
The ruling applies to both times equally.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'There is no prayer after Asr until the sun sets, and no prayer after Fajr until the sun rises.' Also a hadith: 'Let the present convey to the absent: Verily no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs.'
These hadith are sahih and serve as the primary proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The explicit prohibition indicates that these times are not for prayer. However, the Hanafis interpret the word 'no prayer' as a prohibition that implies karahah tahrimiyyah, not absolute prohibition (haram).
The key is that the prohibition is not absolute; it allows exceptions.
4
Note the critical refinement
Understand the Hanafi refinement: the prohibition is explained as 'al-nahyu bi-ma‘nā fī ghayr al-waqt' – meaning the time is considered virtually occupied by the fard prayer of that time. This virtual occupation is better than actual supererogatory prayer, so the prohibition applies only to nafil, not to fard (including missed fard).
This refinement allows making up missed fard prayers at these times.
5
Evaluate the thamarah (practical consequence)
Identify the practical impact: a person may make up a missed Zuhr prayer after Asr without any dislike, but performing a voluntary prayer at that time is makruh tahrimi.
Also, the sunnah of Fajr is allowed before the fard, but not after it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويكره التنقل بعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر من سنته) قبل أداء الفرض لقوله : ليبلغ شاهدكم غائبكم ألا لا صلاة بعد الصبح إلا ركعتين وليكون جميع الوقت مشغولاً بالفرض حكماً، ولذا تخفف قراءة سنة الفجر (و) يكره التنفل (بعد صلاته أي فرض الصبح) ولو سنة سواء تركها بعذر أو بدونه (و) يكره التنفل ( بعد صلاة فرض (العصر) وإن لم تتغير الشمس لقوله عليه السلام الا صلاة بعد صلاة العصر حتى تغرب الشمس ولا صلاة بعد صلاة الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس، رواه الشيخان والنهي بمعنى في غير الوقت وهو جعل الوقت كالمشغول فيه بفرض الوقت حكماً وهو أفضل من النفل الحقيقي فلا يظهر في حق فرض يقضيه، وهو المفاد بمفهوم المتن
His saying: (And it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayers after dawn more than its sunnah) before performing the fard, due to his saying: 'Let the present convey to the absent: Verily no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs' so that the entire time is engaged with the fard de jure. Therefore the recitation of the sunnah of Fajr is lightened. (And) it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayers (after his prayer i.e. the fard of Fajr), even if it is a sunnah, whether he left it due to an excuse or without. (And) it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayers (after the fard of Asr), even if the sun has not changed, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'There is no prayer after Asr until the sun sets, and no prayer after Fajr until the sun rises'—related by al-Bukhari and Muslim. The prohibition is in the sense of 'in non-time' (i.e. making the time considered as occupied by the fard de jure), and it is better than actual supererogatory prayer, so it does not appear in the case of a fard to be made up. And this is understood from the implication of the matn.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement explaining the ruling that it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayers after the Fajr prayer beyond its two-rak'ah sunnah, and similarly after Asr prayer even if the sun has not yet turned yellow. The commentator cites the hadith: 'Let those present inform those absent: Verily no prayer after Fajr except two rak'ahs' and the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim prohibiting prayer after Asr until sunset. The commentator explains that the 'prohibition' is not literal; rather, the time is considered as occupied by the obligatory prayer de jure, and this virtual occupation is better than actual supererogatory prayer. Therefore, the prohibition does not apply to making up missed obligatory prayers. This is the meaning derived from the matn's wording 'disliked for supererogatory' implying it is not disliked for fard.

Key Terms
النهي بمعنى في غير الوقت (al-nahyu bi-ma‘nā fī ghayr al-waqt): The prohibition means that the time is considered as if it is not a time for prayer (i.e., the time is virtually occupied by the fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is makruh tahrimi.
B) It is permissible because it is a sunnah.
C) It is haram.
D) It is mustahab.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that supererogatory prayers after Fajr and Asr are makruh tahrimi, but making up missed obligatory prayers is permissible due to the interpretation that the prohibition applies only to voluntary acts.

Disliked Times for Supererogatory Prayers: Before Maghrib, at Khutbah, and at Iqamah
Ruling on supererogatory prayers in three additional situations with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three additional situations in which supererogatory prayer is disliked in the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
No nafil between adhan and iqamah for Maghrib; obligation to listen to khutbah forbids nafil during it.

You already know that supererogatory prayers are encouraged generally, but there are specific times when they are discouraged. In this lesson, we cover three such situations from the Hanafi fiqh text: before Maghrib, when the khatib emerges for the sermon, and at the iqamah of any fard prayer. Each has a clear evidence and rationale, which we will unpack step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three situations
From the Arabic text, list the three cases: (1) before Maghrib, (2) at the emergence of the khatib, (3) at the iqamah for any fard. Note that the dislike is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) in all three.
The text uses 'يكره' which indicates a strong dislike approaching prohibition.
2
Extract the evidence for Maghrib
Locate the hadith: 'Between every two adhans there is a prayer for whoever wills, except Maghrib.' Understand that 'two adhans' means the adhan and iqamah. The exception proves that no nafil is allowed in that interval for Maghrib.
Al-Khattabi's explanation affirms that the exception applies to the Maghrib prayer only.
3
Understand the evidence for khutbah
The text states 'due to the prohibition of it' (لنهي عنه). The dislike arises from the obligation to listen to the sermon (khutbah). Once the khatib appears, the time becomes dedicated to the sermon, so nafil is disliked until the prayer ends.
This applies to all types of sermons: Jumu‘ah, Eid, eclipse, rain prayer, marriage, etc.
4
Understand the evidence for iqamah
At iqamah, the fard prayer is about to start. Engaging in nafil would delay joining the fard, so it is disliked. The same logic applies to Maghrib and during khutbah – the obligation takes priority.
If one has already started a nafil before the khatib emerges, he completes it lightly as two rak'ahs.
5
Apply the ruling
Now consider practical scenarios: entering the mosque for Maghrib just as iqamah is called; arriving during Jumu‘ah khutbah; or standing for iqamah of any fard. State the ruling in each case and the reason.
The mufta bihi is consistent: nafil is makruh tahrimi at these times.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يكره التنقف قبل صلاة المغرب) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: بين كل أذانين صلاة إن شاء إلا المغرب قال الخطابي : يعني الأذان والإقامة (و) يكره التنقل (عند خروج الخطيب من خلوته وظهوره (حتى يفرغ من الصلاة) لنهي عنه سواء فيه خطبة الجمعة والعيدين والكسوف والاستسقاء والنكاح وغيرها فإنه يكره وقته (ويكره عند الإقامة لكل فريضة)
(And) it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayers before Maghrib, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Between every two adhans there is a prayer for whoever wills, except Maghrib.' Al-Khattabi said: He means the adhan and iqamah. (And) it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayers at the emergence of the khatib from his seclusion and his appearance, until he finishes the prayer, due to the prohibition of it. This applies equally to the sermons of Jumu‘ah, the two Eids, eclipse, rain prayer, marriage, and others; it is disliked at that time. (And) it is disliked at the iqamah for every obligatory prayer.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement covering three more situations where supererogatory prayer is disliked. First, before Maghrib: the Prophet said there is a prayer between every adhan and iqamah except for Maghrib, meaning the time between the adhan and iqamah of Maghrib is not for supererogatory prayer; one should immediately pray the fard. Second, when the khatib comes out for the sermon—whether for Jumu‘ah, Eid, eclipse, etc.—it is disliked to pray supererogatory prayers from his emergence until the end of the prayer, because listening to the sermon is obligatory. Third, at the time of iqamah for any fard prayer, it is disliked to start a supererogatory prayer. The commentator notes that if one had started a nafil before the khatib emerged, he should not cut it but complete it lightly as two rak'ahs (or four for Jumu‘ah sunnah).

Key Terms
خروج الخطيب (khurūj al-khaṭīb): The moment when the preacher emerges from his private room (khalwah) to deliver the sermon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it disliked to pray supererogatory prayers before Maghrib?
A) Because the time is very short.
B) Because the Prophet specifically forbade it between the adhan and iqamah of Maghrib.
C) Because it is better to pray the sunnah of Maghrib first.
D) Because Maghrib prayer is very important.

Key Takeaway
Supererogatory prayer is disliked (makruh tahrimi) before Maghrib, when the khatib appears, and at iqamah, based on hadith and the priority of obligations.

Disliked Times for Voluntary Prayers: Comprehensive Hanafi Rulings
Detailed commentary on disliked times for nafl prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on disliked times for voluntary prayers, distinguish between tanzih and tahrim karahah, and apply the exception for Fajr sunnah at iqamah.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer is disliked at iqamah except Fajr sunnah; congregation outweighs nafl when time conflicts.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details several circumstances where performing voluntary (nafl or sunnah) prayers is considered disliked (makruh) in the Hanafi school. Understanding these rulings helps the believer prioritize obligatory and sunnah acts correctly, ensuring that voluntary worship does not compromise higher obligations or cause distraction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each scenario, identify what voluntary act is being ruled and what the ruling (disliked) is. Note the exception for Fajr sunnah at iqamah.
The ruling is makruh tanzih, not haram.
2
Locate the exception
The text specifies that praying at iqamah is disliked for all nafl except the two rak'at of Fajr sunnah, provided one can still join the congregation.
The exception is conditional.
3
Trace the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'Two rak'at of Fajr are better than the world and all it contains' is cited to show the immense virtue of Fajr sunnah.
This hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni evidence.
4
Understand the conflict resolution
When Fajr sunnah and congregation conflict, the Hanafi school gives priority to congregation because it has both promise and threat, while Fajr sunnah has only promise.
This is a key principle: prioritize what has greater evidence.
5
Apply to other disliked times
Recognize that other scenarios (Eid prayer, between sermons at Arafah/Muzdalifah, tight time, repelling impurities, food, distraction) are also ruled makruh tanzih for similar reasons of distraction or neglect of higher duties.
The common thread is that voluntary worship should not interfere with obligations or khushu.

يترك الواجبات، ويقتصر على أدنى ما تجوز به الصلاة كما في المجتبى. قوله : (حال) مدافعة أحد الأخبثين) أي الحصر بأحدهما، والمفاعلة على غير بابها أو هي على بابها لأنها تندفع للخروج وهو يدفعها لداخل. قوله: القضاء والله أعلم.
The Friday, Eid, Hajj, Nikah, Khatm (completion), Khusuf (eclipse), and Istisqa (rain prayer). And it is disliked (at the iqamah) for every fard (obligatory prayer), except the sunnah of Fajr if one is safe from missing the congregation. And it is disliked to perform voluntary prayer (before) the Eid prayer, even if he prays at home, and similarly (after) it, i.e., Eid (in the mosque), i.e., the Eid prayer ground, not at home, according to the choice of the majority, because he (the Prophet) would not pray anything before Eid, and when he returned home he would pray two rak'at. And it is disliked to perform voluntary prayer between the two gatherings at Arafah, even if it is the sunnah of Zuhr, and at Muzdalifah, even if it is the sunnah of Maghrib, according to the correct view, because if he does not perform voluntary prayer between them... And it is disliked (when the time for the obligatory prayer is narrow) due to missing the fard from its time. And it is disliked to perform voluntary prayer like the fard while repelling one of the two impurities (urine and stool), and similarly wind. And at the time of the presence of food that he desires, and at the presence of what distracts the mind from contemplating the greatness of Allah and fulfilling the right of His service, and it is contrary to humility in prayer without necessity because it introduces deficiency in the performance. And Allah is the giver of success. His statement: 'due to missing the fard' means he leaves what is not fard and does what is not upon him, and this is not the action of intelligent people; rather, if the time after it is a time of corruption like the time of sunrise, he leaves the obligatory acts and confines himself to the minimum that makes the prayer valid as in al-Mujtaba. His statement: 'while repelling one of the two impurities' means being constrained by one of them, and the mutual form (mufa'alah) is not its usual form, or it is its usual form because it (the impurity) pushes to exit and he pushes it back. His statement: 'that he desires' means he craves it, for there is distraction in it, and the dislike is if the time is not narrow; otherwise, he gives priority to it and there is no dislike then. His statement: 'and at the presence of all' is a general conjunction. Supplement: From what is connected to disliked acts: dislike of speaking after Fajr until he prays, except for good; and invalidating the sunnah if separated by speech. And there is no harm in walking for a need after the prayer. And it is said: dislike until sunrise, and it is said until its rising high. As for after Isha, some permitted it and others prohibited it. And sleep before it and speech after it were disliked. What is meant by it is that which is not good; and good is realized in speech that is worship, since permissible (mubah) has no good in it just as there is no sin in it; so it is disliked in these times, transmitted by al-Sayyid from al-Nahr. His statement: 'to introduce deficiency in the performance' means doing acts of worship, even if supererogatory, not in exchange for making up (qada). And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (hashiya) on a section of Maraqi al-Falah concerning disliked acts (makruhat) in salah, specifically regarding voluntary prayers at certain times. The author begins by listing types of prayer (Jumu'ah, Eid, Hajj, etc.) then states the ruling: it is disliked to pray nafl at the time of iqamah (the call to commence prayer) for any fard, except the sunnah of Fajr if one is confident of not missing the congregation. The commentary clarifies that 'iqamah' here means the mu'adhdhin's iqamah, not the commencement of the prayer. If one is praying before the iqamah, it is permissible anywhere except in the road. At the time of iqamah, it is disliked to pray anything other than Fajr sunnah according to the majority view. The exception for Fajr sunnah is due to its great virtue; hadith states: 'Two rak'at of Fajr are better than the world and all it contains.' However, if one fears missing the congregational prayer, he should join the imam because congregation has both promise and threat (of punishment), while Fajr sunnah has only promise. The passage also covers the disliked nature of praying before and after Eid prayer in the musalla (but not at home), based on the Prophet's practice. It is also disliked to pray between the two sermons at Arafah and between Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, even if it is the sunnah prayers of those times. Further, it is disliked to pray when the time for fard is tight (so one may miss it), when one needs to relieve oneself, when food is present and desired, or when the mind is preoccupied. The 'tatmah' (appendix) adds that speaking after Fajr until the prayer is disliked unless for good, and similarly after Isha. The overall lesson is that voluntary worship should not compromise the obligatory or recommended acts of higher priority, and one must avoid distraction to maintain khushu'.

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqamah): In this passage, iqamah refers to the call to commence prayer (the second call) made by the mu'adhdhin, not the actual start of the prayer.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'at sunnah prayer before the Fajr fard, which are strongly recommended and have special virtue.
كراهة (karahah): A legal category meaning disliked. In this context, it implies tanzih (not sinful but better to avoid), as the text does not indicate prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) For all voluntary prayers without exception.
B) For all voluntary prayers except the sunnah of Fajr if one fears missing the congregation.
C) Only for the sunnah of Fajr.
D) Only for the sunnah of Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes congregational prayer over voluntary sunnah, and only the Fajr sunnah is exempted from the general dislike of praying at iqamah, and only if one can still join the congregation.
