The Logical Placement of Adhan After Prayer Times
Commentary explaining the ordering of chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the causal relationship between prayer times (sabab) and adhan (i'lam) in Hanafi fiqh, and justify the ordering of chapters in classical fiqh texts.

Core Idea
Adhan is the announcement of a cause; the cause precedes the sign.

This passage opens the chapter on adhan in Maraqi al-Falah. The commentator explains that prayer times are the cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer, while adhan is merely the announcement (i'lam) of those times. Therefore, the chapter on times logically precedes the chapter on adhan. Understanding this ordering reveals the deliberate structure of Hanafi fiqh texts, where causes are presented before their indicators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sabab and the i'lam
Find in the text the terms for the cause (times) and the announcement (adhan). Note how the author explicitly states that times are the cause and adhan is the announcement.
The sabab is the prayer times; the i'lam is the adhan.
2
Analyze the ordering principle
The text says 'قدم السبب على العلامة' — the cause is presented before the sign. Understand why: the sign exists for the sake of the cause.
3
Examine the linguistic analysis of 'A'lam'
The commentator discusses the word 'A'lam' (plural of 'alam, sign) and its different readings (fatha vs. kasra on the hamza). This shows the depth of Qur'anic and linguistic analysis in fiqh commentaries.
This analysis supports the idea that times are clear indicators of Allah's grace.
4
Understand the reference to the elite
The passage ends by stating that this understanding is for the 'khawass' (elite scholars). Reflect on why the logical ordering might not be apparent to everyone.
This emphasizes the importance of fiqh methodology for deep understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الآذان لما ذكر الأوقات التي هي أسباب ظاهرة وأعلام على نعمة الله تعالى وإيجابه الغيبي ذكر الآذان الذي هو إعلام بدخولها، وقدم السبب على العلامة لقربه ولأن الأوقات أعلام قوله: (وأعلام على نعمة الله تعالى) بفتح الهمزة جمع علم بمعنى علامة أو بكسرها، أي معلمة، أو ذات أعلام والمراد المبالغة، ويؤيد الأول التعبير بعلى والمراد بنعمة الله تعالى الصلاة أو الإيجاب فالعطف للتفسير، وكل منهما نعمة لما يترتب عليه من الثواب قوله : (الذي هو إعلام) بكسر الهمزة، وقوله بدخولها أي الأوقات. قوله : (القربه) وذلك لأن العلامة مجعولة ليعلم بها السبب فهي متأخرة عنه قوله : (في حق الخواص أي العلماء فانهم يعلمون
Chapter of Adhan: Since he mentioned the times which are apparent causes and signs of the grace of Allah and His unseen obligation, he mentioned the adhan which is an announcement of their entry. And he presented the cause before the sign because of its closeness, and because the times are signs. His statement: 'And signs of the grace of Allah' - with fatha on the hamza, plural of 'alam (sign), or with kasra, meaning marker, or possessing signs, and the intended meaning is exaggeration. The first is supported by the expression 'ala. And what is meant by the grace of Allah is the prayer or the obligation, so the conjunction is explanatory. And each of them is a blessing because of the reward that follows from it. His statement: 'which is an announcement' - with kasra on the hamza. And his statement: 'of their entry' i.e., the entry of the times. His statement: 'the close' - because the sign is made to know the cause, so it is subsequent to it. His statement: 'in the right of the elite' i.e., the scholars, for they know.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on Adhan (the call to prayer). The author explains why the discussion of adhan follows the discussion of prayer times: times are the underlying cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer, while adhan is the announcement (i'lam) of those times. The cause is presented before the sign because it is more essential. The commentary then analyzes the phrase 'A'lam 'ala ni'mat Allah' — 'A'lam' (with fatha on the hamza) is plural of 'alam (sign), or with kasra means a distinguished thing. The intended meaning is that prayer times are clear indicators of Allah's grace regarding the obligation of prayer. The 'grace of Allah' here refers to the prayer itself or the divine command (ijab), both being blessings due to the reward. The adhan is defined as an 'i'lam' (announcement) of the entry of these times. The author notes that the sign (adhan) is placed after the cause (times) because the sign is created for the sake of the cause, thus it is subsequent. This logical ordering demonstrates the wisdom in the arrangement of the fiqh text. The passage concludes with a note that this understanding is particularly for the scholars (khawass) who comprehend the subtle connections.

Key Terms
الآذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer, defined as an announcement (i'lam) of the entry of prayer times.
أعلام (a'lam): Signs or markers. Here it refers to the prayer times as indicators of Allah's grace.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause or occasion. Here, prayer times are the cause (sabab) that triggers the obligation of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author place the chapter on adhan after the discussion of prayer times?
A) Because adhan is more important than times.
B) Because times are the cause and adhan is the sign; the cause is mentioned first.
C) Because adhan is a separate independent obligation.
D) Because the author forgot to mention it earlier.

Key Takeaway
Adhan is the announcement of the prayer times, and in Hanafi fiqh, the cause (time) logically precedes the sign (adhan) in textual arrangement.

Makruh Times for Nafl Prayers and Related Matters
Rulings on when nafl prayer becomes disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the situations in which performing nafl prayer becomes makruh and state the underlying reasoning.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer is disliked when it compromises the fard, disturbs khushu, or conflicts with urgent needs.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi lists several conditions that render nafl prayer disliked (makruh). While nafl is generally recommended, its performance becomes blameworthy when it risks missing the obligatory prayer, when one is repressing natural urges, when food is desired, or when the mind is distracted. The appendix extends similar rulings to speech and sleep after Fajr and Isha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
Note the initial reference to Maghrib: the author affirms that nafl between Maghrib and Isha is correct, establishing that nafl is generally permissible.
This sets the default: nafl is not inherently makruh.
2
List the four conditions of karahah
The passage explicitly states four situations where nafl becomes makruh: (1) when the fard time is narrow, (2) while repressing urine/stool (or wind), (3) when a desired meal is present, (4) when anything distracts from khushu.
Each condition has its own rationale.
3
Understand the rationale
Each condition either risks missing the fard (narrow time) or prevents full concentration (khushu) due to physical or mental preoccupation.
Khushu is essential for the perfection of prayer.
4
Analyze the appendix
The tamimah adds rulings: speaking after Fajr until praying is disliked unless for good; sleep and conversation after Isha are disliked. The key principle is that permissible speech has no good and is therefore disliked during these virtuous times.
The exception 'except for good' shows that beneficial speech is allowed.
5
Connect to the concept of makruh
The passage implies makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful). The act itself is valid but incomplete in reward due to deficiency in khushu.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between makruh tanzih and tahrimi; here it is likely tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المغرب على الصحيح لأنه لو لم يتطوع بينهما (و) يكره (عند ضيق وقت المكتوبة) لتفويته الفرض عن وقته (و) يكره التنفل كالفرض حال (مدافعة) أحد الأخبثين) البول والغائط، وكذا الريح (و) وقت (حضور طعام تتوقه نفسه و عند حضور (ما يشغل البال) عن استحضار عظمة الله تعالى والقيام بحق خدمته وبخل بالخشوع) في الصلاة بلا ضرورة لإدخال النقص في المؤدى والله الموفق بمنه. تتمة: مما يتصل بالمكروهات كراهة الكلام بعد الفجر إلى أن يصلي إلا بخير، وفي إبطال السنة إذ فصل به، كلام ولا بأس بالمشي لحاجة بعد الصلاة، وقيل يكره إلى طلوع الشمس، وقيل إلى ارتفاعها وأما بعد العشاء فأباحه قوم وحظره آخرون، وكان يكره النوم قبلها والحديث بعدها والمراد به ما ليس بخير وإنما يتحقق الخير في كلام هو عبادة إذ المباح لا خير فيه كما لا إثم فيه فيكره في هذه الأوقات نقله السيد عن النهر. قوله: (لإدخال النقص في المؤدى المراد به فعل العبادات ولو نفلاً لا مقابل القضاء والله أعلم.
Maghrib is correct because if he does not pray nafl between them. (And) it is makruh (when the time for the obligatory prayer is narrow) because it causes the fard to be missed from its time. (And) it is makruh to pray nafl like the fard while (repressing) one of the two impurities (urine and stool), and likewise wind. (And) when (food is present that he desires) and when there is (what occupies the mind) from contemplating the greatness of Allah and fulfilling the right of His service, and it is niggardly with humility in prayer without necessity because it introduces deficiency into what is performed. And Allah grants success by His grace. Appendix: Among the related makruhat is the dislike of speaking after Fajr until he prays except for good, and in nullifying the sunnah when it is separated by speech. And there is no harm in walking for a need after prayer, and it is said it is makruh until sunrise, and it is said until it is high. As for after Isha, some permitted it and others prohibited it. Sleep before it and conversation after it were disliked, meaning what is not good. Good is only realized in speech that is worship, since permissible has no good in it just as there is no sin in it, so it is disliked in these times. Al-Sayyid transmitted it from Al-Nahr. His saying: (to introduce deficiency into what is performed) means by performing acts of worship, even if nafl, not in place of qada. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the dislike (karahah) of performing nafl prayers under certain conditions. It begins by affirming the correctness of the maghrib prayer (as a baseline) and then lists several situations where nafl becomes makruh. First, when the time for the obligatory prayer is tight, because occupying oneself with nafl risks missing the fard. Second, while repressing the urge to urinate or defecate (or pass wind), as this disturbs concentration. Third, when a desired meal is present, because it preoccupies the mind. Fourth, when anything distracts the mind from contemplating Allah and maintaining humility. The author emphasizes that this deficiency is introduced without necessity. The appendix (tamimah) adds further disliked acts: speaking after Fajr until performing the sunnah prayer (unless for good), and sleeping or talking after Isha. The key point is that permissible speech has no good, so it is disliked during these times. The passage ends by clarifying that 'deficiency in what is performed' refers to acts of worship, even nafl, not to making up missed prayers.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an action that is not sinful but contrary to the preferred practice, and avoiding it is rewarded.
مدافعة الأخبثين (mudafa'at al-akhbathayn): Repressing the two impurities: urine and stool (and by extension, wind). It is a state of needing to relieve oneself.
تتمة (tamimah): A supplementary section added to complete the discussion of a topic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the time for fard is tight
B) When one is thirsty
C) When one has already prayed fard
D) When one is in a mosque

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer is disliked when it conflicts with the obligatory prayer, bodily needs, or mental focus; preserving khushu is paramount.

Definition of Adhan and Its Virtue vs. Imamah
Definition of adhan and comparison with imamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definition of adhan, and explain why the Hanafi school holds imamah to be more virtuous than adhan.

Core Idea
Adhan notifies; Imamah leads. The Hanafi school follows the Prophet's practice in preferring imamah.

This lesson unpacks the opening of the chapter on Adhan. We first clarify what adhan means both linguistically (as an announcement) and legally (as a call to prayer), then address the key comparative virtue: according to the Hanafi school, leading the prayer (imamah) is superior to calling it. The proof lies in the consistent practice of the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and the lesson explains how a statement of Umar is not a counterevidence.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the linguistic root of adhan
Identify the Arabic origin (أذن — to inform) and how the term shifted from a verbal noun to a specific ritual call.
The text notes it is مصدر (source) and then اسم للتأذين (noun for the act of calling).
2
Identify the legal definition and function
Understand adhan as an 'إعلام' (notification) of the entry of prayer time, distinct from other signs used by scholars.
The passage contrasts the elite (scholars) who use shadows/twilight with the common people who rely on adhan.
3
Extract the Hanafi ruling on adhan
From the definition and context, determine that adhan is sunnah muakkadah (highly recommended), not fard.
The hukm level is inferred from the overall discussion; text does not repeat it but it is standard Hanafi view.
4
Locate the superiority claim and its proof
Read the statement 'عندنا الإمامة أفضل منه' (imamah is better than adhan). Examine the supporting evidence: the Prophet's constant practice of leading prayer, and the Caliphs' practice.
Note that the text explicitly refutes the inference from Umar's statement, showing it does not elevate adhan.
5
Summarize the practical conclusion
The mufta bihi is that imamah is more virtuous; thus the best arrangement is for the imam to also be the mu'adhdhin.
This aligns with the principle that what the Prophet consistently did is more excellent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He was governor of Egypt during the time of Mu'awiyah. Bilal used to come at dawn to the tallest house around the mosque belonging to a woman from Bani al-Najjar and call the adhan from it. His saying: (According to us, imamah is better than it, and likewise iqamah is better than it, as in al-Tanwir. This is because of the Prophet's constancy in imamah, and likewise the Rightly Guided Caliphs after him. The saying of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Were it not for the caliphate, I would have given the adhan' does not imply its superiority over it. Rather, he meant: I would have given the adhan along with imamah, not abandoning it. So it indicates that the better thing is that the imam be the mu'adhdhin. This is our madhhab, and Abu Hanifah, may Allah be pleased with him, was upon it. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, end of the commentary.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on Adhan (the call to prayer). It is a commentary that defines adhan linguistically and legally, and discusses its superiority relative to imamah. The author first explains the text of the matn: 'And signs of Allah's grace' are interpreted as the prayer times, which are signs for the elite (scholars), while adhan is a sign for the common people. The linguistic analysis shows that 'adhan' is derived from 'adhina' meaning to inform, and it is a noun for the act of calling to prayer. The passage then addresses the question of superiority: according to the Hanafi school, imamah (leading prayer) is better than giving the adhan, and likewise iqamah (the second call) is better. The proof is the Prophet's constant practice of leading prayer, as well as the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The statement of Umar that he would have given adhan were it not for the caliphate does not suggest adhan is better; rather, he meant he would combine both roles. Hence, the best is for the imam to also be the mu'adhdhin. This is the established Hanafi position, following Abu Hanifah. The passage also includes historical notes: Salamah ibn Khalaf was the first to introduce minarets in mosques, and Bilal used to give adhan from a tall house.

Key Terms
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, informing the entry of prayer time.
إمامة (imamah): Leading the congregational prayer.
مئذنة (mi'dhana): Minaret, the place from which adhan is given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Adhan is more virtuous
B) Leading prayer (imamah) is more virtuous
C) Both are equal
D) It depends on the person

Key Takeaway
Adhan is a highly recommended sunnah, but leading prayer (imamah) holds greater virtue in the Hanafi school.

Adhaan is Sunnah Mu'akkadah, Not Wajib
Establishes adhaan as sunnah mu'akkadah with proof and resolves intra-madhhab conflict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhaan and explain why it is sunnah mu'akkadah rather than wajib, using evidence from the Bedouin hadith and responding to the intra-madhhab objection.

Core Idea
Adhaan is a strongly emphasized sunnah, not an obligation, as the Prophet taught prayer without it.

This lesson clarifies the legal status of adhaan in the Hanafi school. While many assume adhaan is compulsory due to its regular practice, the school's most correct position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah—emphasized but not legally obligatory. We will examine the textual evidence and address an apparent contradiction from Imam Muhammad's statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its evidence
The base ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah. The primary proof is that when the Prophet taught a Bedouin how to pray, he did not mention adhaan, showing it is not essential.
This is the most correct view according to the text.
2
Examine the dalil in detail
The hadith of the Bedouin omits adhaan entirely, implying it is not a mandatory component of prayer. The later hadith from Salman encourages adhaan for a lone traveler, confirming its virtue but not obligation.
Both hadith are ahad, so they are zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Consider the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad's statement that he would fight a town and beat an individual who abandons adhaan appears to indicate obligation. However, the commentary reconciles this by noting that sunnah mu'akkadah incurs sin when abandoned, similar to wajib, but the legal classification remains sunnah.
The text says the two views are 'close' (متقاربان) because of the sin incurred.
4
Understand the category of sunnah mu'akkadah
Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) is a distinct category: it carries a strong recommendation, and its abandonment is blameworthy, but it does not have the legal force of wajib. The text distinguishes between sunnah hadi (guidance) and sunnah za'idah (additional).
Leaving sunnah hadi is considered 'isa'ah' (evil).
5
Apply to practical cases
Adhaan is prescribed for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah, not for Eid, istisqa, janazah, or witr. For a lone person in an empty land, giving both adhaan and iqaamah is mustahabb, but leaving both together is makruh tanzihi.
The hadith of Salman promises immense reward for the lone person who gives both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سن الأذان فليس بواجب على الأصح لعدم تعليمه الأعرابي وكذا الإقامة سنة مؤكدة في قوة الواجب لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا حضر الصلاة فليؤذن لكم أحدكم وليؤمكم أكبركم وللمداومة عليها للفرائض ومنها الجمعة فلا يؤذن لعيد واستسقاء وجنازة ووتر فلا يقع أذان العشاء للوتر على الصحيح ولو صلى الفرائض منفرداً بفلاة فإنه يصلي خلفه جند من جنود الله أداء كان أو قضاء سفراً أو حضراً كما فعله النبي صلى الله واحد ضربته وحسبته قال في المعراج وغيره والقولان متقاربان لأن السنة المؤكدة لها حكم الواجب في لحوق الإثم بالترك وإن كان الإثم مقولاً بالتشكيك ثم إن محمداً لا يخص الحكم المذكور بالواجب بل هو في سائر السنن فلا دليل فيه على الوجوب والسنة نوعان سنة هدى كالأذان والإقامة وتركها يوجب الإساءة وسنة زائدة وتركها لا يوجبها كسنة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في قعوده وقيامه ولبسه وأكله وشربه ونحو ذلك كما في السراج ولكن الأولى فعلها لقوله تعالى ولقد كان لكم في رسول الله أسوة حسنة قوله لعدم تعليمه الأعرابي الضمير للأذان من إضافة المصدر إلى مفعوله الأول والفاعل هو يعني أنه لما علم الأعرابي كيف يصلي لم يذكر له الأذان قوله سنة مؤكدة بالنصب مفعول لسن مبين للنوع وقوله وكذا الإقامة مبتدأ أو خبر بالنظر للشرح ومعطوف على الأذان من عطف المفردات بالنظر إلى المتن قوله لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الحديث قاصر على الأذان قوله على الصحيح وقيل هو لهما لأن الوقت لهما قوله ولو صلى الفرائض منفرداً إتيان المنفرد به على سبيل الأفضلية فلا يسن في حقه مؤكداً والمكروه له ترك الأذان والإقامة معاً حتى لو ترك الأذان وأتى بالإقامة لا يكره كما في البحر قوله فانه يصلي خلفه الخ أخرج عبد الرزاق عن سلمان رضي الله عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا كان الرجل بأرض فحانت الصلاة فليتوضأ فإن لم يجد ماء فليتيمم فإن أقام صلى معه ملكان وإن أذن وأقام صلى معه من جنود الله ما لا يرى طرفاه
Adhaan is sunnah, not wajib according to the most correct view, because the Prophet did not teach it to the Bedouin. Similarly, iqaamah is sunnah mu'akkadah, in the strength of wajib, due to the Prophet's statement: 'When the prayer is established, let one of you give the adhaan and let your eldest lead you.' And due to continuous practice. [Adhaan is sunnah] for obligatory prayers, including Jumu'ah; adhaan is not given for Eid, istisqa, janazah, or witr. The adhaan for Isha does not count for witr according to the correct view. If one prays the obligatory prayers alone in an empty land, an army from the armies of Allah prays behind him, whether it is ada or qada, travel or residence, as the Prophet did for men. Its conditions: the conditions of its validity: 'with a good voice' meaning beautiful and loud voice. It is narrated that Umar ibn Abdul Aziz said to a mu'adhdhin: 'Give a good adhaan, otherwise leave us.' 'The obligation of responding to it' meaning its obligation; it is said it is sunnah, and 'by action' is weak and contains hardship; the relied-upon view is that responding by speech alone is recommended. 'And speech' – the waw is in the sense of 'or', indicating a difference of opinion. 'Times of prayer' meaning originally and desirably. 'Even if qada' – here qada has no time, unless by 'time' is meant the time of the action. 'And it is required from the listener' – this is dispensed with by his statement 'its ruling' etc., and he only mentioned it to explain his previous statement. 'Like action' – you already know what is in it. 'Not wajib according to the most correct view' – and it is said it is wajib because of Muhammad's statement: 'If the people of a town agree to abandon it, I would fight them; and if one person abandons it, I would beat him and imprison him.' He said in al-Mi'raj and others: the two views are close because the sunnah mu'akkadah has the ruling of wajib in incurring sin by leaving it, although sin is said by tashkik (gradation). Then Muhammad did not specify the ruling mentioned to wajib, but it applies to all sunan, so there is no evidence in it for obligation. Sunnah is of two types: sunnah hadi (guidance) like adhaan and iqaamah, and leaving it necessitates evil (isa'ah); and sunnah za'idah (additional) and leaving it does not necessitate evil, like the Prophet's sunnah in his sitting, standing, dress, eating, drinking, etc., as in al-Siraj. However, it is better to do it due to the verse: 'Indeed in the Messenger of Allah you have a good example.' His statement: 'because the Prophet did not teach it to the Bedouin' – the pronoun is for adhaan, from the addition of the masdar to its first maf'ul, and the fa'il is implied – meaning that when he taught the Bedouin how to pray, he did not mention adhaan. His statement: 'sunnah mu'akkadah' – it is in the accusative as maf'ul of 'sanna' explaining the type. And his statement: 'and similarly iqaamah' is mubtada or khabar according to the sharh, and it is conjoined to adhaan as a conjunction of individual words according to the matn. His statement: 'due to the Prophet's statement' – the hadith is specific to adhaan. His statement: 'according to the correct view, and it is said it is for both because the time is for both.' His statement: 'even if he prays the obligatory prayers alone' – the lone person does it on the basis of preference, so it is not sunnah mu'akkadah for him, and it is makruh for him to leave both adhaan and iqaamah together, to the extent that if he leaves adhaan and offers iqaamah, it is not makruh, as in al-Bahr. His statement: 'for an army from the armies of Allah prays behind him' – Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Salman that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If a man is in a land and prayer time comes, let him perform wudu, and if he does not find water, let him perform tayammum. Then if he gives iqaamah, two angels pray with him; and if he gives adhaan and iqaamah, an army from the armies of Allah prays with him whose ends cannot be seen.'
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah addresses the legal status of adhaan and iqaamah. The author states that adhaan is a sunnah (recommended) and not wajib (obligatory) according to the most correct view. The proof is that when the Prophet taught a Bedouin how to pray in the famous hadith, he did not include adhaan, indicating it is not an obligatory element. The text then clarifies that iqaamah is also sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), which carries the strength of wajib in terms of reward and sin but not legal obligation. The commentary mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad said that if a whole town abandons adhaan, the ruler should fight them, and if an individual abandons it, he should be beaten and imprisoned. This suggests obligation, but the commentators reconcile by noting that sunnah mu'akkadah is so emphatic that its abandonment incurs sin, but this does not make it wajib. The passage also discusses the conditions for adhaan, including that the mu'adhdhin should have a good voice, and that responding to the adhaan is recommended (andab) by speech only, not by action. Finally, it presents a hadith that for a person alone in a desert, giving both adhaan and iqaamah results in a multitude of angels praying behind him, underscoring the virtue.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized recommended act; its omission is blameworthy but does not entail sin like leaving a wajib.
صيتاً (sayyitan): Having a good and loud voice; a condition for the mu'adhdhin to effectively convey the call.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of adhaan for the five daily prayers?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds adhaan as an emphatic sunnah, not an obligation, based on prophetic practice and reconciled with the strong statements of Imam Muhammad.

Ruling on Adhaan for Women: Makruh in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on adhaan for women and its rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhaan for women, explain the reasoning based on concealment and prohibition of raising voice, and distinguish it from other schools.

Core Idea
Women's adhaan is makruh because concealment and voice prohibition override the recommendation of adhaan.

The source text begins by stating that adhaan and iqaamah are disliked for women. This ruling is not arbitrary; it is based on the principle that women are required to conceal themselves and raising their voice is haram. The commentary expands on why their congregation is not legislated. Let's unpack the reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text clearly states that adhaan and iqaamah are makruh for women. Determine the exact hukm level (makruh tahrimi or tanzihi).
The commentary implies it is close to haram due to the prohibition of raising voice, so it is likely makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a narration from Ibn Umar expressing dislike. Identify the type of evidence (hadith) and its strength.
Though not quoted verbatim, the narration supports the ruling.
3
Understand the rationale
The commentary provides the rationale: women must conceal themselves, and raising voice is haram. Adhaan involves loud voice, so it conflicts with these requirements.
Even iqaamah, though less loud, is still discouraged.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies to women's congregations and also to other groups whose congregation is not legislated (slaves, naked persons, those with excuses).
Referenced from al-Bahr and al-Halabi.
5
State the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is that adhaan for women is makruh tahrimi, and they should not perform it.
This is the position of the Hanafi school.

Source Text

وكرها أي الأذان والإقامة للنساء لما روي عن ابن عمر من كراهتهما لهن قوله وكرهما للنساء اعلم أن الأذان والإقامة من سنن الجماعة المستحبة فلا يندبان لجماعة النساء والعبيد والعراة لأن جماعتهم غير مشروعة كما في البحر وكذا جماعة المعذورين يوم الجمعة للظهر في المصر فإن أداءه بهما مكروه كما في الحلبي قوله من كرهتهما لهن لأن مبنى حالهن على الستر ورفع صوتهن حرام والغالب أن الإقامة تكون برفع صوت إلا أنه أقل من صوت الأذان قوله يكبر في أوله أربعا بصوتين وأكبر أما بمعنى أعظم أو أقدم وقيل بمعنى عظيم فأفعل التفضيل ليس على بابه كقوله تعالى وهو أهون عليه أي هين بأهون تقريبا لعقول المخاطبين إذ الإعادة عندهم أسهل من الابتداء قوله وروى الحسن مرتين وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف وبه قال مالك قوله ويجزم الراء في التكبير كان أبو العباس المبرد يقول سمع الأذان موقوفا في مقاطعه كقولهم حي على الصلاة على الفلاح والأصل فيه الله أكبر الله أكبر بتسكين الراء فحولت فتحة الألف من اسم الله إلى الراء وهذا يقتضي تعيين التسكين في الراء الثانية وكذا الأولى غير أنه تنفل فتحة الألف إليها والتحقيق أن الراء الأخيرة ساكنة لا محالة وهو مخير فيما قبلها بين الضم والفتح من الساكنين إذ لا يتعين الفتح في ذلك كما لا يخفى ولفظ الجلالة مرفوع في جميع الحالات أفاده بعض الأفاضل قوله ويسكن كلمات الأذان يعني للوقف والأولى ذكره قوله في الأذان حقيقة أي الوقف الذي لأجله السكون حقيقة في الأذان لأجل الترسل فيه قوله وينوي الوقف في الإقامة لأنه لم يقف حقيقة لأن المطلوب فيها الحدر أفاده في الشرح قوله القوله علة لقوله ويسكن الخ ويأتي بالشهادتين كل واحدة مرتين يفصل بينهما بسكتة وهكذا الخ ويأتي بحي على الصلاة وهو المقصود من الأذان لأن المراد نداؤهم إلى الصلاة بل هو الأذان في الحقيقة إلا أنه سمي المجموع أذانا مجازا تسمية للكل باسم الجزء الحصول المقصود بذلك وهو الإعلام بدخول الوقت وسميت الإقامة بها لأجل قد قامت كما في التبيين وهي هنا بمعنى أقبلوا لأنه هو الذي يتعدى بعلي ومعنى حي على الفلاح أقبلوا على ما فيه فلا حكم ونجاتكم وهي الصلاة أو أقبلوا على الصلاة عاجلا وعلى الفلاح أجلا قالوا وليس في كلام العرب كلمة أجمع للخير من لفظ الفلاح ويقرب منه النصيحة ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم تخلصا
And [adhaan and iqaamah] are disliked for women, because of what is narrated from Ibn Umar regarding their dislike. His statement: 'And they are disliked for women' – know that adhaan and iqaamah are from the desirable sunan of the congregation, so they are not recommended for the congregation of women, slaves, and naked persons, because their congregation is not legislated, as in al-Bahr. Similarly, the congregation of those with excuses on Friday for Zuhr in the city, then performing it with [adhaan] is makruh, as in al-Halabi. His statement: 'their dislike for them' – because their condition is based on concealment, and raising their voice is haram, and usually iqaamah is with raising the voice, though less than adhaan. His statement: 'He says takbeer at its beginning four times' with two voices. 'Akbar' means 'greater' or 'older', or it is said 'great'. The superlative is not used in its literal sense, like His statement: 'and He is easier for Him' [30:27], meaning 'easy' by 'easier' as an approximation for the minds of the addressees, because repetition is easier for them than initiation. His statement: 'And Hasan narrated it twice' – this is a narration from Abu Yusuf, and Malik held it. His statement: 'And he pronounces the ra with sukun in the takbeer' – Abu al-Abbas al-Mubarrad used to say: 'I heard the adhaan paused at its stopping points, like their saying: 'Haya 'ala al-salah, haya 'ala al-falah.' The original is 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar' with sukun on the ra, then the fatha of the alif from the name of Allah was transferred to the ra. This necessitates the sukun on the second ra, and similarly the first, except that the fatha of the alif is moved to it. The investigation is that the last ra is necessarily sukun, and the one before it is given a choice between damm and fatha among the two sukun letters, since fatha is not determined there, as is not hidden. And the word of majesty is marfu' in all cases, as some virtuous ones have mentioned. His statement: 'And he makes sukun on the words of adhaan' meaning for stopping, and it is better to mention it. His statement: 'in adhaan in reality' – the stopping for which the sukun is real in adhaan because of the slow recitation. His statement: 'And he intends stopping in the iqaamah' because he does not actually stop, since the required in iqaamah is speed, as mentioned in the sharh. His statement: 'the statement' is the cause for his statement 'and he makes sukun' etc. And he comes with the two shahadahs, each one twice, separating between them with a pause, and so on. And he comes with 'Haya 'ala al-salah', which is the intended purpose of adhaan, because the aim is to call them to prayer; indeed it is the adhaan in reality, but the entire set is called adhaan metaphorically, naming the whole by the part to achieve the intended purpose, which is the announcement of the entry of time. And iqaamah is named for 'qad qamat' as in al-Tabyin, and here it means 'come forward' because it is the word that is transposed with 'ala. The meaning of 'haya 'ala al-falah' is 'come toward what has success and salvation for you', i.e., prayer, or 'come toward prayer immediately and toward success later'. They said: there is no word in the speech of the Arabs that gathers more goodness than the word 'falah', and close to it is 'nasihah', as mentioned by al-Nawawi in his commentary on Muslim. End.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on adhaan, addressing two topics: the ruling for women and the correct wording. First, the text states that adhaan and iqaamah are makruh (disliked) for women, citing a narration from Ibn Umar. The commentary explains that women's congregation is not legislated due to the requirement of concealment and the prohibition of raising voices. Even though iqaamah involves less volume, it is still discouraged. Second, the passage details the pronunciation of the takbeer: 'Allahu Akbar' is said four times at the beginning of adhaan according to the zahir al-riwayah, though there is a narration from Hasan (al-Basri) and Abu Yusuf for twice. The takbeer's ra should be pronounced with sukun (no vowel) when pausing, but during continuous recitation, it may have a vowel. The commentary also discusses the meaning of 'Akbar' and the transfer of the fatha from the alif to the ra. Finally, it explains the phrases 'haya 'ala al-salah' and 'haya 'ala al-falah', noting that the adhaan's essential purpose is calling to prayer, and 'falah' encompasses success and salvation. The iqaamah is named for the phrase 'qad qamat' and its wording is similar but more rapid.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): A disliked action; in this context, adhaan for women is makruh due to the requirement of concealment and prohibition of raising voice.
رفع صوت (raf' sawt): Raising the voice; considered haram (for women) and thus the basis for the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because women are not obligated to pray in congregation.
B) Because women's congregation is not legislated and raising voice is haram.
C) Because adhaan is only for men.
D) Because women may not enter the mosque.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, women giving adhaan is makruh tahrimi due to the prohibition of raising voice and the requirement of concealment.

Pronunciation of the Takbeer in Adhaan: Sukun on the Ra and Related Rules
Details of pronunciation of takbeer and other phrases in adhaan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the correct pronunciation of 'Allahu Akbar' in adhaan, including the sukun on the ra at the end of phrases and the transfer of the fatha.

Core Idea
The ra in 'Allahu Akbar' is pronounced with sukun at the end of adhaan phrases, reflecting its original form and the transfer of the fatha.

This part of the passage delves into the precise wording of the takbeer in adhaan. The commentator, expanding on the base text, explains the rules concerning the pronunciation of the ra in 'Allahu Akbar', the meaning of 'Akbar', and the handling of pauses. Understanding these details ensures that the adhaan is recited correctly according to Hanafi guidelines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase under discussion
The text focuses on 'Allahu Akbar' and how the ra should be pronounced.
The phrase is the first part of the adhaan.
2
Understand the base pronunciation at stopping
When pausing (waqf) after 'Allahu Akbar', the ra is sakinah (without vowel). The original pronunciation had sukun on the ra, and the fatha of the alif was transferred to the ra.
The commentator quotes al-Mubarrad about the pause.
3
Learn the rule for continuous recitation
In continuous recitation (wasl), the ra may have a fatha or dammah. The last ra is always sakinah at the end of a stopping point.
The text says the last ra is necessarily sakinah.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Hasan al-Basri and Abu Yusuf that the takbeer is said twice, but the relied upon view is four times.
The text mentions this as a variant.
5
Apply the rule to practice
The mu'adhdhin should recite the takbeer with sukun on the ra at the end of each phrase, and be aware of the flexibility of the vowel on the ra when continuing.
This ensures correct pronunciation.

Source Text

The Hanafi Ruling on Tarji' in Adhan
Explains Hanafi ruling against tarji' in adhan and refutes Shafi'i proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tarji' in adhan, identify the Shafi'i proof, and explain the Hanafi reinterpretation of that proof.

Core Idea
Tarji' in adhan is not part of the sunnah; the Shafi'i evidence from Abu Mahdhurah is a teaching method, not a permanent practice.

Adhan has specific forms in each madhhab. One point of difference is whether the mu'adhdhin should softly say the shahadah then repeat it loudly (tarji'). This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that tarji' is not part of adhan and the refutation of the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
Identify the ruling: tarji' is not part of adhan. The proof is the practice of Bilal (ra) and the action of the descending angel.
Bilal was the Prophet's mu'adhdhin; his action is the primary precedent.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i considers tarji' a sunnah based on the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah, who was ordered by the Prophet to repeat the adhan loudly.
Abu Mahdhurah was a mu'adhdhin in Makkah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The Hanafi response reinterpretes Abu Mahdhurah's action: the Prophet taught him to be loud because he was new to Islam and shy; it was not a general instruction for tarji'.
The Prophet twisting his ear was a teaching gesture, not a command for a new sunnah.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis do not perform tarji' in adhan; Shafi'is consider it sunnah and practice it.
In mixed communities, mu'adhdhins may follow their school's practice.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that tarji' is not part of adhan, and doing it is makruh tahrimi.
This is the position of the matn and its commentators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا) ترجيع في كلمتي (الشهادتين) لأن بلالاً رضي الله عنه لم يرجع، أن يخفض صوته بالشهادتين ثم يرجع فيرفعه بهما والإقامة مثله لفعل الملك النازل. وقال الشافعي: إنه سنة لترجيع أبي محذورة بأمره، وأجيب بأنه كان تعليماً فظنه ترجيعاً، وبأن أبا محذورة كان مؤذناً بمكة وكان حديث عهد بالإسلام فأخفى كلمتي الشهادة حياء من قومه، ففرك النبي أذنه وأمره أن يعود فيرفع صوته ليعلمه أنه لا حياء من الحق. والإقامة مثله حساً، ومعنى، وصفة إلا ما استثنى واختصاصاً وسبباً ولا لحن ولا ترجيع فيها.
And there is no tarji' in the two phrases of the two shahadahs, because Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) did not do tarji' — that he lowers his voice with the two shahadahs then repeats raising them. And the iqamah is like that due to the action of the descending angel. And al-Shafi'i said: It is a sunnah due to the tarji' of Abu Mahdhurah upon his order. And it was answered that it was teaching, so he thought it was tarji'. And because Abu Mahdhurah was a mu'adhdhin in Makkah and was new to Islam, so he hid the two shahadah out of shyness from his people, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) twisted his ear and ordered him to repeat raising his voice to teach him that there is no shyness from the truth. And the iqamah is like it in sense, meaning, and description except what is excluded, and in specialization and cause, and there is no melody nor tarji' in it.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the practice of tarji' in the adhan. The Hanafi position is that there is no tarji' in the two shahadahs (the two lines of the testimony of faith) in the adhan. The proof is the practice of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him), who did not perform tarji'. Tarji' means to say the shahadah softly and then repeat it loudly. The iqamah follows the same ruling. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that tarji' is a sunnah based on the practice of Abu Mahdhurah, who was ordered by the Prophet to do tarji'. The Hanafi response clarifies that what Abu Mahdhurah did was actually a teaching method, not tarji'; because he was new to Islam and shy, the Prophet taught him to be loud. Thus, it is not a precedent for tarji' in adhan. The iqamah is identical in ruling, having no tarji' or melodious tone.

Key Terms
ترجيع (tarji'): The act of repeating the two shahadahs in adhan by saying them softly first then loudly.
الشهادتين (ash-shahadatayn): The two testimonies of faith: 'Ashhadu alla ilaha illallah' and 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadar Rasulullah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on tarji' in the adhan?
A) It is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is permissible but not recommended.
C) It is not part of the adhan and is considered a disliked innovation.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Tarji' in the two shahadahs of adhan is not part of the Hanafi practice; the school relies on the action of Bilal and rejects the Shafi'i proof from Abu Mahdhurah as a teaching method.
